Introduction to Javascript

It is programming language use to create functionality in web page. functionality :- reading input, performing process and providing output. Ex:- displaying menu when the user click on menu.
  • As it is programming language, it provides all concepts like datatype, functions, objects, variables and more
  • It is a case sensitive language. upper case and lower case are different here
  • It is object oriented programming language
  • It is developed by netscape corporation
    • syntax of javascript
  • Internal javascript :- will be written in same html file.
    • placing script in head tag
    • placing script in body tag
  • External javascript :- will be written in seperate javascript file with extention .js

Output statment in javascript

  • output statment is use to use show some output to user
  • console.log is output statement in js
  • we have to open browser console to see output. to open browser console press F12

variables

variable is named memory location in RAM to store particular value.
  • var is a keyword use to declare variable.
  • In javascript variable's datatype can be changed that means we can assign any type of value

Operators in javascript

  • to perform some operation like ... 10 + 2
      • Type of operator
    • Arithmetic operator.... +, *, -, %, /
    • Increment and decrement operators .... ++, --
    • Assignment operator.... used to assign value to var... =, *=, +=, -=, %=
    • Relational operator... ==, !=, <, >, <=, >=
    • Logical operator...
      • && -- and (both condition must be true)
      • || -- or (at least one condition must be true)
      • ! -- not (given condition will be reversed)
    • concatination operator...use to add two string

Control statement

  • by default, statements executes in sequencial order(top-bottom)
  • Types of control statement
  • conditional control statement
    • if
      • if
      • if-else
      • else-if
      • nested if
    • switch - case
    • when we have one variable with many possibility
  • Looping control statement
    • while
    • do - while
    • for

Function

function is a collection of statements, to perform some specific operation.

Arguments - predefined variable

it is used to represent all the argument value that are received by the current function. it is a pre-defined variable that can be used only in the function.
  • arguments : returns collection of all argument value
  • arguments[index]: returns the single arguments based on given index.
  • arguments.length : count of argument volue received
Recursion :- the function calls itself

syntax :-
function functionName(){
    if (condition)
    {
        functionName();
    }
}

EXAMPLE :- factorial of n numbers
function factorial(n){
    if (n==1){
        return 1;
    }
    else 
        return n * factorial(n - 1);
        }

factorial(5)

let above15 = age1 > 15 ? "yes" : "no";
console.log(above15);

switch case statment

let weekday = 2;
switch(weekday){
    case 1:
        document.write("monday");
        break;
    case 2:
        document.write("tuesday");
        break;
    case 3:
        document.write("wednesday");
        break;
    case 4:
        document.write("thursday");
        break;
    case 5:
        document.write("friday");
        break;
    case 6:
        document.write("saturday");
        break;
    case 7:
        document.write("sunday");
        break;
    default:
        document.write(` Invalid day `);
}


nullish coalescing operator -- ?? 

- it checks whether the expression is null or undefined 
- if it null or undefined  it will return default value -- here unknown
- if not null or undefined - it return value of variable 
let myName = "sarita";

document.write(myName ?? "unknown");


function to print in reverse order

function reverse(array){
    document.write("function to print in reverse order");
    for(var i=array.length-1;i>=0; i--){
        document.write(array[i]);
    }
}
reverse([10,20,30,40,50]);


function to check identical element

function identical(array){
    document.write("function to check identical element");
    let first = array[0];
    for(var i=1; i< array.length; i++){
        if (array[i] != first)
        {
            return false;
        }
         }
            return true;
        }

iden = identical([10,10,10,10,10]);
console.log(iden);


function to check max number

function maximum(array){
    document.write("function to check max number");
    let max = array[0];
    for (i=1;i< array.length;i++){
        if (array[i]>max){
            max = array[i];
        };
       
    };
    return max;
};

maxi = maximum([10,40,50,80,90]);
document.write(maxi);


function to sum all number

function sum(array){
    document.write("function to sum all number");
    let sum = 0;
    for (num of array){
        sum = sum + num;
    }
    return sum;
}

sum1 = sum([10,20,30,40]);
document.write(sum1);


book management system using javascript

var books = [];
var input = prompt('which operation you want to perform ? [add | list | delete | exit');
while (input != 'exit'){
    if (input == 'add')
    {
        addbook();
    }
    else if(input == 'list')
    {
        listbook();
    }
    else if(input == 'delete')
    {
        deletebook();
    }
    else{
        console.log('please choose valid option');
    }
    input = prompt('which operation you want to perform ? [add | list | delete | exit');
}
console.log('thanks for using our application');

function addbook()
{
var newbook = prompt('enter book name to add');
books.push(newbook);
}

function listbook(){
    console.log('list of available book:-');
    for (book of books){
        console.log(book);
    }
}

function deletebook(){
    var name = prompt('enter name of book to delete');
    index = books.indexOf(name);
    if(index == -1){
        console.log('specified book not avasilable');
    }
    else{
        books.splice(index, 1);
        console.log('specified book deleted');
    }
    
}


Array in Javascript

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango'];
console.log(fruits);
console.log(fruits.length);


Access Array Element

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango'];
let x = fruits[0];
console.log(x);


Update Array Element

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango'];
fruits[1] = "blue berry";


Push :- to add element at the end of array

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango'];
fruits.push('chickoo');


unshift :- to add element at the beginning of array

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango'];
fruits.unshift('black berry');


Pop :- to remove element from end of array

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango'];
let popped_item = fruits.pop();
console.log(popped_item);
console.log(fruits);


shift :- to remove element from beginning of array

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango'];
let removed_item = fruits.shift();
console.log(removed_item);
console.log(fruits);


splice :- 

let vegetable = ['lady finger','cucumber','carrot','tomato'];

splice to remove element from array

let vegetable = ['lady finger','cucumber','carrot','tomato'];
removed_item = console.log(vegetable.splice(1,1));  // splice(start index, no of element to delete)
console.log(removed_item);
console.log(vegetable);

splice to add element in array

let vegetable = ['lady finger','cucumber','carrot','tomato'];
vegetable.splice(1,0,'potato','guard'); //1 is start, 0 element to delete, 'potato and guard to add'
console.log(vegetable);


concat :- to join different arrays

let vegetable = ['lady finger','cucumber','carrot','tomato'];
let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango'];
let fru_veg = fruits.concat(vegetable);
console.log(fru_veg);


slice :- to access array elements

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango','water melon']; 
let sliced_array = fruits.slice(1); // it will start from index 1 and go upto last
let sliced_array = fruits.slice(-3); // it will start from index -3 and go upto last
console.log(sliced_array);


includes :- check whether element is present or not in array

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango','water melon'];
console.log(fruits.includes('mango')); // by default starts from 0 index - true or false
console.log(fruits.includes('mango', 2)); //checks for mango after 2nd index


index of :- to find index of element

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango','water melon'];
console.log(indexOf('mango')); //it returns 2
console.log(indexOf('grape')); //it returns -1 for not available element


reverse :- to reverse elements of array

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango','water melon'];
fruits.reverse();
console.log(fruits);


Nested array

let matrix = [[1,2,3],[4,5,6],[7,8,9]];
console.log(matrix.length);
console.log(matrix[1][1]); // access elements from nested array
console.log(matrix[2][1]);


for of loop :- loops through elements of array

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango','water melon'];
for(let fruit of fruits){
    console.log(`fruit name is ${fruit}`); 
}


for in loop :- loops through index of elements of array

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango','water melon'];
for(let i in fruits){
    console.log(i);
    console.log(fruits[i]);
}


for loop and for each loop

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango','water melon'];
for(let i = 0; i< fruits.length; i++){
    console.log(fruits[i]);
}

fruits.forEach(function(element){
    console.log(element);
});


while loop

let fruits = ['apple','banana','mango','water melon'];
i = 0;
while(i< fruits.length){
    console.log(fruits[i]);
    i++;
}



Object Oriented Programming In Javascript


object in javascript

- an object is collection of properties.
- It has key and value.
- value can be a function (it is called method)

Example of object:-
let fees = {
    sarita : 100, // property 
    smruti : 200, // property
    total : function (){return (100 + 200);} //method
}

User-defined Objects :- this are custom objects made by user.

Native Objects :- Provided by javascript like string, boolen, function, date etc..

Host Objects :- supported by most host environments like window, navigator..

Document Objects :- this are part of documentobject model (DOM). access to document object is provided 
by browser via document property of the window(window.document)


Declaration and initialization of object

Using Object Literal

var fees = {};
fees['sarita'] = 100;
fees.smruti = 200;
fees["super man"] = 300; // multiword requires quotation
fees['total'] = function (){return (100 + 200 + 300);};

document.write(fees.total()); // to access total method of object
document.write(fees['total']()); // to access total method of object

Using Object Literal

var object_name = new Object();
var fees = new Object(); // var fees = {}
fees['sarita'] = 100;
fees.smruti = 200;
fees['total'] = function (){return (100 + 200 + 300);};

fees.total = sum; // second way to assign function

function sum(){
    return (100 + 200);
}


Accessing Properties of Object

- A property of an object contains named data.
- this can be accessed with dot operator or array [] operator.
- objects functions are called methods.
- this can be accessed with dot operator or array [] operator.

syntax:-object_name.property_name 

Ex:- 
var fees = {Rahul:100, sarita:200};
document.write(fees.Rahul + " " + fees.sarita);

Adding property in Javascript object

fees.sonam = 500;
fees.show = function(){};

document.write(fees.Rahul + " " + fees.sarita + " " + fees.sonam);

Deleting property from javascript objects

Delete operator is used to delete instance property
syntax :- delete object_name.property_name

Ex :- delete fees.Rahul;

after removal with delete property has undefined value.note

Factory Function

when a function returns an object, we call it factory function.
it can produce object without new keyword or classes.

Ex :- 
function mobile(){
    return {
        model : Galaxy,
        price : function(){return ("price: Rs. 3000");}
    }
}

var samsang = mobile();
document.write(samsang.model + " " + samsang.price());

function mobile(model_no){
    return {
        model : model_no,
        price : function(){
            return "Price is Rs. 3000";
        }
    };
}

var samsang = mobile("Galaxy");
var nokia = mobile('3310');
document.write(samsang.model + " " + samsang.price() + "
");
document.write(nokia.model + " " + nokia.price() + "
");

Constructor in javascript

- object instance are created  with constructor.
- constructor are basically special function that prepare new instance of an object for use. 

// Defining constructor is like class in python 
    --here self is replaced with this
    -- first letter of constructor name should be capital 

Ex :- constructor without parameter 

function Mobile(){
    this.model = '3310';
    this.price = function(){document.write(this.model + " Price Rs. 3000")
    }
};

var samsang = new Mobile(); //creating object using constructor
samsang.price(); // accessing method of object 


 Ex :- constructor with parameter 

function Mobile(model_no){
    this.model = model_no;
    this.price = function(){
        document.write(this.model + " Price Rs. 3000 ");
    };
}

var samsang = new Mobile("samsang");
var nokia = new Mobile("nokia");
samsang.price();
nokia.price();


Check properties exists in Javascript


Using typeof operator :-
syntax:- if(typeof object_name.key !== 'undefined')

Ex :-

function Mobie(){
    this.model = '3310';
    this.price = function(){document.write(this.model + " Price Rs. 3000");
    };
};

var nokia = new Mobile();

// check for memory property exists in nokia object or not
if(typeof nokia.memory !== "undefined"){
    document.write("available");
}else{
    document.write("Not available");
}

Using in operator :-

syntax :- if('key' in object_name)

Ex :- 

if('memory' in nokia){
    document.write("available");
}else{
    document.write("not available");
}

Using hasOwnProperty() :-

syntax :- if(object_name.hasOwnProperty("key"))

Ex:- 

if(nokia.hasOwnProperty("memory")){
    document.write("available");
}else{
    document.write("doesn't exit");
}


For in Loop

the for in loop is used to loop through an object's properties.

syntax :--

for (var variable_name in object_name){
block of statment
}

Ex :--

for (var x in samsang){
    document.write(x);
}

function Mobie(){
    this.model = '3310';
    this.price = function(){document.write(this.model + " Price Rs. 3000");
    };
};

var samsang = new Mobile('Galaxy');
var nokia = new Mobile('nokia');

for (var key in nokia){
    if (typeof nokia[key] !== 'function'){
        document.write(key + " " + nokia[key]);
    }
    
}

document.write(Object.keys(nokia));

var fees = new Object();

    return {
        model : 'Galaxy';
    };
}

var samsang = mobile();
var nokia = monile();

Constructor Function

    this.model = 'Galaxy';
    this.price = 3000;
    this.total = function (){
        document.write("Price of " + this.model+ " is " + this.price);
    }
}

nokia.total()


Class in Javascript

A specific category can be defined as class.

Defining a Class in Javascript

we define class in javascript using custom constructor.

Ex :- 

var Mobile = function(model_no, sprice){
    this.model = model_no;
    this.color = 'white';
    this.price = 3000;
    this.sp = sprice;
    this.sellingprice = function(){
        return (this.price + this.sp);
    };
};

var samsang = new Mobile('Galaxy',2000);
var nokia = new Mobile('3310',1000);
samsang.sellingprice();

Private Properties And Methods

Using var or let or const you can create private properties and methods.

Ex :- 

var Mobile = function(model_no, sprice){
    var model = model_no;
    var color = 'white';
    var price = 3000;
    var sp = sprice;
    var sellingprice = function(){
        return (price + sp);
    };
};

var samsang = new Mobile('Galaxy',2000);
var nokia = new Mobile('3310',1000);
samsang.sellingprice();

Access Private Property outside the function

Private properties declared using var or let or const inside class can be accessed by Defining
public method inside class

Ex :- 

var Mobile = function(model_no, sprice){
    var model = model_no;
    var color = 'white';
    var price = 3000; // by defining public method(sellingprice) we can now access private property price.
    var sp = sprice;
    this.sellingprice = function(){
        return (price); //returns private property's value( price value )
    };
};

var samsang = new Mobile('Galaxy',2000);
var nokia = new Mobile('3310',1000);
samsang.sellingprice();


Prototype in Javascript

to add some property outside the class we use Prototype


syntax :--

classname.prototype.key = 'value';

Ex :- 

var Mobile = function(model_no){
    // Instance member
    this.model = model_no;
    this.price = 3000; 
    };
};

var samsang = new Mobile('Galaxy',2000);
var nokia = new Mobile('3310',1000);
Mobile.prototype.color = 'white'; //prototype member

document.write(samsang.color);

To access keys of Instance member of object

document.write(Object.keys(samsang));

To access keys of prototype member of object

for (var key in samsang){
    document.write(key); 
}


 way to print in javascript

console.log("hello world");

1. Primitive data type
    - undefined
    - null
    - Booleans

    - String
    - symbol

2. Reference data type
    - Arrays
    - Objects
 

Array Methods

let myArr = [1, 'sari', null, true, false, 45, 56.4];

document.write(myArr.length);  // it returns length of array 
myArr.pop();                   // removes array element from last 
myArr.push("smruti");          // add element at last 
myArr.unshift("saanj");        // add element at first     
myArr.shift();                 // remove first element 
myArr.toString();              // converts array into String
myArr.sort();              // it sorts array
document.write(myArr);

document.location; //ref: "file:///home/jalpesh/Desktop/Training/index.html"

let elemClass = document.getElementsByClassName("container"); //target element by class name
console.log(elemClass);

elemClass[0].style.background = "yellow"; // from class list select 0th element and change it's style

elemClass[0].classList.add("bg-primary"); // add a class in class list of 0th element 

elemClass[0].classList.remove("bg-primary"); // remove class from class list of 0th element 

elemClass[0].innerHTML; // it targets HTML of 0th element
elemClass[0].innerText; // it targets Text of 0th element

document.getElementsByTagName('button'); // target element by Tag Name
document.getElementsByTagName("button")[0].click(); access 0th element and click on it
 
Adding child element in any class or tag

Ex:- 

tn = document.getElementsByTagName("h3");
c1 = document.createElement("p");
c1.innerText = 'this is created new para';
tn[0].appendChild(c1); // to append element

c2 = document.createElement("b");
c2.innerText = "this new created bold element";
tn[0].replaceChild(c2,c1); //to replace c1 with c2 element

tn.removeChild(elem2); // to remove child element
 
Selecting using Query

document.querySelector('.note'); // selects first note class element (.note - class selector)

document.querySelectorAll('.note'); // selects first note class element (.note - class selector)

document.querySelector("#h15"); // selects first element with id h15 (#h15 - class selector)

Event Listener

Ex :- 1

ev = document.getElementsByClassName("note")[0];

    document.getElementById("h11").style.backgroundColor = 'cyan';
    console.log("clicked on element");
})

    el = document.createElement('h3');
    el.innerText = "hey, it's magic, it's magic !!";
    ev.appendChild(el); 
    
})


ev1 = document.getElementsClassName('note')[0];
ev1.addEventListener('mouseover',function(){    // when mouse is moved over element it calls function
    console.log('mouse over element');
})


ev2 = document.getElementsByClassName('note')[0];
ev2.addEventListener('mouseout',function(){    // when mouse is moved out of element it calls function
    console.log('mouse out of element');
})


ev3 = document.getElementsByClassName('note')[0];
ev3.addEventListener('mouseup', function(){
    console.log('mouse up when clicked on element'); //when we left mouse button click it calls function
})


ev4 = document.getElementsByClassName('note')[0];
ev4.addEventListener('mousedown', function(){
    console.log('mouse down when clicked on element'); // when we press mouse button it calls function
})



SetTimeOut and setinterval

seTimeout()
//this is a function takes two argument 
- 1st argument is a function
- 2nd argument is time after which u want to run given function

Ex: 1 

//Arrow Function

sum = (a,b)=>{
    return a+b;
}

setTimeout(sum, 3000); // set time out for sum function

Ex: 2 

setTimeout(sum1(12, 13),3000); //after 3ms it will call sum1 function 

chan = ()=>{
    document.querySelectorAll('.note')[0].innerHTML = "it's magic, it's magic";
}

clr = setTimeout(chan,3000); //after 3ms it will call function
clearTimeout(clr);  to stop setTimeout we pass Id in clearTimeout(clr) returned from setTimeout



Ex :- setInterval

clr = setInterval(chan, 3000); //function will run at every 3ms interval continously, it returns id
clearInterval(clr); // to stop setInterval we pass Id in clearInterval(clr) returned from setInterval

let date;
let time;

setInterval(() => {
    a1 = new Date(); //date object 
    date = a1.toLocaleDateString(); //local date 
    time = a1.getHours() + ' : ' + a1.getMinutes() + ' : ' + a1.getSeconds(); //hour, miute, second
    document.getElementById("time").innerHTML = 'time' + ' on ' + date + ' is '  + time;
}, 1000);

// setInterval repetedly calls passed function 


TO - DO list Project

function getAndUpdate() {
    title1 = document.getElementById('title').value;
    if (localStorage.getItem('title') == null) {
        arr = [];
        arr.push([title1]);
        localStorage.setItem('title', JSON.stringify(arr));
    }
    else {
        arr1 = localStorage.getItem('title');
        arr = JSON.parse(arr1);
        arr.push([title1]);
        localStorage.setItem('title', JSON.stringify(arr));
    }
    update();
}

function update() {
    if (localStorage.getItem('title') == null) {
        arr = [];
        localStorage.setItem('title', JSON.stringify(arr));
    }
    else {
        arr1 = localStorage.getItem('title');
        arr = JSON.parse(arr1);
    }

    // populate data
    let table = document.getElementById('data');
    let str = "";
    arr.forEach((element, index) => {
        str += `
        
    table.innerHTML = str;
}

ele = document.getElementById('add');
ele.addEventListener('click', getAndUpdate);
update();
function deleted(itemIndex) {
    arr1 = localStorage.getItem('title');
    arr = JSON.parse(arr1);
    arr.splice(itemIndex, 1);
    localStorage.setItem('title', JSON.stringify(arr));
    update()
}

function clearstorage() {
    conf = confirm('Do you really want to delete all ?');
    if (conf) {
        localStorage.clear();
    };
    update();
}


Prototype Object in Javascript

Every object is associated with another object.
If A is prototype object of object B.
    - B will inherit all properties of prototype object A.

Every object in javascript is associated with object.prototype object. 

Ex :--
var a = {}; //here object.prototype is prototype object of a;
so, a will inherit all properties of Object.prototype

NOTE :- prototype object of object.prototype is Null.

Ex :-
var b = new Array();
prototype property of constructor function which is in this case 'Array.prototype' is Prototype
Object of Object b. 

so prototype object of b is Array.prototype
 - b will inherit all property of Array.prototype

NOTE :- prototype object of b ---> Array.prototype. 
        prototype object of Array.prototype ---> object.prototype. 
        prototype object of object.prototype ---> Null.

console.log(object.prototype);  // it will return object.prototype

var a = {};
console.log(Object.getPrototypeOf(a));
console.log(Object.getPrototypeOf(a));
    
var b = new Array();
console.log(Object.getPrototypeOf(b)); //Array.prototype
console.log(Object.getPrototypeOf(Array.prototype)); //object.prototype
console.log(Object.getPrototypeOf(Object.prototype)); //null

var b1 = new String();
console.log(Object.getPrototypeOf(b1)); //String.prototype
console.log(Object.getPrototypeOf(String.prototype)); //object.prototype
console.log(Object.getPrototypeOf(Object.prototype)); //null


how prototype works in javascript

prototype is the property of function which points to prototype object. 
prototype object can be access using function_name.prototype

Ex :-
function Mobile(){

}

var samsang = new Mobile();
var nokia = new Mobile();

when we create new object of Mobile() function using new keyword Js engine creates an object 
and sets a  property named __proto__ which points to its function's prototype object. 

samsang.__proto__ === Mobile.prototype;

Ex :- 2
function Mobile(){
    this.a = 10; //instance member
}

var samsang = new Mobile();
samsang.a 
// it will search for a first in object, if it can't find then it will search it in prototype
of object and it can't find it there then will return undefined
//here a is available for object only and not for prototype


Ex :- 3
function Mobile(){
    
}
Mobile.prototype.a = 10; //prototype member 
var samsang = new Mobile();
samsang.a 
// it will search for a in object first and it is not defined as instance member so there is no a in object 
so now it will search for a in prototype and as a is defined as prototype property, it will return a.

// as object can inherit from it's prototype we can access a using below way
samsang.__proto__.a = 10;


Ex :--

function Mobile(){

}
console.log(Mobile); //
console.log(Mobile.prototype);

var lg = new Mobile();
console.log(lg.__proto__);

// verify
console.log(Mobile.prototype === lg.__proto__);

Ex :- 2

//when create Mobile constructor, it creates mobile object and prototype object 
function Mobile(){
    
};

console.log(Mobile);
console.log(Mobile.prototype);

var lg = new Mobile();

''' mobile has prototype property which point to prototype object of mobile 
object of Mobile has __proto__  which also point to prototype object of mobile so we can write as below'''

console.log(Mobile.protptype === lg.__proto__);

console.log(Mobile === Mobile.prototype.constructor);


Prototype Inheritance in Javascript

prototype is inherited in javascript instead of class.

Process of inheriting from super class.

function Mobile(){
    this.a =  10;
};

Mobile.prototype.z = 30;
var samsang = new Mobile();

function Nokia(){
    Mobile.call(this); // calls Mobile class constructor to inherit all properties and methods. 
    this.b = 20;
};

var s = new Nokia();
console.log(s.a); // we can access variable a of Mobile class using object of this class.
console.log(s.z) //we can access prototype property of super(parent) class using prototype inheritance.

when we make a constructor function Mobile(), 
it creates two object, 
- one object is of same name of constructor, (Mobile() object).
- other object is prototype object of this function, (Mobile.prototype object). 
    - constructor function (Mobile) has a property which is called prototype property. 
    - this property (prototype) points to prototype object (Mobile.prototype).
    - prototype object (Mobile.prototype) of function also has one property which is __proto__.
    - this property (__proto__) points to it's prototype object (object.prototype).
    - object.prototype has __proto__ property which points to null.

when we create object (samsang) of this constructor, it also defines a property named __proto__.
    - property of this object points to it's own function's prototype (Mobile.prototype object).

If we create another constructor function let's say Nokia, it will also follow same process as above. 
it creates two object, 
- one object is of same name of constructor, (Nokia() object).
- other object is prototype object of this function, (Nokia.prototype object). 
    - constructor function (Nokia) has a property which is called prototype property. 
    - this property (prototype) points to prototype object (Nokia.prototype).
    - prototype object (Nokia.prototype) of function also has one property which is __proto__.
    - this property (__proto__) points to it's prototype object (object.prototype).
    - object.prototype has __proto__ property which points to null.

when we create object (samsang) of this constructor, it also defines a property named __proto__.
    - property of this object points to it's own function's prototype (Nokia.prototype object).

Now Inheritance means accessing all the things from super class in base class.note
    let's here Mobile is super or parent class and Nokia is base or child class.

Now to access all properties from Mobile class in Nokia class, 
    - we have to call or initialize constructor of super class in base class.
    - for calling constructor of super class (Mobile)
        - write Mobile.call(this) in base class. 
        
Mobile.call(this) calls super class constructor and initialize all variable of super class constructor 
and made it available to access in base class.

Prototype Inheritance
Now to use prototype inheritance we need to link Nokia.protype with Mobile.protype so that we can inherit 
from Mobile.prototype directly instead of object.prototype for that we have to write
    - base_class_name.prototype = Object.create(Super_class_name.prototype)
    - Nokia.prototype = Object.create(Mobile.prototype)
        - It links prototype object of base class with prototype object of super class 
        - so we can access prototype property of super class 
        - it gives prototype inheritance 
        

- to access prototype property of parent class we use prototype inheritance
- to reset constructor - Nokia.prototype.constructor = Nokia;


One Super class and two sub class


Super class
var Mobile = function(){
};
//prototype Method
Mobile.prototype.getModel = function(){
    return this.model;
};

Sub class 
var Samsung = function(model, price){
    this.model = model;
    this.price = price;
};

Sub class 
var Lenovo = functon(){
    this.model = model;
}
Samsung.Prototype.getprice = function(){
    return this.price;
}

Inheritance 
Samsung.prototype = Object.create(Mobile.prototype);
Samsung.prototype.constructor = Samsung;

Lenovo.prototype = Object.create(Mobile.prototype);
Lenovo.prototype.constructor = Lenovo;

var galaxy = new Samsung('Galaxy', 3000);
console.log(galaxy.getmodel());

Example :- super class with a parameter 

var Mobile = function(model){
    this.model = model;
};

Mobile.prototype.getmodel = function(){
    return this.model;
}

var Samsung = function(model, price){
    Mobile.call(this, model);
    this.price = price;
};

//Inheritance

Samsung.prototype = Object.create(Mobile.prototype);
Samsung.prototype.constructor = Samsung;

var galaxy = new Samsung('Galaxy',3000);
console.log(galaxy.getmodel()); // it will return undefined because we didn't pass any value for model

for accessing the value of model, we have to pass value of in Mobile.call(this, model); and in Samsung 
function.


Method Overriding

when we define method with same name and different characteristic and when we call it the latest method 
is called is called overriding of method.
6+
Function for inheritance:- 
function extend(child,parent){
    child.prototype = Object.create(parent.prototype);
    child.prototype.constructor = child;
}

};

    return "super class show method";

};

    return "Sub class show method";

Multilevel Inheritance in Javascript


Super class :--

var Mobile = function(){
    this.a = 10;
}
Mobile.prototype.z = 30;

Sub class :--

var Samsung = function(){
    // It calls super class constructor and initialize property. without this you can not access Super
    class property using sub class object
    Mobile.call(this);
    this.b = 20;
}

var Galaxy = function(){
    Samsung.call(this);
    this.c = 100;
}

Prototype Inheritance

Samsung.prototype = Object.create(Mobile.prototype);
Samsung.prototype.constructor = Samsung;

Galaxy.prototype = Object.create(Samsung.prototype);
Galaxy.prototype.constructor = Galaxy;

var m = new Mobile();
var s = new Samsung();
var g = new Galaxy();

console.log('Galaxy Object can access');
console.log('Mobile A: ' + g.a );
console.log('Samsung B: ' + g.b );
console.log('Mobile prototype z: ' + g.z);
console.log('Galaxy C: ' + g.c);

console.log('Samsung Object can access');
console.log('Mobile A: ' + s.a);
console.log('Mobile prototype: ' + s.z);

// this will return undefined
console.log('Samsung B: ' + s.b);
console.log('Galaxy c: ' + s.c)

console.log('Mobile object can access');
console.log('Mobile A: ', m.a);
console.log('Mobile prototype object z: ' + m.z);

// this will return undefined
console.log('Samsung B: ' + m.b);
console.log('Galaxy c: ' + m.c);



Composition or Mixins
         

when we inherit from super class all methods of super class is getting inherited
    but sometimes sub class doesn't need all method and to avoid unnecessary methods being inherited,
    we use Mixins in Javascript.


Function for Inheritance :- 
function extend(child, parent){
    child.prototype = Object.create(parent.prototype);
    child.prototype.constructor = child;
}

Super class:- 

var Human = function(){

};
//Prototype member
Human.prototype.walk = function(){
    return 'Super class walk metho';
};

Human.prototype.talk = function(){
    return 'Super class talk method';
};

Human.prototype.eat = function(){
    return 'Super class eat method';
};

Sub class:-

var Animal = function(){

};

//sub class Animal inheriting super class Human

extend(Animal, Human);

var Robot = function(){

};

//sub class Robot extending from super class Human

extend(Robot, Human); // when we inherit from human class all methods of super class is getting inherit 
but robot can not eat so we don't want this method so we use Mixins in Javascript.


Composition And Mixins

we will define object Literal for methods. and then we will assign required methods to our object
var eating = {
    eat : functon(){
        return 'I can eat';
    }
};

var walking = {
    walk : function(){
        return 'I can walk';
    }
};

var talking = {
    talk : function(){
        return 'I can talk';
    }
};


var Rahul = Object.assign({}, eating, walking, talking);

/* object.assign --> assign all sources --> (here eating, walking ..) to target --> (here {} empty object)
and then to object (here Rahul) */

/* here {} empty object is target and eating, walking etc are sources sources are assigned to 
empty object {} and then empty object assign it to object we are creating (Rahul object here) */

console.log(Rahul.eat());
console.log(Rahul.walk());
console.log(Rahul.talk());

var Robot = Object.assign({}, walking, talking);

console.log(Robot.walk());
console.log(Robot.talk());     

/* Now if we want to create 1000 human we have write 1000 time all above so we can create Human class*/

//Human class
var Human = function(){

};

/* Now instead of assigning to empty object we will directly assign all sources to Human.prototype object
which will take all sources in it */

//compositing feature to Human
Object.assign(Human.prototype, eating, walking, talking);

/* Now instead of writing all code we can create object of Human class*/
var Rahul = new Human();
var Siddhi = new Human();

// Robot function 
var Robot = function(){

};

// Compositing feature to Robot 
Object.assign(Robot.prototype, walking, talking);

var RoboCop = new Robot();


Mixins Function

function mixin (target, ...sources){
    Object.assign(target, ...sources)
}

mixin(Robot.prototype, walking, talking);


Class in Javascript

classes are in fact special function.

there are two ways to define class in javascript using class keyword
- Class Declaration
- Class expression


1. Class Declaration

Syntax :--  

class class_name {
        constructor(){
            Properties
        }
        Methods
}
Ex :--

class Mobile {
    constructor(){
        this.model = 'Galaxy';
    }
    show(){return this.model + "Price 3000";
        }
}
var nokia = new Mobile();

Ex : - 2 Class Declaration
    
class Mobile {
    constructor(){
        //Instance member
            this.a = 12;
            this.show = function(){
                return "Instance member";
            };
    }
    // prototype Member 
    display(){
        return "Prototype member"; 
    }
}

var nokia = new Mobile();
console.log(nokia.a);
console.log(nokia.show());
console.log(nokia.display());


constructor

The constructor method is a special method for creating and initializing an object created within class.
there can be only one constructor in one class. 
- It creates and initialize object


Default constructor in Javascript

if you do not specify a constructor method, default constructor is used.

Ex:- 

class Mobile {
    show(){
        return this.model + "Price Rs 3000";
    }
}
var nokia = new Mobile();

/* here we didn't define constructor so default constructor will be used, but when we define constructor,
it overrides default constructor */ 

class Mobile {}
    display(){
        return "this is prototype member and we are using default constructor";
    }
}

var nokia = new Mobile();
nokia.display();


Parameterized Constructor

    - here we are passing parameter in constructor so it is called parameterized constructor.  
class Mobile {
    constructor(model_no){
        this.model = model_no;
    }
    show(){
        return this.model + "price Rs. 3000";
    }
}
var nokia = new Mobile('Galaxy');


2. Class Expression

class expression can be named or unnamed.
- Unnamed class Expression - we are not giving name to class

syntax:- 

var Mobile = class {
    constructor(){
        properties;
    };
};

Ex :--

var Mobile = class {
    constructor(model){
        this.model = model;
    };
    display(){
        return this.model;
    };
};
        
- Named class Expression

syntax:- we are giving name to class (here Mobile2)

var Mobile = class Mobile2 {
    constructor(){
        properties;
    };
};

Ex :--

var Mobile = class Mobile2{
    constructor(model){
        this.model = model;
    };
    display(){
        return this.model;
    };
};


Class Hoisting

    -  class declaration and class expression are not hoisted. 
    -  you first need to declare your class and then access it.

    we can not create object before class declaration. 

    var nokia = new Mobile();  // we can not create object before creating class. 

    class Mobile{
        constructor(){
            properties 
        };
    };
    

Vaariable Hoisting

HOisting is the javascript's default behavior of moving declaration to the top of  the function,if defined
in function, or the top of the global context, if outside a function. 

var a; // variable declaration
a = 10; // variable initialization

var a = 10; // javascript devides it in two part declaration and initialization


we write like below
 
var a = 10;
document.write(a);
var b = 20;


javascript compile it like below 

/* javascript scans document, it moves all declaration to top of compiling and let the initialization 
remain on the same place where they were */
 
var a; // declaration part of a 
var b; // declaration part of b moved on top 
a = 10; // Initialization of var a is seperated from expression and placed after all var declaration
document.write(a);
b = 20; // Initialization part remained on same place


variable can be used before it has been declared
 


we write like below
 
a = 10; // we can access a before declaration because of hoisting
document.write(a);
var a;


javascript compile it like below 

var a;
a = 10;
document.write(a);


Only variable declarations can be hoisted to the top, not variable initialization


we write like below
 
var a = 10; // we can access a before declaration because of hoisting
document.write(a + " " + b);
var b = 20;


javascript compile it like below 

var a = 10;
var b;
document.write(a + " " + b);
b = 20;

javascript keep variable declation in function to top of the function

we write like below
 
var i = 'hello';
document.write(i);
function(){
    document.write(i);
    var i = "hello";
}


javascript compile it like below 

var i;
i = "hello";
document.write(i);  // hello will be printed because we declared and initialized i before printing
function show(){
    var i;
    document.write(i); // undefined will be printed becuase we didn't initialize i to any value
    i = "hello";
}


Inheritance in Javascript

accessing or using properties of parent class in child class is called Inheritance. 

- The extends keyword is used in class declaraton or class expression to create a class which is 
a child of another class.

- The extends keyword can be used to subclass custom class as well as built in- class.

Syntax :-  Inheriting Custom Class 

class Father{

};

class Child extends Father{

};

syntax:- Inheriting Built-in Class ----> Date, String, Array 

class myDate extends Date{

};

Ex :- 
class Father{
    showFMoney(){
        return "Father Money";
    };
};

class Child extends Father{
    showCMoney(){
        return "Child money";
    };
};

class GrandsSon extends Child{
    showGMoney(){
        return "GrandSon Money";
    };
};

var suman = new Child();
console.log(suman.showFMoney());
console.log(suman.showCMoney());

var swati = new GrandsSon();
console.log(swati.showFMoney());
console.log(swati.showCMoney());
console.log(swati.showGMoney());


Super Method in Javascript

/* If we use constructor in parent class and use object of Child class for passing parameter then 
we do it. */

/* but when we use constructor in child class also, Javascript gives error --->
Uncaught ReferenceError: Must call super constructor in derived class before accessing 'this' 
or returning from derived constructor at new Child */

/* Super() Method is used to initialize parent class constructor. 
If there is constructor present in subclass, it needs to first call super() before using "this".
A constructor can use the super keyword to call the constructor of a parent class. */

/* Sub class Inherits all properties and methods from parent class which needs to be initialized,
 when we don't use constructor in sub class, it uses default constructor, default constructor has Super
 method which initialize all properties and methods of parent class by calling its constructor.
 but when we use constructor in sub class, in that case we are overriding default constructor, 
 so we have to call super() method explicitly to initialize constructor of parent class */

 /* If we are passing any parameter in parent constructor then we have to pass that in sub class's 
 constructor and super() method. */

 /* first statement must be super() method in constructor of sub class then we can write this.a or etc. */
Ex :--

class Father{
    constructor(money){
        this.Fmoney = money;
    };
    showFMoney(){
        return this.money + " Father Money";
    };
};

class Child extends Father{
    constructor(money){
        super(money); // first statement must be super() method in constructor 
        this.a = 10; 
    }
    showCMoney(){
        return "Child money";
    };
};

class GrandsSon extends Child{
    showGMoney(){
        return "GrandSon Money";
    };
};

var suman = new Child(10000);
console.log(suman.showFMoney());
console.log(suman.showCMoney());


Method Overriding in Javascript

Same function name with different implementation. 

/* method name will be same but if we want to add or remove some feature from that method, we will write 
that method again with same name but required modification, is called method overriding. */

Ex :--

class Father{
    show(){
        return "super class method";
    };
};

class Son extends Father{
    show(){
        return "Sub class method"; // here inherited show method from parent, is overriden with new code
    };
};

var s = new Son();
console.log(s.show());


Static Method in Javascript

/* static keyword is used to define a static method for a class. */
/* static methods are called without creating an object and can not be called through object */
/* static method are often used to  create utility function for an application */
/* static method can be called using class_name */
/* this method is related to class and not any object so when we need common thing in class, we use it */

Ex :--

class Mobile{
    constructor(){};
    static disp(){
        return "this is display method";
    };
};

Mobile.disp(); // calling static method using class_name 


Array in Javascript

    - arrays are collection of data items 
    - we use when we have to deal with multiple data items. 
    - it is speacial type of object.

var stu = ["sarita", "smruti"];
console.log(typeof(stu));


Declartion and Initialization of Array

    - Using array Literal
    - Using Array constructor

Using array Literal
Syntax:- 
var array_name = [];

Ex :--

var stu = [];
stu[0] = "smruti";
stu[1] = "smriti";
stu[3] = "smri";

or 

var stu = ["sarita", "smruti"];

Note :- Array starts with 0 index. 

or

var a = 10, b = 20, c = 30;
var num = [a,b,c];

Using Array constructor

Syntax :- 

var array_name = new Array();

Ex:- 

var stu = new Array(value1, value2, value_n);
var stu = new Array(smruti, sarita, bali, 45);
stu[4] = "mamma";

// when we pass one parameter in array, it will take it as length and not argument so array will be empty 
// this will create an empty array with 5 length. so it is not good idea to use array if we have 1 value. 
var stu = new Array(5);  

Array Important points
 - Javascript arrays are 0 indexed: the first element of an array is at 0 index 
 - Using an invalid number returns undefined.
 - It's possible to quote the javascript array indexes as well (e.g. stu['2'] instead of stu[2])
 - Arrays can not use string as element index, it must use integer.
 - There is no associative array in javascript like stu['fees'] = 200;
 - It is better to Array Literal.

 Access Array in Javascript

 var stu = ["sarita", "smruti"];
 stu[2] = "Rahul";
 document.write(stu[0]);
 document.write(stu[1]);
 document.write(stu[12]); // undefined 

Modifying Array element in javascript

var stu = ["sarita", "smruti"];
document.write(stu);
stu[1] = "Rahul"; // modified element of index 1
document.write(stu);

var stu = ["sarita", "smruti"];
var geek = stu; // assigning array 
document.write(geek);
document.write(stu);
geek[2] = "sweety";  // if we modify in  geek, stu array will also be modified. 
document.write(geek);
document.write(stu);

Removing Array element

Array element can be removed using delete operator.
this operator sets the array element it is invoked on to undefined but does not change the array's length. 

Syntax :- 

var stu = ["sarita", "smruti"]; 
delete Array_name[index];
Ex :- delete stu[0]; // it sets the element to undefined but does not change the length

Length property of array

the length property retrives the index of the next available position at the end of array.
the length property is automatically updated as new elements are added to the array.
length is commonly used to iterate through all element of array. 

length starts from 1.
Index starts from 0. 
var stu = ["sarita", "smruti"]; 
document.write(stu.length);

Array for loop

var stu = ["sarita", "smruti", "Rahul", "Riya", "ravina"]; 
for(var i; i< stu.length; i++){
    document.write(stu[i]);
}

forEach loop

The forEach calls a provided function once for each element in an array, in order.   

Syntax :-

array.forEach(function(value, index, arr)){

});

where, value = it displays array element  // It is the current value of array index 
       Index = It display array index number  // Array's index number
       arr = It displays array name  //The array object the current element belongs to 

Ex:- 

geek = ["sarita", "smruti", "sweety"]
geek.forEach(function(element){
    console.log(element);
});

for of loop

the for...of statement creates a loop iterating over iterable objects. 

Syntax :- 

for (var variable_name of array){

};

Ex :- 

var geek = ["sarita", "smruti", "sweety"];
for (let value of geek){
    console.log(value);
};

Input from User in javascript

you can get input from user in an empty array. 

no = prompt('enter the no of name - ');
stu = [];
for(let i = 0; i < no; i++ ){
    stu[i] = prompt("enter the name :- ");
}
console.log(stu);

var stu = new Array(3);
var ln = stu.length;
 
Multidimentional array

Multidimentional array is arrays of arrays

Multidimentional array can be 2D, 3D, 4D etc... 

Ex:- 

2D --> var name[[],[],[]];

var data = [
            ["Rahul", "Dell", 16], 
            ["Smruti", "lenovo", 23], 
            ["HP", "Zed", 45] ];

for(let i=0; i< 3; i++){
    for(let j=0; j< 3; j++){
        console.log(data[i][j]);
    };
};

var stu = new Array([], [], []);

How to create empty 2D array

- using array literal 

var geek = [[], []];

- using array constructor

var geek = new Array([], []);
for(let i = 0; i< 2; i++){
    for(let j = 0; i< 2; j++){
        document.write(i + " " + j);
    };
    document.write("< br>");
};

Ex :- 
var geek = [];
var rows = 2;
var cols = 3;
for(var i = 0; i < rows; i++){
    geek[i] = []; // it creates empty array in array ---> [[], [], [] ... ]
}
for(var i = 0; i< rows; i++){
    for(var j = 0; j< cols; j++){
        document.write(geek[i][j] + " ");
        //document.write(i +  " " + j + "|");
    }
    document.write("< br>");
};

Ex :- 

var rows = 2;
var cols = 3;
var geek = new Array(rows);
for(var i = 0; i < rows; i++){
    geek[i] = new Array(cols); // it creates empty array in array ---> [[], [], [] ... ]
}
for(var i = 0; i< rows; i++){
    for(var j = 0; j< cols; j++){
        document.write(geek[i][j] + " ");
        //document.write(i +  " " + j + "|");
    }
    document.write("< br>");
};

How to get input from User in 2D array
 
var rows = 3;
var cols = 3;
var stu = new Array(3);
for(let i = 0; i< rows; i++){
    stu[i] = new Array(cols);
};
for(var i = 0; i< rows; i++){
    for(var j = 0; j< cols; j++){
        stu[i][j] = prompt('enter element in array');
        document.write(stu[i][j] + " ");
    };
    document.write("< br>")
};

Concat() Method in javascript

/* this method is used to merge two or more arrays.
 This method does not change an existing arrays, but instead returns new array. */

 Syntax :- new_array = old_array.concat(value1, value2, value_n); // for concating value 
 Syntax :- new_array = old_array1.concat(old_array2, old_array_n); // for concating array 
 
 Ex:- 
 var geek = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit"];
 var new_geek = geek.concat("Raj", "Ravi"); // adding value in old array 
 Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Raj", "Ravi"]

 var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit"];
 var geek2 = ["Riya", "Rehan"];
 var new_geek = geek1.concat(geek2);
 Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Riya", "Rehan"]


 Join() Method in Javascript

- join() method joins the element of an array into string, and returns the string. 
- The element will be separated by a specified separator. The default separator is comma (,). 

Syntax :- 
array_name.join(separator);

Ex: - 
var geek = ["Riya", "Rehan", "sweety"];
console,log(geek.join(','));
Output :-Riya,Rehan,sweety

console,log(geek.join('/'));
Output :-Riya/Rehan/sweety

console,log(geek.join(' or '));
Output :-Riya or Rehan or sweety 

console,log(geek.join(' '));
Output :-Riya Rehan sweety  

Reverse() Method 

the reverse() method reverses the order of the elements in an array. 

Syntax :- array_name.reverse();

var geek = ["Riya", "Rehan", "sweety"];
geek.reverse();

console.log(geek); 
Output :-["sweety", "Rehan", "Riya"]

Slice() method 
Slice() method returns a copy of a portion of an array into new array object  selected from begin
to end(end not included) the original array will not be modified. 

Syntax :-  array_name.slice(begin, end);

start : - 
    - If begin is undefined, slice begins from index 0. 
    - If begin is greater than the length of sequence, an empty array is returned.
    - A negative index can be used, indicating an offset from end of the sequence. slice(-2) extracts
      the last two element in the sequence. 

End :- 
    - If end is omitted, slice extracts through end of sequence (arr.length). 
    - If end is greater than the length of sequence, slice will extracts to end of the sequence.
    - A negative index can be used, indicating an offset from the end of the sequence. 
    - slice extracts up to but not including end.                                 

Ex :- 
var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];
var new_arr = geek.slice(1, 3);
console.log(new_arr); 
Output :-["Sonam", "Sumit"]

var new_arr = geek.slice(-3, -1);
console.log(new_arr);
Output :- ["Sumit", "Ruhi"]

var new_arr = geek.slice(undefined, 3);
console.log(new_arr);starts from 0 upto 3
Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi"]

toString() Method

the toString method returns the string containing (',') separated value of the array. 
this method is invoked automatically when you print an array. 
It is equivalent to invoking join method without any argument.
the returned string will separate  the element  in the array with commas. 

Syntax :- 

var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];
console.log(geek1.toString());
Output :- Rahul,Sonam,Sumit,Ruhi,Reva

Array.isArray() Method 

The Array.isArray() method determines wheather the passed value is Array. 
this function returns true if the object is an Array and false if not. 

Syntax :- Array.isArray(value);
Ex :- 

var result = Array.isArray(["Rohan", "Raj"]); // true
var result = Array.isArray("a string"); // false   

var result = Array.isArray(["Rohan", "Raj"]); 
console.log(result);
Output :- true

var result = Array.isArray("a string"); 
console.log(result);
Output :- false 

splice() method

the splice method changes the content of an array by removing existing elements and/or adding new element
this method changes the origin array. 

Syntax :- array_name.splice(start, deletecount, replacevalues);

Start :- it specifies at what position to add/remove items, use negative values to specify the position
from the end of the array. 

deletecount :- it is the number of element to delete begging with start. 

Replace value :- replace values are inserted in place of the deleted element. if more than one separate it 
by comma. 

var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];

geek1.splice(2); // it will remove all element start from index 2
console.log(geek1);  
Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam"]

geek1.splice(2, 1); // it will remove 1 element start from index 2
console.log(geek1); 
Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Ruhi", "Reva"]

geek1.splice(2, 0, "swati"); // it will not remove anything but insert "swati" at position 2
console.log(geek1); 
Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam", "swati", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"]

geek1.splice(2, 0, "swati", "Ravina"); // it will not remove anything but start inserting from index 2
console.log(geek1); 
Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam", "swati", "Ravina", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"]

geek1.splice(2, 3, "swati", "Ravina"); // it will remove 3 elements from index 2 and then insert from 2
console.log(geek1); 
Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam", "swati", "Ravina"]

IndexOf() Method

- this method allows to find the occurrence of an item in array. 
- If the item not found, it returns -1. 
- the search will start at the specified position or at the beginning if no start position is specified, 
and end the search at the end of the array. 
- If the item is present more than once, the indexOf method will return the position of first occurrence. 

Syntax :- var position = array_name.indexOf(item, start);

Ex :- 
var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];

var position = geek1.indexOf("Rohit", 2); //search "Rohit" start searching from index 2 
console.log(position); // -1
Output :- -1

var position = geek1.indexOf("Rahul"); //search "Rahul" start searching from index 0
console.log(position);
Output :- 0 

var position = geek1.indexOf("Ruhi",2); //search "Ruhi" start searching from index 2 
console.log(position);
Output :-  3

Fill() Method

the fill() method fills all the element in array with a static value. 

Syntax :-- array_name.fill(value, start, end);

var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];
console.log(geek1.fill('Don')); // all elements fill with Don 
Output :- ["Don", "Don", "Don", "Don", "Don"];

console.log(geek1.fill('Don', 1, 3)); // from index 1 to 3 fill with Don (3 not included)
Output :- ["Rahul", "Don", "Don", "Ruhi", "Reva"];

var new_array = new Array(3).fill("Don");
console.log(new_array);
Output :-

Unshift() Method

the unshift() method adds one and more elements to the beginning of an array and returns the new length 
of an array.
this method change the length of an array. 

Syntax :- 

Array_name.unshift(value1, value2, value_n);

Ex :- 

var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];
geek1.unshift("Raja", "Riya");
var arr_len = geek1.unshift("Raja", "Riya"); // it will add element and return length 

console.log(geek1);
Output :- ["Raja", "Riya", "Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"]

console.log(arr_len);
Output :- 7


Push() Method

The push() method adds one or more element to the end of an array and returns the new length of the array.
the new item will be added at the end of array.
this method changes the length of array. 

Syntax :- 
Array_name.push(value1, value2, value_n);

Ex :- 

var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];
var arr_len = geek1.push("Raja", "Riya");
console.log(geek1);
Output :- ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva", "Raja", "Riya"]

console.log(arr_len);
Output :- 7

shift() Method

the shift() method removes the first element from the beginning of an array and returns the removed element
this method change the length of an array. 

Syntax :- 

Array_name.shift();

Ex :- 

var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];
var removed = geek1.shift(); // it will remove first element of an array
console.log(removed);
Output :-Rahul

pop() Method

the pop() method removes the last element of an array and returns the removed element
this method change the length of an array. 

Syntax :- 

Array_name.pop();

Ex :- 

var geek1 = ["Rahul", "Sonam", "Sumit", "Ruhi", "Reva"];
var removed = geek1.pop(); // it will remove last element of an array
console.log(removed);
Output :- Reva


boolean in javascript


Boolean is the built-in object Primitive data -type.

there are two boolean :- 
 - True 
 - False 

Primitive Value:- 
var v1 = true;
var v2 = false;

boolean function :--

var fun = Boolean(true);
var fun = Boolean(false);

boolean constructor
var v1 = new Boolean(true);

If value parameter is omitted or is 0, -0, null, false, NaN, undefined, or the empty string(""), the 
object has an initial value of false. 

var a = Boolean() // false
var a = Boolean("") // false
var a = Boolean(0) // false
var a = Boolean(-0) // false
var a = Boolean(NaN) // false
var a = Boolean(null) // false
var a = Boolean(undefined) // false
var a = Boolean(false) // false
var a = Boolean(true) // True
var a = Boolean(10) // True
var a = Boolean(-10) // True

primitive type :-
var str = ""welcome""; // string type

using constructor :-
var str = new String("welcome"); // object type

joining of string is called string concatenation

+ is concat operator

console.log(str + str1);    Output :- welcome hello

Ex:- "Hello".concat(" something ","missing");

Escape sequence in javascript

\0 - "the null character"
\' - "single quote"
\" - "double quote"

\n - "new line"
\r - "carriage return"

\b - "backspace"
\f - "form feed"

Template Literal / Template String

- Template literal are string literal allowing embedded expression.
- we can use multi-line string and string interpolation feature with them. 
- Template literals are enclosed by the back-tick(` `) character instead of double or single quote. 

Multi Line string :- 

- we can not write multi line string using single or double quote. 
- but we can write it using back tick. 

var str = `hi
            hello
            welcome `;

String Interpolation :- 

- Template Litera can contain placeholders. 
- this are incicated by dollar sign and curly braces (${expression}).

var str1 = "hello";
console.log(`${str1} world`);
console.log(`${5 + 4} world`);
console.log(`${a + b} world`);
console.log(`${function()} world`); // we can also call function 


Ex :- calling function using back tick is very Important and useful concepts in javascript frameworks. 

function myfun(say){
    return say;
}
console.log(`${myfun("I love cycling")}`);
Output :- I love cycling

Tagged Template

- Tagged Templates are advanced form of template literal. 
- Tags allow you to parse template literal with function. 
- the first argument of a tag function contains an array of string values. 
- The remaining arguments are related to the expression. 
- In the end, your function can return your manipulated string. 


Length property in string 

length proper returns the length of the string 

var str = "hey, I am here";
console.log(str.length);
Output :- 14

charAt() method

charAt(position);
- this method returns the character at specified index (position). 

var str = "hey, I am here";
console.log(str.charAt(10)); // it will return char at 10th index of string
Output :- h 

charCodeAt() Method

- this method returns unicode of the character at specified index in a string. 

var str = "hey, I am here";
console.log(str.charCodeAt(10)); // it will return char at 10th index of string
Output :- 104

toUpperCase and toLowerCase method

toUpperCase :- it converts string into upper case letter 
toLowerCase :- it converts string into lower case letter 

var str = "hey, I am here";
console.log(str.toUpperCase());     
Output :- HEY, I AM HERE

console.log(str.toLowerCase());     
Output :- hey, i am here

trim() Method in javascript

It removes white space from both side of string 

var str = "             hey, I am here            ";
console.log(str.trim());
Output :- hey, I am here

replace() Method in javascript 

replace(old, new);
 
- replace method replace specified value with another value in a string.
- replace function replaces only the first match. 


var str = "hey, I am here";
console.log(str.replace("here", "everywhere"));
Output :- hey, I am everywhere

split() Method 
- split() Method breaks the string into separate string according to delimeter passed.
- It returns array of string separated by passed delimeter 

var str = "hey, I am here";
console.log(str.split(" ")); //it will break string from space and return an array of all strings 

Output :- ["hey,", "I", "am", "here"]

indexOf() method

- this method takes a string argument and returns the first occurrence of the argument in string. 
- If the argument is not found returns length-1 
- it also takes option argument to specify start index for searching 
- It connot take regular expression as search value 

var str = "hey, I am here";
console.log(str.indexOf("e",11)); // it will start searching from 11th index 
Output :- 11

console.log(str.indexOf("sweety")); // it will return -1 
Output :- -1 

search() Method

- It is same as indexOf() method. 
- It searches a string for specified value and returns the position of match 
- It cannot take second start position argument 

var str = "hey, I am here";
console.log(str.search("e")); // it will start searching from 11th index 
Output :- 1

console.log(str.search("sweety")); // it will return -1 
Output :- -1

slice() Method

the slice method extracts a part of a string  and return the extracted part in new string. 

var str = "we are on a mission to be something";
console.log(str.slice(8, 20)); // 20 mot included
Output :- n a mission 

substring() Method

The substring is similar to slice() the only difference is it does not take - negative index. 
the first argument specifies the index where substring begins 
the optional second argument specifies index at which substring ends. 
methods returns string containing the substring beginning at the given index up to but not including 
the character at the index specified by second argument.

var str = "we are on a mission to be something";
console.log(str.substring(8, 20)); // 20 mot included
Output :- n a mission 

substr() Method

- The substr is similar to slice().
- the first argument specifies the index where substring begins 
- the second argument specifies no of character we want to access. 
methods returns the part of string between the start index and a number of character after it. 
- It extracts length of character from string, counting from the start index.
- If start is the positive number, index starts counting at the start of the string. 
- If start is the Negative number, index starts counting at the end of the string. 

 
var str = "we are on a mission to be something";
console.log(str.substr(8, 8)); // it will extracts 8 character starting from index 8
Output :- n a mission

constructor:-

NaN in javascript

- The NaN property represents "Not a Number" value. 
- This property indicates that a value is not a legal number.
- NaN never compare equal to anything even itself.
- The NaN property is same asthe Number.Nan property.

//NaN (Not a number)

console.log(20/"sar"); // not a legal number
Output :- NaN
 
isNaN() Method in javascript

this isNaN() function is used to determine whether a value is illegal number (Not-a-Number)
- this function returns true if the value equates to NaN. otherwise it returns false. 
console.log(20/"sar"); // not a legal number 
Output :- NaN

console.log(isNaN("sar")); // not a legal number
Output :- true

console.log(isNaN("50")); //  it converts it into number and then check, it is a legal number 
Output :- false

Infinity and negative Infinity

Infinity or - Infinity is the value javascript will return if the number is too large or too small.
All Infinity values compare equal to each other. 

console.log(5/0); //  it converts it into number and then check, it is a legal number 
Output :- infinity

console.log(-5/0); //  it converts it into number and then check, it is a legal number 
Output :- -infinity

Number methods

toString()
toExponential()
toFixed()
toPrecision()
valueOf();

toString Method

toString() Method returns a number as a string in other words it converts number number into string. 
we can use this method to output numbers as hexadecimal(16), octal(8), binary(2)

Syntax:-

toString();

Ex:- 
var a = 10;
console.log(a.toString());
Output :- 10

convert into binary 

var a = 10;
console.log(a.toString(2)); // Binary conversion 
Output :- 1010 // 8421 method to convert in to binary 

convert into octal 

var a = 10;
console.log(a.toString(8)); // octal conversion
Output :- 12

convert to hexadecimal

var a = 10;
console.log(a.toString(16)); // octal conversion
Output :- a 

toExponential() Method

- this method converts a number into an exponential notation. 

Syntax :- 
Variable_name.toExponential(y)

where y is an integer between 0 and 20 representing the number of digit in the notation after 
the decimal point. If omitted, it is set to as many digits as necessary to represent the value. 

var a = 58975.98745;
console.log(a.toExponential());  // as many digits as necessary to represent the value
Output :- 5.897598745e+4
 
console.log(a.toExponential(2)); // two digit after decimal 
Output :- 5.90e+4

console.log(a.toExponential(4));  // 4 digit after decimal 
Output :- 5.8976e+4

toFixed() Method

the toFixed() method converts a number into a string, keeping a specified number of decimals also 
it rounds the decimal. If the desired number of decimals are higher than the actual number, nulls are 
added to create the desired decimal legth 

Syntax :- 

a.toFixed(y)
where y is the number of digits after the decimal point. default is 0 (no digit after decimal point)

Ex :- 

var a = 19.65823;
console.log(a.toFixed());
Output :-20 // bydefault 0 digit after decimal 

console.log(a.toFixed(2));
Output :-19.66 // 2 digit after decimal 

console.log(a.toFixed(4));
Output :-19.6582 // 4 digit after decimal 

console.log(a.toFixed(8));
Output :-19.65823000 // 4 digit after decimal last 3 0's are added

toPrecision() Method

- the toPrecision() Method formats a number to a specified length. 
- the decimal points and nulls are added(if needed), to create the specified length. 

Syntax :- 

Variable_name.toPrecision(y);

where y is the number of digits. if ommited it returns entire number without formatting 

var a = 19.65823;
console.log(a.toPrecision());
Output :-19.65823 // returns entire number without formatting 

console.log(a.toPrecision(2));
Output :-20 // 2 digit with round off

console.log(a.toPrecision(4));
Output :-19.66 // 4 digit with round off of last digits after decimal

console.log(a.toPrecision(8));
Output :-19.658230 // 8 digit 0 is added at last 

Number.isInteger() Method 

- the Number.isInteger() Method determines whether a value is an integer. 
- it returns true if number or integer else returns false. 

console.log(Number.isInteger());
Output :- false  

console.log(Number.isInteger(100));
Output :- true  

console.log(Number.isInteger(-100));
Output :- true 

console.log(Number.isInteger(8.5));
Output :- false  

console.log(Number.isInteger(8-4));
Output :- true  

console.log(Number.isInteger("100"));
Output :- false  

Number.isSafeInteger() Method 

- the Number.isSafeInteger() Method determines whether a value is a Safe integer. 
- it returns true if number is safe integer else returns false. 
- A safe integer is all integer from 2^53-1 to -2^53-1 

console.log(Number.isSafeInteger());
Output :- false  

console.log(Number.isSafeInteger(100));
Output :- true  

console.log(Number.isSafeInteger(-100));
Output :- true 

console.log(Number.isSafeInteger(8.5));
Output :- false  

console.log(Number.isSafeInteger(4594949949494949444444444444444444444444444444444444444444));
Output :- false

console.log(Number.isSafeInteger("100"));
Output :- false  

Global javascript methods

javascript global method can be used on all javascript data types. 

    - Number()
    - parseFloat()
    - parseInt()

- The number() function converts the object argument to a number that represnts the object's value. 
- If the object can not be converted as a legal number it will return NaN. 
- If the parameter is a Date object, the Number() function returns the number of millisecond since 
  midnight January 1, 1970 UTC.

console.log(Number(true));
Output :- 1  

console.log(Number(false));
Output :- 0

console.log(Number("100"));
Output :- 100 

console.log(Number(100/"hello"));
Output :- NaN 

console.log(Date()));
Output :- Fri Mar 19 2021 23:32:07 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time) 

parseInt() function

- It parse a string and returns an integer. 

Syntax :- parseInt(string, radix)

- radix specify which numeral system to be used. 
- a radix of 16 indicates that the number in string should be parsed from hexadecimal to decimal number.
    - If radix is ommited, javascript assumes as following :--
    - If string begins with 0x, the radix is 16 (hexa)
    - If string begins with any other value, the radix is 10 (decimal)
only the first number in string returned 
leading and trailing spaces are allowed
If the first character can not be converted to a number, parseInt() returns NaN. 

console.log(parseInt("10"));
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseInt("12.00"));
Output :- 12

console.log(parseInt("15.45"));
Output :- 15 

console.log(parseInt("10 20 30")); // will consider first number
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseInt("    10    ")); // remove space
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseInt("10 years")); // it will convert first number to int so 10
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseInt("years 10")); // years is string so not a number
Output :- NaN

console.log(parseInt("010"));
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseInt("12",8)); // 12 octal = 10 decimal
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseInt("0x12")); // 12 hex = 18 decimal
Output :- 18 

console.log(parseInt("10",16)); // 10 hex = 16 decimal
Output :- 16 

parseFloat() function

- It parse a string and returns a Float number. 

Syntax :- parseFloat(string, radix)
- If the first character in specified string is a number it parses string untill end of num and returns 
number as number and not a string. 
- only the first number in string returned 
- leading and trailing spaces are allowed
- If the first character can not be converted to a number, parseFloat() returns NaN. 

console.log(parseFloat("10"));
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseFloat("12.00"));
Output :- 12

console.log(parseFloat("15.45"));
Output :- 15.45

console.log(parseFloat("10 20 30")); // will consider first number
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseFloat("    10    ")); // remove space
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseFloat("10 years")); // it will convert first number to Float so 10
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseFloat("years 10")); // years is string so not a number
Output :- NaN

console.log(parseFloat("010"));
Output :- 10 

console.log(parseFloat("12",8)); // first string is 12 so it will convert 12 into float 
Output :- 12

console.log(parseFloat("0x12")); // first is 0 so it will convert 0 into float 
Output :- 0 

console.log(parseFloat("10",16)); // first string is 10 so it will convert 10 into float 
Output :- 10

Math object in javascript

The Math object holds a set of constants and methods that enable more complex mathematical operations 
than the basic arithmetic operators. we can not instantiate a Math Object. the math object is staic so 
it's properties and methods accessed directly. 

Min() Method and Max() Method in Javascript 

console.log(Math.min(50, 2, 90, 100, 20));
Output :- 2

console.log(Math.max(50, 2, 90, 100, 20));

The floor() method rounds a number downwards to the nearest integer, and returns the result.

Output :- 0

Output :- 0

Output :- -3

Output :- -7

- The round() method rounds to the nearest integer.
- 6.4 will be rounded down, 6.5 will be rounded up.

Output :- 6

Output :- 0

Output :- 1

Output :- -2
