Date in Javascript

the date object provides a set of methods for manipulating time and date.

it reads client machine date and time so if the client's date and time is incorrect 
- Days of week and month of year starts from 0.
0 - sunday, 1 - monday and so on 
0 - january 1 - february and so on

creating date object 

Date objects are created with new Date() constructor. 
Date objects created by programmer are static. they do not contain ticking clock. 

Syntax :- 
new Date();  
new Date(millisecond);
new Date(year,month,day,hours,minutes,seconds,millisecond);
new Date(dateString)

var date = new Date();
console.log(date); // current date and time 

new Date(millisecond) 

- It creates a new object as January 1, 1970, 00:00:00 Universal time(UTC)

var date1 = new Date(1530867166586);  // we can get date from millisecond
var date2 = new Date(8640000);
console.log(date1);
Output :- Fri Jul 06 2018 14:22:46 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

console.log(date2);
Output:- Thu Jan 01 1970 07:54:00 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)


new Date(year,month,day,hours,minutes,seconds,millisecond);

it creates date objects with the date specified by the integer values for the year,month,day,hours,
minutes,seconds,millisecond. we can omit some arguments.

date = new Date(2018,12,4,4,10,16,0);
console.log(date);
Output:- Fri Jan 04 2019 04:10:16 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

new Date(dateString);

- it creates new date object from a date string. 

date = new Date("May 12, 2018 10:16:05");
console.log(date);
Output:- Fri Jan 04 2019 04:10:16 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

ISO date in javascript 

ISO 9601 is the international standard for the representation of date and time. 

var date = new Date("2018-06");
console.log(date);
Output :- Fri Jun 01 2018 05:30:00 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

short date in javascript 

short date are written with an "MM/DD/YYYY" format 
the behavior of "YYYY/MM/DD" is undefined. 
some browser will try to guess the format. some will return NaN.

var date = new Date("06-25-2018");
console.log(date);
    Output :- Mon Jun 25 2018 00:00:00 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

Long Date

Long dates are most often written with a "MMM DD YYY" format. 
month and day can be in any order. 
month can be written in full (January) or abbreviated (jan).

var date = new Date("March 25 2018");
console.log(date);
Output :- Sun Mar 25 2018 00:00:00 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

set Date Methods 

getDate()       Returns the day of month (from 1-31)
setDate()       Set the day as a number(1-31)
setFullYear()   Set the year(optionally month and day)
setHours()      set the hour(0-23)
setMilliseconds() set the millisecond(0-999)
setMinutes()    set the minutes(0-59)
setMonth        set the Month(0-11)
setSeconds()    set the second(0-59)
setTime()       set the time(millisecond since January 1, 1970)


var date = new Date();
console.log(date);
Output :-Sat Mar 20 2021 23:13:54 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

console.log(date.setHours(22));
Output :-  Mar 20 2021 22:56:54 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

console.log(date.setSeconds(46));
Output :- Sat Mar 20 2021 22:56:46 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

console.log(date.set(26));
Output :- Fri Mar 26 2021 22:56:46 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

console.log(date.setFullYear(2022));
Output :- Sat Mar 26 2022 22:56:46 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

console.log(date.setMonth(11));
Output :- Mon Dec 26 2022 22:56:46 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

Get date methods in javascript

getDate()       get the day as a number(1-31)
getFullYear()   get the year as four digit number (yyyy)
getHours()      get the hour(0-23)
getMilliseconds() get the millisecond(0-999)
getMinutes()    get the minutes(0-59)
getMonth()       get the Month(0-11)
getSeconds()    get the second(0-59)
getTime()       get the time(millisecond since January 1, 1970)
getDay()        get the weekday as number(0-6)

var date = new Date();
console.log(date);
Output :- Sat Mar 20 2021 23:32:03 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

console.log(date.getHours());
Output :- 23

console.log(date.getMinutes());
Output :- 32

console.log(date.getSeconds());
Output :- 3

console.log(date.getDate());
Output :- 20

console.log(date.getFullYear());
Output :- 2021

console.log(date.getMonth());
Output :- 2


Retrive month name and day name in javascript 

var date = new Date();
month = date.getMonth();
day = date.getDay();

console.log(getMonthName(month));
console.log(getDayName(day));

function getMonthName(month){
    AllMonth = ["January", "February", "March", "April", "May", "June", "July", "August", "September", 
    "October", "November", "December"];
    return AllMonth[month];
}

function getDay(day){
    AllDay = ["sunday", "monday", "tuesday","wednusday", "thrusday", "friday", "saturday"];
    return AllDay[day];
}

Format Date and Time in Javascript:- 

var date = new Date();
console.log(formatDate(date));
console.log(formatTime(date));

function formatDate(date){
    var date = date.getDate();
    var month = date.getMonth();
    var year = date.getFullYear();
    return date + "-" + month + "-" + year;
}

function formatTime(time){
    var hour = time.getHours();
    var minute = time.getMinutes();
    return hour + "-" + minute;
}

converting Dates to Time 

If you want to create a string in standard format, Date provides three methods :- 

toString()
toUTCstring()
toGMTstring()

toUTCstring() and toGMTstring() format the string according to Internet (GMT) standard,whereas toString()
creates the string according to Local Time. 

var date = new Date();
console.log(date.toString()); 
Output:- Sun Mar 21 2021 19:52:00 GMT+0530 (India Standard Time)

console.log(date.toUTCString()); 
Output:- Sun, 21 Mar 2021 14:22:00 GMT

console.log(date.toGMTString()); 
Output:- Sun, 21 Mar 2021 14:22:00 GMT


What is Document Object Model Javascript


- The Document Object Model(DOM) is a application programming interface (API) for HTML and XML documents. 
- with the document object model, programmar can create and build documents, navigate their structure,
and add, modify, or delete elements and content. 
- the DOM is an object-oriented representation of the webpage, which can be modified with a scripting 
language such as javascript. 
- The DOM model represents a document with a logical tree.
- According to Document Object Model(DOM), every HTML tag is an object. 
- Nested tags are called "children" of enclosing tag. 
- All operation with the DOM starts with document object from it we can access any node. 
- The document object model can be used with any programming language. 


DOM levels


DOM level 0 - this level supports the common document object collections - form[], image[], anchors[],
links[], and applets[]. this is also known as classic or traditional Javascript object Model. 

DOM level 1 - It provides the ability to manipulate all elements in a document through a common 
set of functions. In this level all elements are exposed and parts of the page can be read and written 
all times. 

DOM level 2 - It provides further access to page element primarily related to CSS and focuses on 
combining level 0 and 1 while adding improved support for working with XML document. 

DOM level 3 - Enhanced level of level 1 and 2 and added support for Xpath and keyboard event handling.

DOM level 4 - Enhanced year 2015 

Categories of DOM 

DOM core :- It specifies a generic model for viewing and manipulating a marked up document as tree. 
DOM HTML :- It specifies an extention to core DOM for use with HTML.
this represent DOM level 0 with capability to manipulating all HTML element. 
DOM CSS :- It specifies the interfaces necessary to manipulate CSS rules.
DOM Events :- It adds event handling to DOM. 
DOM XML :- It specifies an extention to core DOM for use with XML. 


Document Tree in Javascript

the HTML document we right is rendered javascript into tree format.
html tag is root of tree.
then all other tag make branches from root.
the text, attribute, or tag inside tag are also make a branch of outer tag. 

Any element is called element Node in javascript. like head, title, h1, br etc. all tags. 
texts are called text Node. 
Comments are called comment Node. 
attribute are called attribute Node.

DOM Node Types

constant Node Type Description
Node.ELEMENT_NODE 1 an Element such as h1 or div
Node.TEXT_NODE 3 Tthe actual text of element or attribute
Node.PROCESSING_INSTRUCTION_NODE 7 an Instuction to a parser on aspect of document
Node.COMMENT_NODE 8 a comment such as
Node.DOCUMENT_NODE 9 a document node
Node.DOCUMENT_TYPE_NODE 10 a document statment
Node.DOCUMENT_FRAGMENT_NODE 11 a document fragement, which represents a lightweight structure to hold a collection of DOM nodes for manipulation or insertion

getElementById Method in javascript

Element Access Methods
Method Description
document.getElementById("ID") get the element with the specified ID
document.getElementsByTagName("Tag_Name"); get all the specified element by the Tag Name
document.getElementsByClassName("Class_Name"); get all specified element by class name
document.querySelector("CSS_Selector"); It returns the first match of the passed selector string
document.querySelectorAll("CSS_Selector"); It returns a node list of DOM elements that match the query 
getElementById("ID_name")

the method getElementById("ID_name") returns element object representing the element whose id propery 
matches the specified string. 

Ex :- getElementById("geek")
    where geek is id.


getElementsByTagName("Tag_Name");

- getElementsByTagName("Tag_Name") returns a node list which updates itself with DOM automatically.
- so modification of DOM tree will be reflected in returned collection. 
- the returned node list or collection of nodes can be accessed by index number starting from 0. 
- a special value "*" returns all element in the document. 
- we can use length property of the Nodelist object to determine the number of elements of specified tag. 

EX :- getElementsByTagName("p");
document.getElementsByTagName("p");
where p is tag name. 

// it will return all element of body 
var result = document.body.getElementsByTagName("*");
console.log(result);



// for getting span elements of specific element which has geek id
var getSpan = document.getElementById("geek");
var result = getSpan.getElementsByTagName("span");

            or 

var result = document.getElementById("geek").getElementsByTagName("span");

// for getting all elements of specific element which has geek id
var result = document.getElementById("geek").getElementsByTagName("*");


Length Property

var len = getSpan.getElementsByTagName("span").length;


Looping through any tag collection

var len = getSpan.getElementsByTagName("h3").length;

for(let i=0; i< len; i++){
    var result = document.getElementsByTagName("h3");
    console.log(result);
}


getElementsByClassName Method in Javascript

- getElementsByClassName("Class_Name") returns a node list which updates itself with DOM automatically.
- so modification of DOM tree will be reflected in returned collection. 
- the returned node list or collection of nodes can be accessed by index number starting from 0. 
- we can use length property of the Nodelist object to determine the number of elements of specified Class. 
- we can also pass multiple class name. 

EX :- document.getElementsByClassName("geek");

//it will return all element of both class geek note but both class should be present in one element 
document.getElementsByClassName("geek note");


// it will return element with class name geek only present in body
document.body.getElementsByClassName("geek");

//if there is any one class present in element then it return that element 

Ex :- 
< h3 class="love color">welcome< /h3>

document.getElementsByClassName("color");
// it will also return  above h3 element because atlist one class name is matching. 

// for getting span elements of specific element which has geek Class
var getSpan = document.getElementsByClassName("geek");
var result = getSpan.getElementsByTagName("span");

            or 

var result = document.getElementByClassName("geek").getElementsByTagName("span");


Length Property

var len = document.getElementsByClassName("geek").length;


Looping through any tag collection

Output :-

    var result = document.getElementsByClassName("geek");
    console.log(result);
}


querySelector("CSS Selector")

- the method querySelector() returns the first element match of the specified selector, or group of selectors. 
- If no matches are found, null is returned. 

Ex :- 
Element Selector 
querySelector("p");
querySelector("p, h1"); // in this case it will return element which comes first in document 

ID Selector 
querySelector("#show1"); // it will return first element which has ID show1
querySelector("#show,#show1"); // it will return element which ID comes first in document

Class Selector 
querySelector(".geek");
querySelector("p.myclass"); // it will return element which has myclass inside p tag 
querySelector(".geek, .myclass")


querySelectorAll("CSS Selector")

- the method querySelectorAll() returns a static(Not live) NodeList representing a list of the document's 
element that match the specified group of selectors. 
- The NodeList object represents collection of nodes. The nodes can be accessed by index number. 
the index starts from 0.
- we can use the length property of the NodeList object. 

Element Selector :- 

querySelectorAll("p");
querySelectorAll("p, div, h1"); // it will return all p, div, h1 tags starting from document

Class Selector :- 

querySelectorAll(".geek");
querySelectorAll("p.myclass"); // it will return element which has myclass inside p tag 
querySelectorAll("p > span.myclass"); // child selector 

Attribute Selector :- 

querySelectorAll("div[id]") //it will return div which has attribute id
querySelectorAll("div[id="geek"]") //it will return div which has attribute id = "geek" value 

Ex :- access a element which has span tag and class = myclass and 
which is inside a element which has id = show.

var data = document.getElementById("show");
var result = data.querySelectorAll("span.myspan");
console.log(result);
Output :- 

or 

// it will get element which has id = show and inside that element the span tag with class name = myclass
var data = document.getElementById("show").querySelectorAll("span.myspan");
console.log(data);
Output :- 

//it will return element which has id = show and inside that element with classname = geek and inside 
that element span tag with classname = myspan will be accessed. 
var result = document.querySelectorAll("#show > .geek > span.myspan");
console.log(result);
Output :- 


length property for querySelectorAll()

var len = document.querySelectorAll(".geek").le ngth; // it will give length of Nodelist 
console.log(len)
Output :- 


querySelectorAll with loop method

var len = document.querySelectorAll(".geek").length; 

for(i=0; i< len; i++){
    var data = document.querySelectorAll(".geek")[i]; 
    console.log(data);
}

Properties of Node object in Javascript

- The Node object represents a single node in the document tree. 
- nodeName
- nodeValue
- nodeType
- textContent
- parentNode
- childNode
- firstChild
- lastChild
- previousSibling
- nextSibling


nodeName

the nodeName read-only property returns the name of the current node as string. 

- comment   "#comment"
- Document  "#document"
- DocumentType the value of documentType.name
- Element   the value of Element.TagName
- Entity    the entity name 
- EntityReferance  the name of entity referance 
- NOtation  the notation name 
- Text      "#text"


nodeValue

- CDATASection        content of CDATASection 
- Comment             content of comment 
- Document            null
- DocumentType        null
- Element             null
- Entity              null
- EntityReferance     null
- NOtation            null
- Text                content of text node
- ProcessingInstruction   entire content excluding the target


nodeType

the read-only Node.nodeType property represents the type of node. 

// Document 
console.log(document.nodeName);
Output :- #document 

console.log(document.nodeValue);
Output :- null 

console.log(document.nodeType);
Output :- 9

// Element 

element = document.getElementById("add");

console.log(element.nodeName);
Output :- BUTTON 

console.log(element.nodeValue);
Output :- null 

console.log(element.nodeType);
Output :- 1

//Text --- to access the text which is inside element and it is first child 
< h2 id="h14">A Description List < !-- comment text is here -- > < /h2>

var txt = document.getElementById("h14");

console.log(txt.firstChild.nodeName);
Output :- #txt

console.log(txt.firstChild.nodeValue);
Output :- A Description list 

console.log(txt.firstChild.nodeType);
Output :- 3

//Comment --- to access the comment which is inside element but next to text so it is sibling

Output :- comment text is here 

console.log(txt.firstChild.nextSibling.nodeType);

// accessing text of element which has Id = "h14" and changing text 
var txt = document.getElementById("h14").firstChild.nodeValue = "This is Important text";
console.log(txt);

Difference between node of an element and element node of an element

- node created by element are called element node and all other are called node of element.
Ex :- h1, html, body, head, title, p etc .. are elements so they are called element node.
while the node created by an element like text, enter, comment, para text all are called node of an element


DOM Traversal in javascript

parentNode :- returns parent node 
parentElement :- returns parent element node 
childNodes :- returns collection of an element's child nodes(including text and comment node)
children - returns a collection of an element's child element node( do not include text and comment node)
firstChild :- return firstChild node of an element (it can be text or comment)
firstElementChild :- returns first child element node of an element 
lastChild :- returns last child node of an element (it can be text or comment node)
lastElementChild :- returns last child element node of an element 
previousSibling :- Returns previous node of same level (it can be text or comment node)
previousElementSibling :- returns previous element node of same level 
nextSibling :- returns next node of same level (it can be text or comment node)
nextElementSibling :- Return next element of same level  


parentNode and parentElement in javascript

the parentNode (read-only property) returns the parent of the specified node in the DOM tree.

the parentElement property returns the parent element of the specified element. 
- If the parent node is not an element node, it returns null. 

both returns parent, only difference is .... 

---> If the parent node is not an element node, parentElement returns null.
                                                                                        
---> Though the parent node is not an element node, parentNode returns parent of that node.

Ex :-

var elem = document.getElementById("h14");
console.log(elem.parentNode);
Output :- it returns body element // its parent node is body node 

console.log(elem.parentElement);
Output :- it also returns body element // its parent node is body node

Ex :- 

var elem = document.getElementById("elem");
console.log(elem);

console.log(elem.parentNode);
Output :- it returns #document because parent of html element is document

console.log(elem.parentElement);
Output :- it will return null because parent of html is document and it is not an element


childNodes and children in javascript

 childNodes :-

- The childNodes (read-only property) returns a live Nodelist of child nodes of the given element.
- the first child node is assigned index 0. 
- childNodes includes all child nodes, including non-element nodes like text and comment nodes.

- whitespace inside element is considered as text, and text is considered as nodes. 
- any whitespace will create a #text node, from a single space to multiple spaces, returns, tabs, & so on. 
- we can use length property and loop through all child nodes. 

 children :-

The children (read-only property) returns collection of child elements of the given element.
- the first child is assigned index 0. 
- children includes only element node(no whitespace, text node, comment node).

Ex :- 

var elem = document.getElementById("add");
console.log(elem);

console.log(elem.childNodes);
Output :- it returns all child elements of element including whitespace, enter and all 
--> NodeList [text] 

console.log(elem.children);
Output :- it will return child element of element but no whitespace, enter, comment node, text etc..
---> HTMLCollection [] // empty collection because exclude text node

elem.children[0].textContent = "leanring javascript";

Ex :- 2 

var elem = document.getElementById("myid");

len = elem.children.length

console.log(elem.childNodes);
Output :- it returns all child elements of element including (whitespace, enter and all are text nodes)  
--> NodeList(17) [text, link, text, meta, text, meta, text, meta, text, meta, text, comment, text, meta,
                  text, title, text] 
                  // whitespace, enter and all are considered as text nodes

console.log(elem.childNodes.length);
Output :- 17

for(let i=0; i< len; i++){
    console.log(elem.childNodes[i]);
}

console.log(elem.children);
Output :- it will return child element of element but no whitespace, enter, comment node, text etc..
---> HTMLCollection(7) [link, meta, meta, meta, meta, meta, title]
// it doesn't include text, comment or whitespace

console.log(elem.children.length);
Output :- 7 

len = elem.children.length

for(let i=0; i< len; i++){
    console.log(elem.children[i].textContent); //for accessing text content of element
}


firstChild and firstElementChild in javascript

 firstChild :
- the firstChild returns the node's first child in the tree or null if node has no children. 
- if the node is document, it returns the first node in the list of its direct children. 
- It includes text node and comment node. 
- whitespace inside is considered as text and text is considered as node. 
- any whitespace will create a #text node, from a single space to multiple spaces, returns, tabs, & so on. 

 firstElementChild :
- it returns the element's first child element node in the tree or null if node has no children element.
- it ignores text node and comment node or any whitespaces. 

Ex :- 

var elem = document.getElementById("myid");

console.log(elem.firstChild);
Output :- it returns first child of an element including (whitespace, enter and all are text nodes)  
--> #text

console.log(elem.firstElementChild);
Output :- it will return child element of element but no whitespace, enter, comment node, text etc..
--> < link rel="stylesheet" type="text/css" href="basic.css" > 

// it doesn't include text, comment or whitespace

elem.firstChild.textContent = "here is first child of element";


lastChild and lastElementChild in javascript

 lastChild :
- it returns last child of node or null if there is no node. 
- whitespace inside is considered as text and text is considered as node. 
- any whitespace will create a #text node, from a single space to multiple spaces, returns, tabs, & so on. 

 lastElementChild 
- it returns element's last child element node or null if node has no children. 
- it ignores text node, comment node or any whitespace. 


var elem = document.getElementById("myid");

console.log(elem.lastChild);
Output :- it returns first child of an element including (whitespace, enter and all are text nodes)  
--> #text

elem.lastChild.textContent = "I am last child";

console.log(elem.lastElementChild);
Output :- it will return child element of element but no whitespace, enter, comment node, text etc..
---> < title>Learn HTML


previousSibling and previousElementSibling in javascript

 previousSibling 

- it returns the node preceding the specified one in it's parent's child node list or null if
specified node is first in list. 
- it includes text node and comment node or any whitespace. 

 previousElementSibling 

- it returns the node preceding the specified one in it's parent's child node list or null if
specified node is first in list. 
- it ignores text node, comment node or any whitespace. 

var elem = document.getElementById("myid");

console.log(elem.lastChild.previousSibling);
Output :- it returns previousSibling of last child. it includes whitespace, text, comment and all   
---> < title>Learn HTML

elem.lastChild.previousSibling.textContent = "I am last child";

console.log(elem.lastChild.previousElementSibling);
Output :- it will return previousSibling of last child element but no whitespace, enter, comment node, text etc..
---> < title>Learn HTML


nextSibling and nextElementSibling in javascript

 nextSibling :
- it returns node next to specified one in its parent's childNode list or null if specified one is the 
last node in list. 
- it includes text node and comment node or any whitespace. 

 nextElementSibling 
- it returns node next to specified one in its parent's childNode list or null if specified one is the 
last node in list. 
- it ignores text node and comment node or any whitespace. 

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById("myid");

console.log(elem.firstChild.nextSibling); 
Output :-< link rel="stylesheet" type="text/css" href="basic.css">
//firstchild is space and nextSibling is link

console.log(elem.firstChild.nextElementSibling); 
Output :-< link rel="stylesheet" type="text/css" href="basic.css">
//firstchild is space and nextElementSibling is link

console.log(elem.firstElementChild.nextElementSibling);
Output :-< meta charset="UTF-8"> 
//firstElementchild is link and nextElementSibling is meta 

elem.firstChild.nextElementSibling.textContent = "we are assigning to nextsibling";

What is Document Fragment in Javascript

 - the DocumentFragment interface represents a minimal document object that has no parent. 
 - a common use of DocumentFragment is to create one, assemble a DOM subtree within it, then append 
 or insert the fragment into the DOM using Node interface methods such as appendchild() or insertBefore. 
 - DocumentFragment isn't part of the active document tree structure, changes made to the fragment 
 don't affect the document. 
 - Doing this, moves the fragment's node into the DOM, leaving behind an empty document Fragment. 
 - An empty document fragment can be created using the document.createDocumentFragment() Method. 

 Create Document Fragment

 - the createDocumentFragment() method creates an imaginary Node object, with all the properties and 
 method of the Node object. 

 var df = document.createDocumentFragment(); // creates empty DocumentFragment
 console.log(df);
 Output :- #document-fragment 

 How to Append Element Node in javascript

 - The appendChild(Child_Node) method is used to add a node to the end of the list of children of 
 specified parent node. 
 - If the given child is a referance to an existing node in the document, appendChild() moves it from 
 its current position to the new position. this method returns the new child node. 

 syntax :- appendChild(Child_Node)
 Parent_Node.appendChild(Child_Node);
  
 mysec.appendChild(child);
 It will append child to mysec. child will be last child of mysec. 

Ex :- 

var parent = document.getElementById("myid");
var child = document.getElementById("add");
console.log(parent);
console.log(child);
parent.appendChild(child);
console.log(parent);

// creating a new element node and appending node. 

var nenode = document.createElement("h3");
var parent = document.getElementById("add");
parent.appendChild(nenode);
console.log(parent)

or

var parent = document.getElementById("add");
parent.appendChild(document.createElement("h3"));
console.log(parent)

Append Text Node in javascript

var parent = document.getElementById("add");
// creating new text node 
var txtNode = document.createTextNode(" / add your future activity to list");
parent.appendChild(txtNode);
console.log(parent);

Append Comment Node in Javascript

var parent = document.getElementById("add");
// creating a comment node 
var commentNode = document.createComment(" adding to do iteams in list");
parent.appendChild(commentNode);
console.log(parent);

Append Element node, Comment node and text node together

// creating new element h2 
var nENode = document.createElement("h2");

//creating text node 
var txtNode = document.createTextNode("here is text node created");

//creating comment node 
var cmtNode = document.createComment("the coment text for element");

// Append text node to element node 
nENode.appendChild(txtNode);
console.log(nENode);

// Append element to an existing element
var parent = document.getElementById("add");
parent.appendChild(nENode);
parent.appendChild(cmtNode);
console.log(parent);

Example of DocumentFragment in javascript

// create empty DocumentFragment and create any two element then add text to those element then append 
those element to DocumentFragment and append DocumentFragment to any element of document 

var df = document.createDocumentFragment(); // create empty DocumentFragment

var elem1 = document.createElement("h3");  // creating h3 element
var elem2 = document.createElement("p");   // creating p element

elem1.textContent = "here is h3 element";  // adding text content to element 
elem2.textContent = "here is p element";   // adding text content to element 

df.appendChild(elem1);  // adding elements to DocumentFragment
df.appendChild(elem2);  // adding elements to DocumentFragment

var parent = document.getElementById("add");

parent.appendChild(df);  // moving DocumentFragment elements to element of document
console.log(parent); // elemnts will be added from document fragment to parent element 

console.log(df);
Output :- #document-fragment //empty document fragment


normalize() method in javascript

this method removes empty text nodes, and joins adjcent text nodes so there will be no adjcent text nodes.

Syntax :- normalize()

var elem = document.getElementById("add");
elem.normalize()

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById("add"); // accessing element

elem.appendChild(document.createTextNode(" hello "));  // adding text node to parent elem
elem.appendChild(document.createTextNode(" I want to"));   //adding text node to parent elem
elem.appendChild(document.createTextNode(" learn JAVASCRIPT "));  //adding text node to parent elem

console.log(elem.childNodes);

elem.normalize(); // it merges all adjcent text nodes, removes empty text nodes
console.log(elem.childNodes);  //it returns all child nodes including whitespace, text & comment nodes 


insertBefore() Method in javascript

- The insertBefore() method is used to insert a node before the reference node as a child of a specified 
parent node. 
- If the given child is reference to an exising node in the document, insertBefore() moves it from 
its current position to the new position. 
- If referenceNode is null, the newNode is inserted at the end of the list of child nodes. 

syntax :- 

var insertedNode = parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, referenceNode);

insertedNode = the node being inserted, that is new node. 
parentNode = the parent of the newly inserted node. 
newNode = the node to be inserted. 
referenceNode = the node before which new node is inserted.

Ex:- 

 inserting new created element before referance eleme

parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");   // accessing element  
refNode = document.getElementById("myli"); // accessing element 

newNode = document.createElement("li"); // creating an element
newNode.textContent = "for loop"; 

parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, refNode); // inserting new element(newNode) before referance element(refNode)
console.log(parentNode);

 inserting existing element before referance element

parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");   // accessing element  
refNode = document.getElementById("myli"); // accessing element 

newNode = document.getElementById("el"); // Existing element

parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, refNode); // inserting Existing element(newNode) before referance element(refNode)
console.log(parentNode);

 inserting element without referance element(null), it will insert element at last position

parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");   // accessing element  

newNode = document.getElementById("el"); // Existing element

parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, null); // inserting Existing element(newNode) at last 
console.log(parentNode);

 inserting text node before referance element

parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");   // accessing element  
refNode = document.getElementById("myli"); // accessing element 

newNode = document.createTextNode("For loop"); // new text nodeValue

parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, refNode); // inserting new text node before reference node  
console.log(parentNode);

insertAdjacentElement() Method

- The insertAdjacentElement() method inserts the specified element into a given specified position. 
- It returns the element that wes inserted or null if insertion failed. 

Syntax :- 

targetElement.insertAdjacentElement("position", element); 
where positions are :- 
    beforebegin :- before the element itself. 
    afterbegin :- just inside the element, before its first child 
    beforeend :- just inside the element, after its last child 
    afterend :- after the element itself. 
element :- the element to be inserted into tree. 
the beforebegin and afterend position work only if the node is in a tree and has an element parent. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");   
var newElem = document.createElement("span");
newElem.textContent = "this is text";
var tarElem = document.getElementById("myli");

tarElem.insertAdjacentElement("beforebegin", newElem); // beforebegin----> < h1> < br> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentElement("afterbegin", newElem);  // < h1> <---- afterbegin < br>< /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentElement("afterbegin", newElem); // < h1> < br> beforeend----> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

// tarElem.insertAdjacentElement("afterend", newElem); // < h1> < br>< /h1> <--- afterend
console.log(elem); 

insertAdjacentHTML() Method 

- this method is used to insert text as HTML (parse the specified text as HTML or XML)

Syntax :- 
element.insertAdjacentHTML("position", text);
where positions are :- 
    beforebegin :- before the element itself. 
    afterbegin :- just inside the element, before its first child 
    beforeend :- just inside the element, after its last child 
    afterend :- after the element itself.

text :- The string to be parsed as HTML or XML and inserted into tree. 

- It is recommended you not use insertAdjacentHTML when inserting plain text instead, 
use the node.textContent property. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");   
var newElem = "< span>Hello < /span>""

var tarElem = document.getElementById("myli");

tarElem.insertAdjacentHTML("beforebegin", newElem); // beforebegin----> < h1> < br> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentHTML("afterbegin", newElem);  // < h1> <---- afterbegin < br>< /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentHTML("afterbegin", newElem); // < h1> < br> beforeend----> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

// tarElem.insertAdjacentHTML("afterend", newElem); // < h1> < br>< /h1> <--- afterend
console.log(elem); 

insertAdjacentText Method in javascript

The insertAdjacentText() method inserts the specified element into a specified position. 

Syntax :- 
targetElement.insertAdjacentText("position", text);
where positions are :- 
    beforebegin :- before the element itself. 
    afterbegin :- just inside the element, before its first child 
    beforeend :- just inside the element, after its last child 
    afterend :- after the element itself.

text - the text which is about to insert. 
The beforebegin and afterend positions work only if the node is in tree and has an element parent. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");   

var tarElem = document.getElementById("myli");
var txt = " Hello ";

tarElem.insertAdjacentText("beforebegin",txt); // beforebegin----> < h1> < br> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentText("afterbegin",txt);  // < h1> <---- afterbegin < br>< /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentText("beforeend",txt); // < h1> < br> beforeend----> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentText("afterend",txt ); // < h1> < br>< /h1> <--- afterend
console.log(elem); 

innerHTML in javascript

- The Element property innerHTML gets or sets the HTML or XML markup contained within the element. 

Syntax :- 
var content = element.innerHTML;
element.innerHTML = htmlstring;

document.getElementById("add").innerHTML = htmlString;

outerHTML in javascript

- The outerHTML is the HTML of an element including the element itself.
- Use the outerHTML to completely replace an element and its content. 
- Use innerHTML to replace the content of an element. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");
var elem1 = element.outerHTML;
elem.outerHTML = " ";

innerText in javascript

- It works same as innerHTML property, except it focus on textual content within an element. 
- it sets and returns the text content of specified node. 
- If we set innerText property, any child nodes are removed and replaced by single text node. 

outerText :- outerText property works same as outerHTML property, modifies the element itself, and replace 
it with a single text node. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");
var elem1 = element.innerText;
elem.innerText = " ";

write and writeln in javascript

document.write() :- this is used to write arbitary HTML and content into page. 
- If we use this function after HTML document is fully loaded, will delete all existing HTML. 
- It is used for testing purpose. 

Ex :- 
document.write("hello world"); 

document.writeln() :- this is same as document.write() method writing a newline character 
after each statment. 

Ex :- 
document.writeln("hello world");

copy Node in javascript

- The cloneNode(deep) method is used to copy the node. 
- It creates copy of node including their all attribute, values and return the clone. 
- It takes a single boolean argument, indicates wheather copy should include all children or just element. 
- The duplicate node returned by cloneNode is not part of document untill it is added to node 
    which is part of document. 

Syntax :- 

cloneNode(false) -- will copy only element, attribute and their value
cloneNode(true) -- will copy entire element with child as well. 

var duplicateNode = targetNode.cloneNode(false);

Ex :- 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");

var duplicateNode = elem.cloneNode(true);
console.log(duplicateNode);
Output :- it returns all element including child

var duplicateNode = elem.cloneNode(false);
console.log(duplicateNode); 
Output :- it only returns element

Remove Node in javascript

- removeChild(child_name) Method is used to delete node from tree. 
- the removed child node still exist in memory but no longer part of the DOM. 
- It returns node object that was removed on success and null on failure. 

Syntax :- parentNode.removeChild(target_node);
var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(target_node)

Ex:- 

var parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");
var targetNode = document.getElementById("myli");

var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(targetNode);
console.log(delNode);
console.log(parentNode);

// removing element of which we have not id 

var parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");
var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(parentNode.firstElementChild);
var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(parentNode.firstElementChild.nextElementSibling);
var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(parentNode.childNodes[1]);

// removing element without parent element 

var childElemNode = document.getElementById("myli");
var delNode = childElemNode.parentNode.removeChild(childElemNode);

console.log(parentNode);

How to Replace Node in JAVASCRIPT

- the replaceChild(newChild, oldChild) method is used to replace a node with new node or existing node. 
- It will destroy the content of nodes that are replced. 
- It returns the replaced node (oldChild). 

syntax :- 

var replacedNode = parentNode.replaceChild(newChild, oldChild); 

- newChild is the new node to replace oldChild. If it already exists in the DOM, it is first removed. 
- oldChild existing child to be replaced. 

replacing element with new element

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");
var newChild = document.createElement("li");
newChild.textContent = "while loop is infinite when true";
oldChild = document.getElementById("myli");

var replacedNode = elem.replaceChild(newChild, oldChild);
console.log(replacedNode);

replacing element with existing element

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");
oldChild = document.getElementById("myli");
var existChild = oldChild.firstElementChild;

var replacedNode = elem.replaceChild(existChild, oldChild);
console.log(replacedNode);

Split Text in javascript

- The splitText(start) method breaks the text node into two nodes at the specified start index, keeping 
both nodes in the tree as sibling. 
- It returns right side of the split in new text node and leaves left side in the original node. 

var rightSide = TextNode.splitText(start);

var rightSide = TextNode.splitText(3) // 3 is index where text will be split.

Ex:- 

var elem = document.getElementById("add");
var rightSide = elem.firstChild.splitText(3); // spilt text will be in right side node
console.log(rightSide);  
Output :- to list

HTML DOM mapping in javascript

- Many object properties are simply direct mapping to the attribute of the HTML element.
- There is a mapping directly between HTML and DOM.

Ex :- 
< p id="myid" title="hello"Paragraph>< /p>

Above title can be accessed in DOM by 
document.getElementById("myid").title;

p tag's title attribute is mapped to DOM property title in the above example that is the reason we can 
access title in DOM that way. 

HTML - DOM mapping

The mapping is direct between HTML Attribute and DOM properties with the following considerations. 

- The mapping is direct if the attribute is single non - reserved word. that's why we can access 
title attribute of element via DOM object's property. 
- the mapping will change case if the attribute has two word. 
    - tabindex attribute will be represented as tabIndex in the DOM. 
- If the HTML attribute is reserved under javascript, the value will be modified to work. 
    - Ex :- class attribute will be represented as className in DOM
            for attribute will be represented as htmlFor in DOM 
- There are also some exception
    - char attribute will be represented as ch in DOM
- For others and custom attribute we have to use setAttribute and getAttribute method because they may 
not have direct mapping. 

CSS DOM mapping in javascript

- We can modify the CSS property by applying  a mapping between the CSS property and the DOM object. 
The mapping is direct between CSS property and the DOM properties with following consideration. 

- If CSS property is  of single word their mapping is direct. 
    Ex :- color in CSS will be represented as color in DOM too. 
- Hyphenated CSS properties are represented as a single word with camelCase in the DOM. 
    - Ex:- background-color in CSS is backgroundColor in DOM
- CSS properties value with vendor prefix. 
    - -webkit-box-shadow in CSS is webkitBoxShadow in DOM.  
- There are some reserved words which can be exception in the above cases. 
 - Ex :- float in CSS will be represented  as cssFloat in DOM. 

CSS Style Declaration object style property in javascript

CSS Style Declaration object Inline style manipulation property in javascript

- It(CSSStyleDeclaration) represents a collection of CSS property value pair. 
    - It is used in API :- 
        - HTMLElement.style 
        - window.getComputedStyle()
    
- when we write any element.style(p.style) it returns CSSStyle Declaration object. 

 properties              Methods
 - cssText               - getPropertyValue(property)
 - length                - getPropertyPriority(property)
 - parentRule            - removeProperty(property)
                         - setProperty(property, value, priority)
                         - item(index)

Inline style Manipultion

- to modify CSS value within javascript through style property, we have to access style object of elemenet.

style property 

- the style property is used to get or set the inline style of an element, while getting, it returns a 
CSSStyleDeclaration object that contains a list of all style properties with value assigned for the 
attribute defined in element's inline style attribute. 
- style attribute represents only CSS declaration in the element's inline style element. 
set :-- 
element.style.property = "value";

- Style declaration is reset by setting it to null or an empty string. 
Ex :- element.style.property = null;

var elem = document.getElementById('add');
elem.style.fontSize = "90px";
elem.style.backgroundColor = "yellow"; 

Dynamic style Manipulation className

- we might manipulate style rules using CSS class selector. 
- The element's class atrribute is represented as className property in DOM. 

Properties              Methods 
- length                - item()
- value                 - add()
                        - remove()
                        - replace()
                        - contains()
                        - toggle()
                        - value()
                    
classList Property

The Element.classList is a read-only property which returns a live DOMTokenList collection of the class 
attributes of the element. 

Syntax :-
var elementClasses = elementNodeReference.classList;

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById('add');
var elementClass = elem.classList;
console.log(elementClass); // it returns DOMTokenList which has element's class collection 
Output :- DOMTokenList ["mycl1", value: "mycl1"]

console.log(elementClass[0]);
Output :- mycl1

console.log(elementClass.length);
Output :- 1

console.log(elementClass.value);
Output :- mycl1

console.log(elementClass.item(0));
Output :- mycl1

elementClass.add("myclass");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList(2) ["mycl1", "myclass", value: "mycl1 myclass"]

elementClass.add("myclass2","myclass1");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList(3) ["mycl1", "myclass2", "myclass1", value: "mycl1 myclass2 myclass1"]

elementClass.remove("myclass1");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList(3) ["mycl1", "myclass2", value: "mycl1 myclass2"]

elementClass.remove("myclass2","myclass1");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList ["mycl1", value: "mycl1"]

elementClass.replace("myclass2","myclass1");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList(2) ["mycl1", "myclass1", value: "mycl1 myclass1"]

console.log(elementClass.contains("myclass2"));
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- false

elementClass.toggle("myclass2");
console.log(elementClass); // adding myclass2
Output :- DOMTokenList(3) ["mycl1", "myclass1", "myclass2", value: "mycl1 myclass1 myclass2"]

// toggle adds and removes class from element 

elementClass.toggle("myclass2");
console.log(elementClass); // removing myclass2
Output :- DOMTokenList(2) ["mycl1", "myclass1", value: "mycl1 myclass1"]


CSSStyle Declaration object Properties and methods in javascript

CSSStyle Declaration object represents a collection of CSS property-value pairs. 

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById('add');
var cs = elem.style;
console.log(cs.cssText); 
Output :- 

cs.cssText = "font-size: 70px;"; // setting CSS property of element, it will override all old property 

console.log(cs.length);
console.log(cs.item(0));
console.log(cs[0]);
console.log(cs.getPropertyValue('color'));

cs.removeProperty('color');
console.log(elem);

cs.setProperty('font-size', '90px', 'important');
console.log(elem)

var priority = cs.getPropertyPriority('font-size');
console.log(priority)


Computed Style and getComputedStyle method in javascript

- computed style used to display the element after styling from multiple sources have been applied. 
- style sources can be internal style sheets, External stylesheet inherited styles and browser default. 
- To get the values of all CSS properties for an element you should use window.getComputedStyle(). 
- It returns CSSStyleDeclaration object (collection of CSS property-value pair) which updates 
automatically  when element's style is changed. 

Syntax :- 
window.getComputedStyle(element, pseudoElement)
where 
    element = element for which to get the computed style. 
    pseudoElement = a string specifying pseudo element to match. must be ommited or null for regular 
    elements. 

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById('add');
var allCSSProp = window.getComputedStyle(elem);
console.log(allCSSProp);
console.log(allCSSProp.fontStyle);
console.log(allCSSProp.fontSize);
console.log(allCSSProp[0]);


HTMLTableElement

- It provides special properties for manipulatiing the layout and presentation of tables in an HTML 
element. 

Properties          Methods 
- caption           - createCaption()
- tHead             - deleteCaption()
- tFoot             - createTHead()
- rows              - deleteTHead()
- tBodies           - createTFoot()
                    - deleteTFoot()
                    - insertRow()
                    - deleteRow()

Properties :- 

caption :- this property represents the table caption. If no caption in table, it will return null. 

tHead - this property represent table's < thead> element. It's value is null if there is no such element. 

tFoot - this property represents the table's < tFoot> element. If not present it will return null. 

rows :- this property returns live HTML collection of all rows in table.
        though the property is read-only, returned object allows modification of content. 

tBodies :- this property returns HTMLCollection of table bodies. 
            though the property is read-only, returned object allows modification of content. 

< table id="mytab" border="1">
    < caption>My table Caption < /caption>
    < thead>
            < tr>
                < th>Id< /th>
                < th>Name < /th>
                < th>Courses< /th>
            < /tr>
    < /thead>
    < tbody>
            < tr id="mybody">
                < td>11< /td>
                < td>Rahul < /td>
                < td>Javascript < /td>
            < /tr>
            < tr>
                < td>12< /td>
                < td>Rajul < /td>
                < td>PHP < /td>
            < /tr>
    < /tbody>
    < tfoot>
            < tr>
                < td>55< /td>
                < td>Rahan < /td>
                < td>JSP < /td>
            < /tr>
    < /tfoot>

< /table> 

var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");

// caption property 
var tcap = table.caption;
tcap.innerHTML = Student Data;
console.log(tcap.innerHTML);

// thead property 
var thed = table1.tHead;
console.log(thed);
console.log(thed.innerHTML);
thed.innerHTML = "< tr> 
                    < th> NO < /th>  
                    < th> Student < /th>  
                    < th> course < /th> 
                < /tr> "

// tFoot property 
var tfut = table1.tFoot;
console.log(tfut);
console.log(tfut.innerHTML);
tfut.innerHTML =  "< tfoot>
                    < tr>
                        < td>55< /td>
                        < td>Rahan < /td>
                        < td>JSP < /td>
                    < /tr>
                  < /tfoot> " ;

HTML table element Methods :-  

createCaption() :-

- this method returns the caption for the table. If no caption element exists on table, this method  
creates it, then returns it. 

deleteCaption() :-

- this method removes the caption from the table. If there is no caption, this method does nothing 

Ex :- 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");

var tcap = table1.createCaption();
tcap.innerHTML = "new caption";
console.log(tcap); 
console.log(tcap.innerHTML);

table1.deleteCaption();

createTHead() :-  

- this method returns the < thead> element of table. If there is no such element in table, this method
 creates it then returns it. 

deleteTHead() :-  

- this method removes < thead> from table. 

Ex :- 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
var thed = table1.createTHead();
console.log(thed);  // it returns < thead> of table 

// if < thead> is not present it creates empty < thead>, we can assign it value

thed.innerHTML = "< thead>
                    < tr>
                        < th>Id< /th>
                        < th>Name < /th>
                        < th>Courses< /th>
                    < /tr>
                  < /thead>"
console.log(thed); 

// to delete < thead> from table. 

var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
table1.deleteTHead();

createTFoot() :- 

- this method returns the < tFoot> element of table, If there is no footer for table, this creates it, 
then returns it. 

deleteTFoot() :- 

- this method removes < tFoot> element from the table. 

var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
var tfut = table1.createTFoot();
console.log(tfut); 

tfut.innerHTML = "< tfoot>
                    < tr>
                        < td>55< /td>
                        < td>Rahan < /td>
                        < td>JSP < /td>
                    < /tr>
                  < /tfoot> "; 

// to delete < tfoot> from table. 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
table1.deleteTFoot();

insertRow() :-  

- this method inserts a new row in the table and returns a reference to the new row. 

Syntax :- 
var row = HTMLTableElement.insertRow(index = -1)

    - index is the row index of new row. 
    - If index is -1 or equal to the number of rows, the row is appended as the last row. 
    - If index is greater than number of rows, an IndexSizeError exception will result. 
    - If index is ommited it defaults to -1. 
    - If a table has multiple tbody elements, by default, the new row is inserted into the last tbody. 

deleteRow() :- 

- this method removes a row from the table. 
- If number row to delete is greater or equal to the number of row available row, or if it is negative
    and not equal to special index -1(last row of table), the exception INDEX_SIZE_ERR is thrown. 

Ex :- 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
var row = table1.insertRow(-1); // it inserts row at last position
var row = table1.insertRow(1); // it inserts row at first position
row.insertCell(0).textContent = "New Data";
console.log(row);

// To delete row 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
table1.deleteRow(0);
console.log(table1);

HTML Table Section Element in javascript

var tbody = document.getElementById("mybody");
var ro = tbody.rows;
console.log(ro);
console.log(ro[0].innerHTML);
ro[1].innerHTML = " < td>55< /td> < td>Rahan < /td> < td>JSP < /td>"

var row = tbody.insertRow(-1);
row.insertCell().textContent = "New";

tbody.deleteRow(1);

 HTML Table Row Element in javascript

- It provides special properties and methods for manipulating the layout of rows in HTML Table. 

Properties :- 
- cells
- rowIndex
- sectionRowIndex

Methods :- 
- insertCell()
- deleteCell()

cells :- 

- It returns HTMLCollection containing the cells in the row. 
- HTMLCollection is automatically updated when cells are added or removed. 

rowIndex :- 

- It returns a long value whichgives the logical position of the row within entire table. 
- If the row is not part of table, returns -1. 

sectionRowIndex :- 

- It returns the long value which gives the logical position of the row within table section it belongs to.
- If the row is not part of section, returns -1. 

Methods :- 

insertCell() :-  

- this method inserts a new cell into a table row and returns a reference to the cell. 

Syntax :- 
var cell = HTMLTableRowElement.insertCell(index = -);

- index is the cell index of new cell. 
- If index is -1 equal to number of cells, the cell is appended as the last cell in row. 
- If index is greater than number of cells, an IndexSizeError exception will result. 

deleteCell() :- 

- It removes the cell at the given position in the row. 
- If given position is greater than amount of cells in row, or smaller than 0, it raises DOMException 
with IndexSizeError.

Ex :- 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
var myrow = table1.rows;
console.log(myrow[0].cells.length); // returns number of cells present in 0th row
console.log(myrow[0].cells[0]);
console.log(myrow[2].cells[0]);
console.log(myrow[2].cells.item(0));
console.log(myrow[1].cells.namedItem("mycell")); // It returns cell of 1st row given Id="mycell"
console.log(myrow[2].cells[1].innerHTML);
myrow[2].cells[1].innerHTML = "Rehan";

var mycell = myrow[2].insertCell(2); // it will insert an empty cell in 2nd row at 2nd position
mycell.innerHTML = "new cell";

// to delete cell from row 
myrow[1].deleteCell(2); // it will delete 2nd cell of first row

textContent :- 
- This property sets or returns the text content of specified node. 
- setting this property on node removes all children and replaces them with single text node with the 
given value. 
- to grab all text we can use document.element.textContent. 
- textContent returns null if the node is document, DOCTYPE or notation. 

Syntax :- 
node.textContent
node.textContent = text 

var p = document.getElementById("h11");
console.log(p.textContent);
p.textContent = "Hello world";

Difference between textContent and innerHTML

when we want to use only text, we can use textContent but when we want to use HTML also at that time 
we should use innerHTML.

Ex :- 

var p = document.getElementById("h11");
p.textContent = "< em>here we are< /em>"; // em will be same and not applied to text 
p.innerHTML = "< em>here we are< /em>"; // the content will be changed to em
