// CSS Selector DOM

// Element Selector 
var list = document.querySelectorAll("p");
console.log(list);

// Group selector 
var list = document.querySelectorAll('div, p');
console.log(list);

//Universal Selector 
var listbook= document.querySelectorAll('*');
console.log(list); 

// Class Selector 
    // Universal style class
    var list = document.querySelectorAll('.game'); // element which has class name 'game' is returned 
    console.log(list); 

    // Element specific style class 
    var list = document.querySelectorAll('p.red');
    console.log(list);
    Output :- it will return collection of all p element which has class = 'red'  

    var list = document.querySelectorAll('p.red.black');
    console.log(list);
    Output :- it will return collection of all p element which has both class = 'red black' 

// ID Selector 
var list = document.querySelectorAll('#book');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return collection of element which has id='book'

var list = document.querySelectorAll('p#book');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return p element which has id='book'

// Attribute Selector 
var list = document.querySelectorAll('p[title]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return all p element which has title attribute 

var list = document.querySelectorAll('p[title = "mypara1"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return all p element which has title = "mypara1" 

var list = document.querySelectorAll('img[width = "30%"][height = "20%"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return img element which has width = 30% and height = 20%

var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class ~= "game"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and value of class attribute is "game"

var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class |= "game"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and it's value should start with word "game"
         the word should either "game" or seperated by hyphen "game-super" but not like "gamesuper" or
         "game super"

var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class ^= "game"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and it's value start with "game"
            it will return any element start with game .... "gamesuper", "game super", "game-super" etc..
         
var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class $= "game"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and it's value ends with "game"
            ex. "game","supergame","super-game" etc. 

var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class *= "ga"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and it's value has "ga" word anywhere 

// pseudo Class
    //first-child
    var list = document.querySelectorAll('li:first-child');
    console.log(list);
    Output :- it will return first child of li element 
                         
// In this case second function (disp2) will be executed, it will override disp1 
// when two events are called on same element the newest will override the oldest one. 


addEventListener in javascript

- This method is used to engage an event handler in a page. 

Syntax :-  
Object.addEventListener(event, handler, capturePhase); 
 
where, 
- object is the node to which the listener is to bound. 
- Event is a string indicating the type of event. 
- Handler is the function that should be called when the event occurs. 
- capturePhase is a boolean indicating wheather to use bubbling(false) or capture(true). this is optional.
If you omit there is false bydefault. 

Ex :- 
btn.addEventListener("click", show, false);

Why should we use addEventListener ?
- It allows you to bind multiple handler to an object for same event. 
- It enables you finer-grained control of the phase when the listener is activated( Capture or Bubbling) 
- It works on any DOM element, not just HTML. 

Ex :- 

function show(){
    alert('Button clicked');
}
var btn = document.getElementById('add');
btn.addEventListener('click', show);
btn.addEventListener('mouseover', show);

// It allows you to bind multiple handler to an object for same event. 

function disp1(){
    alert('Button clicked 1');
}
function disp2(){
    alert('Button clicked 2');
}

var btn = document.getElementById('add');
btn.addEventListener('click', disp1);
btn.addEventListener('click', disp2);


removeEventListener()


- This method is used to remove handlers, with the same arguments give when event was added. 
Ex :- 

function show(){
    alert('Button clicked');
}
var btn = document.getElementById('add');
btn.addEventListener('click', show, false);
btn.addEventListener('click', show, true);

btn.removeEventListener('click', show, true);


DOM event flow or event propagation in javascript

- The DOM 2 Event Model specification describes a standard way to create, capture, handle and cancel event 
in a tree like structure such as an XHTML document's object hierarchy. 

Phases :- 
- Capture phase 
- Target phase 
- Bubbling Phase 

Ex :- 
< div id="one">1
    < div id="two">2
        < div id="three">3
            < div id="four">4
        
    


// parent of 4 is 3, parent of 3 is 2, parent of 2 is 1, parent of 1 can be anything like body, etc... 

- Bubbling Phase :- It propagtes from bottom to top. for example, if click event is given to all above 
< div> element and we click 4 then it will triger from 4 then if its parent has click event then it triger 
its parent 3, same way it will triger its parent 2 and then 1 and so on.. 

- Capture Phase :- It is opposite to bubbling phase, it propagates from top to bottom. 
- If we click on 4 then it will move to the top parent element which has click event, here 1 is parent 
with click event so it will triger 1 then it's child which has click event(here 2) then child of 2 is 3, then
child of 3 is 4.

- Target Phase :- 
- It will triger the targetted element not parent and not child. not from top to bottom And not from bottom
to top. 
If we click element 4 then it will triger element 4. 

Ex :- 

//Bubbling Phase 
document.getElementById('one').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('1');},false);
document.getElementById('two').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('2');},false);
document.getElementById('three').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('3');},false);
document.getElementById('four').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('4');},false);

// Capture Phase 
document.getElementById('one').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('1');},true);
document.getElementById('two').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('2');},true);
document.getElementById('three').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('3');},true);
document.getElementById('four').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('4');},true);


Event Object in javascript

- DOM events pass an event object as an argument to the event handlers. 
- This object contains extra information about the event that occured. 

Ex :- addEventListener('click', function(e){console.log(e)});

where, e is object passed by DOM events as argument which has information about the event that occured. 

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log(e);
    console.log(e.clientX); 
    console.log(e.clientY);
    console.log(e.type);
    console.log(e.target);
    console.log(e.currentTarget);
}); 

we can access many properties through e. 


What is difference between target and currentTarget ?

- Target is pn which we click while current target is according to propagation execution. 

Ex :- 
< div id="one" data-name="1">1
    < div id="two" data-name="2">2
        < div id="three" data-name="3">3
            < div id="four" data-name="4">4
        
    


// Bubbling Phase 
- when we click on 4 the target will remain same 4 but current target will propagate from bottom to top. 

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log('1'); // 1
    console.log('Target = ' + e.target.dataset.name); // Target :- 4
    console.log('current Target = ' + e.currentTarget.dataset.name); // current Target :- 1
}, false);

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log('2'); // 2
    console.log('Target = ' + e.target.dataset.name); // Target :- 4
    console.log('current Target = ' + e.currentTarget.dataset.name); // current Target :- 2
}, false);

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log('3'); // 3 
    console.log('Target = ' + e.target.dataset.name); // Target :- 4
    console.log('current Target = ' + e.currentTarget.dataset.name);  // current Target :- 3
}, false);

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log('4'); // 4
    console.log('Target = ' + e.target.dataset.name); // Target :- 4
    console.log('current Target = ' + e.currentTarget.dataset.name); // current Target :- 4
}, false);

Output :- when we click 4

4
target :- 4
current Target :- 4
3
target :- 4
current Target :- 3
2
target :- 4
current Target :- 2
1
target :- 4
current Target :- 1


Event Methods stopPropagation and stopImmediatePropagation in javascript

stopPropagation() :- Prevents further propagation of the current event in the capturing and bubbling phases. 
Syntax :- e.stopPropagation();

stopImmediatePropagation() :- Prevents other listener of the same event from being called.
Syntax :- e.stopImmediatePropagation();


1
    
2
        
3
        

    




Ex :- 
< div id="one" >1
    < div id="two" >2
        < div id="three" >3
        
    


function div1(e){
    this.style.backgroundColor = 'red';
};

function div2(e){
    this.style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
    e.stopPropagation(); // It will stop propagation and stop div1 from triggering
    e.stopImmediatePropagation(); // this method will stop all event handler even of same event
};

function div2_2(e){
    this.style.width = '250px'; // it should be stopped, but it is trigged because it is stopPropagation()
    // when stopImmediatePropagation() method is called this event will also be stopped. 
};

function div3(e){
    this.style.backgroundColor = 'green';
};

var div_1 = document.getElementById('one');
var div_2 = document.getElementById('two');
var div_3 = document.getElementById('three');

div_1.addEventListener('click', div1, false);
div_2.addEventListener('click', div2, false);
div_2.addEventListener('click', div2_2, false);
div_3.addEventListener('click', div3, false);

// div2 has two event listener 
// bubble up phase will triger event from bottom to top 

- when I click on 3rd element (div), firstly 3 then 2 and then 1 will change its color as per bubble phase. 
- but if we don't want to triger all element, instead only clicked element should be trigered. 
in such case we can add stopPropagation in 3rd element, it will stop propagate so only 3 element will be 
trigered. 
- Now we want 3rd and 2nd element to triger but the 2nd element has two event handlers but we want only One
to be trigged. now if we add stopPropagation() in 2nd element's one handler, even then it will triger both
handlers will not stop another handler because all listener of same event will be triggered and 
stopPropagation() method will not stop it.

- For stoping any event handler of same event we will use stopImmediatePropagation() method it will stop 
all other handlers of same event.  


How to prevent Element default behavior in javascript

preventDefault() :- The event interface's preventDefault() method tells user agent that if the event is not
explicitly handled, its default action should not be taken as it normally would be. 

Syntax :- e.preventDefault();

Ex :- 
< a href="http://www.google.com" id="mylink">Google site< /a>

// default behavior of anchor tag is, when we click link inside it, we will be redirected to that link. 
but if we want something else, we have to first stop default behavior using preventDefault

Ex :- 
< a href="http://www.google.com" id="mylink">Google site< /a>

function stopLink(e) {
    e.preventDefault();
}
var ln = document.getElementById('mylink');
ln.addEventListener('click', stopLink, false);

// It will stop default behavior of link, when we will click on link it will not be redirected and no 
action will be taken. 


Mouse Event in javascript

mousedown :- It fires when mouse button is pressed down. 

mouseup :- It fires when the mouse button is released.

click :- It fires when something is clicked.mousedown, mouseup and click events fires in sequence. 

dblclick :- It fires when something is clicked twice in repid succession. mousedown, mouseup, click, 
mousedown, mouseup, click, and dblclick events fires in sequence. 

mouseenter :- It fires when mouse starts to hover over some element. No bubble. 

mouseleave :- It fires when a mouse exits while while hovering over some element. No bubble. 

mouseover :- It fires when mouse is hovering over some element. 

mouseout :- It fires when mouse leaves from hovering over some element. 

mousemove :- It fires when the mouse moves. 

contextmenu :- It fires when mouse right button is clicked.     

Ex :- 

function div1(e){
    console.log(e.type);
}
function div2(e){
    console.log(e.type);
}
var div_1 = document.getElementById('one');
var div_2 = document.getElementById('two');

div_1.addEventListener('mousedown', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mouseup', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('click', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('dblclick', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mouseenter', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mouseleave', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mousemove', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('contextmenu', div1, false);

// bubble up // when we will click on one element there will be 2 click, mousedown and mouseup event 
beccause of bubble phase propagation 

div_2.addEventListener('click', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('click', div1, false);

div_2.addEventListener('mousedown', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mousedown', div1, false);

div_2.addEventListener('mouseup', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mouseup', div1, false);

div_2.addEventListener('contextmenu', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('contextmenu', div1, false);

div_2.addEventListener('mousemove', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mousemove', div1, false);

Ex :- 

Name 

var txt = document.getElementById('mytext');

function changeColorOrange(){
    txt.style.backgroundColor = 'orange';
}
function changeColorWhite(){
    txt.style.backgroundColor = 'white';
}

txt.addEventListener('mouseover', changeColorOrange, false);
txt.addEventListener('mouseout', changeColorWhite, false);


Focus Event in javascript

focus :- It fires when an element gains focus such as selecting form field. No bubble. 

blur :- It fires when an element loses focus, such as moving away from a form field. No bubble. 

focusin :- It fires just as an element is about to gain focus.

focusout :- It fires just as an element loses focus and just before the blur event. 

Name 

var txt = document.getElementById('mytxt1'); 

function focusEvent(e){
    txt.style.backgroundColor = 'orange';
}

function blurEvent(e){
    txt.style.backgroundColor = 'white';
}
txt.addEventListener('focus', focusEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('blur', blurEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('focusin', focusEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('focusout', blurEvent, false);


Key Events in javascript

keydown :- It fires as a key is pressed down. 

keypress :- It fires after a key is pressed down (after keydown). It only works with printable characters. 

keyup :- It fires as the key is released.

Name 

var txt = document.getElementById('mytxt2'); 

function keyEvent(e){
    console.log(e.type + ' ' + e.keyCode + ' ' + String.fromCharCode(e.keyCode));
}

txt.addEventListener('keydown', keyEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('keypress', keyEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('keyup', keyEvent, false);


Text Events in javascript

- It will whatever character is pressed. 

Name 

var txt = document.getElementById('mytxt'); 

function show(e){
    console.log(e.type + ' ' + e.data);
}

txt.addEventListener('textInput', show, false);


window object in javascript

- window object represents the browser's window or potentially frame, that a document is displayed in. 
- As long as a browser window is open, even if no document is loaded in window, the window object is 
defined in the current model in memory. 
- All global javascript variables, functions and objects automatically becomes member of the window object. 

console.dir(window);

var oh = window.outerHeight;
console.log(oh);

var ow = window.outerWidth;
console.log(ow);

var ih = window.innerHeight;
console.log(ih);

var iw = window.innerWidth;
console.log(iw);


Dialog boxes

- It is used to provide some information to user.
- Types of dialog boxes :- 
    - alert 
    - Confirm 
    - Prompt 

alert() Method

- This window object's method is used to display data in alert dialog box. 
- alert should be used only when you truly want to stop everything and let the user know something. 

syntax :- window.alert() or alert()
          
Ex :- window.alert('hello world');
      window.alert(variable);
      window.alert(4+2);
      window.alert('hello world'+ variable);

confirm() Method

- This method of window object is used to display a message for a user to respond by pressing ok button to
agree with the message or cancel button to disagree with the message. 
- It returns True on Ok and false on Cancel. 

Syntax :-  window.confirm() or confirm()

Ex :- window.confirm('are you sure ?');

if(confirm('Do you want to delete ?')){
    document.write('Data deleted');
}else {
    document.write('Action canceled');
}

var crm = confirm('are you sure?');
if (crm){
    console.log('data deleted');
}else{
    console.log('Action canceled');
}

prompt() Method

- window object's prompt() method can be used to get input from user. 
- It displays a dialog box that prompts the visitor for input.  
- Once the prompt function obtains input from user, it returns that input. 
- If the user press the cancel button or close the dialog, null will be returned. 

Syntax :- prompt(text, defaultText)
Ex :- prompt('Enter your name :- ', 'name');

var name = prompt('enter your name:- ')


open() and close() method in javascript

- The open() method creates a new secondary browser window. 
- It returns a window object representing newly created window.
- If the window couldn't be opened, it returns null. 

Syntax :- window.open(URL, name, features, replace)
URL :- URL indicates the document to load into the window. If no URL is specified, a new window with 
        about:blank is opened. 

Name :- specifies the target atrribute or the name of window. The following values are supported: 
_blank - URL is loaded into a new window. This is default. 
_parent - URL is loaded into the parent frame. 
_self - URL replaces the current page. 
_top - URL replaces any frameset that may be loaded.    

Features :- It is comma separated string that lists the features of the window. 

Replace - It indicates wheather or not the URL specified should replace the window's contents. 
this would apply to the window that was already created. Value can be true / false. 

Ex :- 
var newWindow = window.open('www.goole.com','_self','height=100, width=100')

var new = window.open();
console.log(new);



function createWindow(){
    window.open();
    window.open('https://www.google.com');
    window.open('https://www.google.com','_self');
    window.open('https://www.google.com','_blank');
    window.open('https://www.google.com','_blank','height=400,width=800');
    window.open('https://www.google.com','_blank','height=400,width=800,scrollbars=no');
    var newW = window.open('','_blank','height=400,width=800');
    newW.document.Write('Our new window');
}

b1 = document.getElementById('btn');
b1.addEventListener('click',createWindow, false);


close() Method

- Once the window is open, the close() method is used to close it.
- It closes the current window or the window on which it is called.
- This method is only allowed to called for windows opened by script using window.open() method. 
- It is often used together with open() method.

Syntax :- window.close()

Ex :- 


var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('https;//www.google.com','','height=400,width=600');
}
function clWindow(){
    newWindow.close();
}

bn1 = document.getElementById('mybn1');
bn2 = document.getElementById('mybn2');

bn1.addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
bn2.addEventListener('click', clWindow, false);


print() Method in javascript



function printDoc(){
    window.print();
}

var bn3 = document.getElementById('mybn3');
bn3.addEventListener('click', printDoc, false);


focus() and blur() Method

focus() :- when we work in current window, we are focusing on it.
blur() :- when we leave current window, it is blur. 





var newWindow;
function openWin(){
    newWindow = window.open('','_blank','width=600,height=400');
}
function focusWin(){
    newWindow.focus();
}
function blurWin(){
    newWindow.blur();
}
document.getElementById('openbtn').addEventListener('click', openWin, false);
document.getElementById('focusbtn').addEventListener('click', focusWin, false);
document.getElementById('blurbtn').addEventListener('click', blurWin, false);


Moving Window in javascript

moveBy() 

moveBy() - This method moves the current window by specified amount of pixels. 
Syntax :- window.moveBy(horizontalPixels, verticalPixels);
where, 
window :- It is name of the window to move or it is just window if it is main window. 
horizontalPixels :- It is the number of horizontalPixels to move the window where positive number move the 
window to right and negative number move the window to left. 
verticalPixels :- It is the number pixel to move the window where positive number move the window to bottom 
and negative number move the window to up. 

Ex :- newWindow.moveBy(200,200);





var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('','newWindow','height=3 00,width=400');
}

function mvWin(){
    newWindow.moveBy(200,200);
    newWindow.focus();
}

function mvlWin(){
    newWindow.moveBy(-200,-200);
    newWindow.focus();
}
document.getElementById('opn').addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
document.getElementById('mwr').addEventListener('click', mvWin, false);
document.getElementById('mwl').addEventListener('click', mvlWin, false);

moveTo() Method

moveTo() :- This method moves the window to specified coordinates. 
Syntax :- window.moveTo(x, y);
where,
window - It is the name of window to move or it is called just window. 
x - It is the screen co-ordinate on x - axis to move the window to. 
y - It is the screen co-ordinate on y - axis to move the window to. 
Ex :- newWindow.moveTo(200,200); 




var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('','newWindow','height=300,width=400');
}

function mvWin(){
    newWindow.moveBy(200,200);
    newWindow.focus();
}

document.getElementById('opbtn').addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
document.getElementById('mw').addEventListener('click', mvWin, false);


Resizing Window in javascript

resizeBy()
resizeBy() :- This method is used to resize the current window by a certain amount, relative to its 
current size. 

Syntax :- window.resizeBy(width, height);
where, 
window :- It is the name of window to move or is called window if it is main window.
width :- It is the number of width pixel, where positive number increase the windth and negative number 
decrease the width. 
height :- It is the number of height pixel, where positive number increase the windth and negative number 
decrease the width. 

Ex :- window.resizeBy(200, 200); 




var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('','_blank','height=300,width=400');
}

function rsizeWin(){
    newWindow.resizeBy(200,200);
    newWindow.focus();
}

document.getElementById('obtn').addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
document.getElementById('rsize').addEventListener('click', rsizeWin, false);

resizeTo()

resizeTo() :- this method is used to resize the window to specified width and height. 
syntax:- window.resizeTo(width, height);
window :- It is the name of window to move or is called window if it is main window.
width :- It is an integer representing the new outerWidth in pixels(including scroll bars, title bars). 
height :- It is an integer value representing the new outerHeight in pixel(including scroll bars, etc.) 

Ex :- newWindow.resizeTo(200, 200); 




var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('','_blank','height=300,width=400');
}

    newWindow.resizeTo(200,200);
    newWindow.focus();
}

document.getElementById('r1size').addEventListener('click', rsizeWin, false);


Scrolling window in javascript

scrollBy() Method
scrollBy() - This method scrolls the document in the window by the given amount. 
Syntax :- window.scrollBy(x, y); or window.scrollBy(options);
where,
window :- It is the name of the window to scroll or is called just window if it is main window.
x - How many pixels to scroll by, along the x-axis(horizontal), positive values will scroll to the right,
while negative values will be scroll to the left.
y - How many pixels to scroll by, along the y-axis (vertical). Positive values will be scroll down, while 
negative value will be scroll up. 
options :- It is an object with three properties:
            top, which is the same as the y-coord 
            left, which is the same as the x-coord 
            behavior, which is a string containing one of smooth, instant, or auto; default is auto. 
Ex :- window.scrollBy(0, -20);
      window.scrollBy({top:-20, behavior:'smooth'});
      Note :- for this method to work, the visible property of window's scroll bar must be set true. 






function scrollTWin(){
    // window.scrollBy(0, -20);
    // window.scrollBy({top: -20, behavior: 'smooth'});
    window.scrollBy({top: -20, behavior: 'instant'});
}

function scrollDWin(){
    window.scrollBy(0, 20);
}

function scrollLWin(){
    window.scrollBy(-20, 0);
}

function scrollRWin(){
    window.scrollBy(20, 0);
}

document.getElementById('myb1').addEventListener('click', scrollTWin);
document.getElementById('myb2').addEventListener('click', scrollDWin);
document.getElementById('myb3').addEventListener('click', scrollLWin);
document.getElementById('myb4').addEventListener('click', scrollRWin);

scrollTo() Method
scrollTo() :- This method scrolls to a paricular set of coordinates in the document. 
syntax :- window.scrollTo(x, y); or window.scrollTo(options);
where,
window - It is the name of window to scroll or is called just window if it is main window. 
x - It is the pixel along the horizontal axis of the document.
y - It is the pixel along the vertical axis of the document.

options :- It is an object with three properties:
            top, which is the same as the y-coord 
            left, which is the same as the x-coord 
            behavior, which is a string containing one of smooth, instant, or auto; default is auto. 

Ex :- window.scrollTo(0, 400);
window.scrollTo({top:400, behavior:'smooth'});






function scrollTWin(){
    window.scrollTo(0, 0);
    // window.scrollBy({top: 0, behavior: 'smooth'});
    // window.scrollBy({top: 0, behavior: 'instant'});
}

function scrollDWin(){
    window.scrollTo(0, 20);
}

function scrollLWin(){
    window.scrollTo(-20, 0);
}

function scrollRWin(){
    window.scrollTo(20, 0);
}

document.getElementById('mybtn1').addEventListener('click', scrollTWin);
document.getElementById('mybtn2').addEventListener('click', scrollDWin);
document.getElementById('mybtn3').addEventListener('click', scrollLWin);
document.getElementById('mybtn4').addEventListener('click', scrollRWin);


Location object in javascript

- This is used to access the location(URL) of window.
- The location object can be both read and replaced, so it is possible to update the location of a page
through scripting. 
- Location object is property of window. 
syntax :- 
window.location.property 
window.location.method

Properties

hash - The part of the URL including and following the # symbol.
host - The hostname and port number.
hostname - hostname 
href - entire URL 
pathname - Path relative to the host. 
port - Port number 
protocol - protocol of URL. 
search - The part of URL including and after the ?

console.dir(location);
console.log(window.location.hash);
console.log(window.location.hash);
console.log(window.location.port);
console.log(window.location.href);
console.log(window.location.search);
console.log(window.location.protocol);
console.log(window.location.pathname);
console.log(window.location.hostname);

window.location.hash = '#team';
window.location.href = 'www.google.com';

Methods 

- assign(URL) - It changes the location of current page with passed URL. 
- reload() - Reload the current page. 
- replace(URL) - Replace the current page with the given URL in history. 
  as it is replaced in history it won't be possible to access the current page with back/forward.   

  reload method :- 
  Ex :- 
window.location.reload() 

assign method 
Ex :- 
window.location.assign('https://www.google.com');

replace method 
Ex:- 
window.location.replace('https://www.google.com');


History object in javascript

- The history object is read-only property of URL string that show where the user has been recently. 
Syntax :- 
window.history.property
window.history.method

properties:- 
length - It returns the number of URLs in the history list. 

Methods :- 
back() - It loads the previous URL in the history list. 

forward() :- It loads the next URL in history list. 

go() :- It access a particular item in history list relative to current position.
Using a negative value moves to history item previous to the current location, while a positive number 
moves forward in the history list. 

console.log(window.history.length);

console.log(window.history.back());
console.log(window.history.forward());

console.log(window.history.go(-1)); // it will go 1 site back 
console.log(window.history.go(1)); // It will go 1 site forward 
console.log(window.history.go(2)); // it will go 2 site forward


setTimeout() and clearTimeout() method in javascript

- The setTimeout() sets the timer which executes function or piece of code once after the timer expires. 
- The function is only executed once. 
- It returns a positive integer value, this value can be passed to clearTimeout() to cancel timeout.

syntax:- setTimeout(function, millisecond, para1, para2);
Ex :- 
var timeoutId = setTimeout(show, 2000);


color will be changed after completion of set time duration


function changeColor(){
    document.getElementById('setT').style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
}

setTimeout(changeColor, 5000);

or 

setTimeout(() => {
    document.getElementById('setT').style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
    }, 5000);

or


setTimeout(function() {
    document.getElementById('setT').style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
    }, 5000);

clearTimeout() Method

- The clearTimeout() method cancels a timeout previously established by calling setTimeout() method. 
- The ID returned by setTimeout() method is used to pass as parameter for the clearTimeout() method. 
syntax :- 
clearTimeout(timeoutId);


Ex :- 

var timeoutID = setTimeout(() => {
    document.getElementById('setT').style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
    }, 5000);

function clrTime(){
    clearTimeout(timeoutID);
}

document.getElementById('bt1').addEventListener('click', clrTime);


setInterval() and clearInterval() Method

setInterval() :- 
- It repetedly calls a function or execute a code with a fixed time delay between each call. 
- It returns an intervalId which uniquely identifies interval so we can remove it by calling clearInterval(). 

Syntax :- setInterval(function, millisecond, para1, para2);

clearInterval() :- 
- This method cancels a timed, repeating action which was set by setInterval()
Syntax :- clearInterval(intervalID);


use of setInterval :- 



Ex :- 

intervalID = setInterval(function(){
    document.getElementById('setI').textContent += ' hello';
 }, 2000);

 function clrInt(){
     clearInterval(intervalID);
 }

document.getElementById('clI').addEventListener('click', clrInt);

Form handling in javascript

- javascript provide access to forms within an HTML document through the form object known as 
HTMLFormElement in the DOM. which is a child of the document object. 

Accessing Forms :- 
- javascript provides various way of accessing form:-
    - document.forms[index_number] -  It returns collection of form in the document. 
    - document.forms["name_attribute_value"] - we can use name attribute of the form.
    - document.name_attribute_value - we can use name attribute of form with dot as well. 
    - getElementById('ID') - If form has an unique id we can use it. 



    User Name: 
    Password : 
    






    User Name: 
    Password : 
    



Ex :- 
Accessing Form :- 
// with Index number

var form1 = document.forms[0];
var form2 = document.form[1];
console.log(form1); // It will returns form1
console.log(form2); // It will returns form2

// with name attribute using square bracket

var form1 = document.forms['form1'];
var form2 = document.forms['form2'];
console.log(form1); // It will returns form1
console.log(form2); // It will returns form2

// with name attribute using dot 

var form1 = document.form1;
var form2 = document.form2;
console.log(form1); // It will returns form1
console.log(form2); // It will returns form2

// getElementById method

var form1  = document.getElementById('fm1');
var form2  = document.getElementById('fm2');
console.log(form1);
console.log(form2);

Accessing form fields in JAVASCRIPT

- If form field has unique Id then we can access it using getElementById method. 
- elements[] - It contains collection of elements. 

Syntax :- document.form_name.elements[index_number];
document.form_name.elements['name_attribute_value'];
document.form_name.name_attribute_value;
document.form_name.ID_attribute_value;

- getElementsByName('field_name') - this method is also used to access form field. 

var usrname = document.getElementById('usr1');
console.log(usrname.type);
console.log(usrname.name);
console.log(usrname.id);

// with element [indexNumber]
var username = document.form1.elements[0];
console.log(username);
console.log(username.name);
console.log(username.type);

// with name attribute value 
var username = document.form1.elements['username1'];
console.log(username);
console.log(username.value);

// with name attribute
var username = document.form1.username1;

// with name attribute value
var username = document.form1.elements['username1'];

// with id attribute
var username = document.form1.usr1;

Form validation in javascript



    Username : 
    



function validateData(){
    var ptrn = /^([^0-9\W]*)$/;
    if(ptrn.test(document.myform.usr.value)){
        document.getElementById('u1').textContent = 'User is valid';
        document.getElementById('u1').style.color = 'green';
    }else{
        document.getElementById('u1').textContent = 'User is Invalid';
        document.getElementById('u1').style.color = 'red';
    }
}
document.myform.usr.addEventListener('keyup', validateData);


What are cookies and How it work? 

- A cookie is small piece of text data set by web server that reside on the client's machine. 
- once it's been set, the client automatically returns the cookie to the web server with each request 
that it makes. 
- this allows the server to place value in cookie, and have access to them when creating a response. 

Types of cookies :- 

- Session Cookies - cookies that are set without expires field are called session cookie. 
                  - It is destroyed when the use close browser. 
- Persistent Cookies - The browser keep it until their expiration date is reached. 


javascript cookies

- Cookies are exposed as the cookie property of document object. This property is both readable and writable. 
- We can see cookies in google chrome by following chrome://settings/content/cookies

How to set cookies into client system using javascript

- creating cookies :- when you assign a string to document.cookie, the browser parses it as a cookie and adds
it to its list of cookies.
- There are several parts to each cookies, many of them optional. 

Syntax :- 
document.cookie = 'name=value';
document.cookie = 'name=value; expires=date; domain=domain; path=path; secure';
document.cookie = 'name=value; max-age=inSecond; domain=domain; path=path; secure';

Ex :- 
document.cookie = 'username=geeky';
document.cookie = 'username=geeky; expires=Monday, 3-Sep-2018 09:00:00 UTC';
document.cookie = 'username=geeky; max-age=' + 60*60*24*10;

Note :- name-value pair must not contain any whitespace character, commas or semicolon.

optional cookies attribute :- 
max-age 
expires 
domain 
path 
secure 

whenever we omit optional attribute browser will fill it with default. 

Ex :- 
document.cookie = 'username=sarita';

How to set cookies max-age in javascript

- It is used to create Persistent cookie. It is supported by all browser except IE.
Ex :- 
document.cookie = 'username=geeky; max-age=' + 60*60*24*10;
document.cookie = 'username=geeky; max-age=' + 60*60*24*10 + ';path=/';

document.cookie = 'username=sarita; max-age=' + 60*60*24*10;

How to set expires date in javascript

- It is used to create persistent cookie. 

Ex :- 
document.cookie = 'username=sarita; expires=Monday, 3-Sep-2018 09:00:00 UTC';

How to set cookie domain, path and secure in javascript

domain :- It specifies the domain for which cookie is valid. If not specified, this defaults to the host 
portion of the current document location.
- If a domain is specified, subdomains are always included. 

Ex :- document.cookie = 'username=sarita; domain=code.geeky.com';

path :- path can be /(root) or /mydir(directory). If specified, defaults to the current path of the 
current document location, as well as its decendants.

Ex :- document.cookie = 'username=sarita;path=/';
Ex :- document.cookie = 'username=sarita;path=/home';

secure :- Cookie to only be transmitted over secure protocol as https. 

Ex :- document.cookie = 'username=sarita;secure';

How to Replace and Append cookie in javascript

- When we assign a new cookie value to document, the current cookie are not replaced. 
- The new cookie is parsed and its name-value pair is appended to list. 
- The exception is when you assign new cookie with same name and same domain and path if they exist) 
as a cookie  that already exists. In this case the old value is replaced with new.


Ex :- 
// Replace cookie 
document.cookie = 'username = sarita';
document.cookie = 'username = smruti';

// Append cookie 
document.cookie = 'username = sarita';
document.cookie = 'userId = sarita';

How to read cookies in javascript

- We can read cookie by document.cookie. 



    Name: 
    Email: 
    Language: 
    
    



function setCookie(){
    document.cookie = 'name=' + document.myfm.name.value;
    document.cookie = 'email=' + document.myfm.email.value;
    document.cookie = 'language=' + document.myfm.lang.value;
}

// name=rahul; email=rahul@gmail.com; language=hindi

function getCookie(){
    var cookieArray = document.cookie.split(';');
    for(i=0; i < cookieArray.length; i++){
        console.log(cookieArray[i]); 
        var valueArray = cookieArray[i].split('=');
        console.log(valueArray);
        if(valueArray[0].trim()=='name'){
            document.myfm.name.value = valueArray[1];
        }
        else if(valueArray[0].trim() == 'email'){
            document.myfm.email.value = valueArray[1];
        }
        else if(valueArray[0].trim() == 'language'){
            document.myfm.lang.value = valueArra
            y[1];
        }
    }
}

How to delete cookie in javascript

- A cookie is with the same name(damain and path) is deleted by setting an expiration date in the past and if using max-age 
then must set a negative value. 
Ex :- 

document.cookie = 'username=sarita; expires=Mon, 3-sep-2021 09:00:00 UTC';
document.cookie = 'username=sarita; expires=Thu, 3-Jan-2021 09:00:00 GMT';

document.cookie = 'username=sarita; max-age=' + 60*60*24*10;
document.cookie = 'username=sarita; max-age=-60';

document.cookie = 'username=sarita;
document.cookie = 'username=sarita; expires=Thu, 3-Jan-2021 09:00:00 GMT';

How to update cookie in javascript

- A cookie is possible to update by setting new value to a cookie with the same name.

Ex :- 
document.cookie = 'username=sarita;
document.cookie = 'username=smruti;

Cookie security Issues

- Can misuse client details 
- Can track user 
- client can delete cookies 
- Client can manipulate cookie 

Local storage in javascript

- The local storage is read only property of window object. 
- It stores data in the web browser specifically to domain and protocol. 
- It is not get sent to server as it is stored locally in web browser with no expiration date. 
- The data will not be deleted when the browser is closed and reopened.

Ex :- window.localStorage

Methods :- 

setItem(key,value):- 
- It allows to add key/value pair to the storage object. 
If the key already exists the value will overwrite old value. 

getItem(key):- 
- It returns the value of given key. 

key(n):- It returns the key of item in storage object at nth index.

removeItem(key):- It removes the item in the storage object at given key. 

Ex :- 

window.localStorage.setItem('username','sarita');
console.log(localStorage);
console.log(localStorage.length);

console.log(localStorage.getItem('username'));

console.log(localStorage.key(0));

console.log(localStorage.removeItem('username'));

localStorage.clear();
console.log(localStorage);

Session Storage in javascript

- The session strorage is read only property of window object. 
- It stores data in browser specially to the domain and protocol for a particular session. 
- It is not sent to server. 
- data stored in session storage gets cleared when page session ends. 
- page session lasts as long as browser is open and survives over page reload and restores. 


Methods :- 

setItem(key,value):- 
- It allows to add key/value pair to the storage object. 
If the key already exists the value will overwrite old value. 

getItem(key):- 
- It returns the value of given key. 

key(n):- It returns the key of item in storage object at nth index.

removeItem(key):- It removes the item in the storage object at given key. 

Syntax :- 
window.sessionStorage;

Ex :- 
sessionStorage.setItem('username','sarita');
console.log(sessionStorage); 

console.log(sessionStorage.getItem('username'));

console.log(sessionStorage.key(0));

sessionStorage.removeItem('username');
console.log(sessionStorge); 


Exception handing in javascript

Exception :- An exception is concept of an error to include any unexpected condition encountered 
during execution. 

Exception Handling :- 
- try
- catch
- finally
- throw 

Ex:- 1
try {
    add();
    console.log('skipped code');
}
catch(e){
    console.log('Message:' + e.message );
    console.log('name:' + e.name);
    console.log('stack:' + e.stack);
}

Ex :- 2
try{
    add();
}
catch(e){
    console.log(' this function is not defined');
}

Ex :- 3
try{
    add();
}
catch(e){
    console.log('your function is not defined');
}
finally{
    console.log('this block of code is executed whether exception or not');
}

Ex :- 4 
function getRectArea(w, h){
    if(isNaN(w) || isNaN(h)){
        throw 'Parameter is not a number';
    }
}
try{
    getRectArea(10,'A');
}
catch(e){
    console.log(e);
}
console.log('I have no idea what is going on above');


strict mode in javascript

- 'use strict'; is written at the top of javascript file or any function which we want to execute in strict
mode. 
- It will raise error if code is written weakly for example 
a = 10; // it will raise error in strict mode that a is not defined. while we can write it without error if 
strict mode is mode used in .js file or any function. 

var a = 10; // it will not raise error. 


How to check browser cookie enabled or disabled in javascript

Navigator object

console.dir(navigator);

console.log(navigator.userAgent);

if(navigator.cookieEnabled){
    console.log('cookie is enabled');
}else{
    console.log('cookie is disabled');
}


callback function in javascript

- A callback function is a function(it can be any function annonymous, Arrow function) passed in another 
function as an argument, which is then invoked inside outer function to perform some action.        

Ex :- 

function show(){
    console.log('I am show function'+a);
}
function geeky(callback){
    callback();
}
geeky(show); 

Ex: - 2 

function show(a){
    console.log('I am show function'+a);
}
function geeky(callback){
    var a = 10;
    callback(a);
}
geeky(show);    

or

function geeky(callback){
    var a = 10;
    callback(a);
}
geeky(function show(a){
    console.log('I am show function'+ a);
});    

or

function geeky(callback){
    var a = 10;
    callback(a);
}
geeky(function(a){
    console.log('I am show function'+ a);
});    

or 
function geeky(callback){
    var a = 10;
    callback(a);
}
geeky(a => console.log('I am show function' + a));    

function geeky(callback){
    var a = 10;
    callback();
}
geeky(() => {
    console.log('I am show function ');
    console.log('we are using arrow function');
});    


Difference between synchronous and Asynchronous function 

synchronous function
 
- It waits for each operation to complete after that it executes next operation

Ex:- 
function geeky(callback){
    var a = 10;
    callback(a);
}
geeky(function show(a){
    console.log('I am show function'+ a);
});    

console.log('I will be execute after above function');

Asynchronous function

- It never waits for each operation to complete rather it executes all operations in one go only. 

Ex:- 
setTimeout(function(){
    console.log('I will execute after 5 sec but the next line will execute before me and won't wait for me);
}, 5000);

console.log('I will not wait for above function and execute before it');

map() Method in javascript

- The map() method creates a new array with the result of calling given function on every element in the 
calling array.
- map calls a given callback function once for each element in an array, in order and returns a new array 
from the result. 

Syntax :- 

map(callback(currentValue, index, array), thisArg);

Ex:- 
var arr = [10,20,30,40,50];
var newArr = arr.map(function(value, index){
    value++;
    //  console.log(value);
    // console.log(index);
    return value;
})

Ex:- 2 
var arr = [
{price:'100', product:'Mobile'},
{price:'300', product:'Mic'},
{price:'200', product:'pc'},
];
var newArr = arr.map(value => value.price); // return value.price 
console.log(newArr);


Array destructuring in javascript

- Destructuring is a way of extracting multiple values from data stored in objects or arrays. 
- The destructuring makes it possible unpack value from arrays or properties from objects, into distinct
variable. 

Ex:- 
var a = [10,20,30];
[x,y,z] = a;
left hand side defines what values to unpack from the sourced variable.
console.log(x); //10 
console.log(y); //20
console.log(z); //30

var a = ['javascript', 'sixMonth', 'sarita'];
var [courseName, duration, tutor] = a;
console.log(courseName);
console.log(duration);
console.log(tutor);

when destructuring array, we use their index/position in the Assignment. 
var [courseName,,tutor] = a;

var a,b;
[a,b] = [10,20];
console.log(a);
console.log(b);

var a,b;
[a,b=20] = [10];
console.log(a); // 10
console.log(b); // 20

var a,b;
[a=40,b=20] = [10];
console.log(a); // 10
console.log(b); // 20

 Array passing to a function
var arr = [10,20,30];
function show([value1, value2, value3]){
    console.log(value1); // 10
    console.log(value2); // 20 
    console.log(value3); // 30
}
show(arr);

var arr = [10,20,30,40,50,60];
function show([value1, value2, ...rest]){
    console.log(value1); // 10
    console.log(value2); // 20 
    console.log(value3); // 30
}
show(arr);

Array Returning from a function 

var arr = [10,20.30];

function show(z){
    return z;
}

var x = show(arr);
var [value1, value2, value3] = x;
console.log(value1); // 10
console.log(value2); // 20
console.log(value3); // 30

Module Import Export in javascript

What is Module in javascript

- Module is a the javascript file where we write codes. 
- The object in a Module is not available for use, unless the module file exports them. 

Exporting Module

export - export statment is used to export functions, objects or primitive values from modeule. 
- There are two default types of export : named and default 
- we can have multiple named export per module but only one default export. 

Default export : we can have only one default export per module. 
- A default can be exported with any name. 

mobile.js 

// class exporting default 
export default class Nokia{
    Properties 
    Methods 
}

or 

class Nokia{
    Properties 
    Methods 
}
export default Nokia;

// function exporting default 
export default function show(){

}

or 

function show(){

}
export default show();

// variable exporting default 
var a = 10; 
export default a;

Named Export

- We can have multiple named exports per module. 
- Named exports are useful to export several values. 
- During the import, it is mandatory to use the same name of corresponding object. 

mobile.js 

// class exporting default 
export class Nokia{
    Properties 
    Methods 
}

or 

class Nokia{
    Properties 
    Methods 
}
export {Nokia};

// function exporting default 
export function show(){
   
}
or 

function show(){

}
export {show()};

// variable exporting default 
export const a = 10;

var a = 10; 
export {a};

class Nokia{
    Properties 
    Methods 
}
function show(){

}
export const a = 10;

export {Nokia, show};

Importing Module

import - import statement is used to import bindings which are exported by another module. 
- Imported modules are in strict mode whether you declare or not. 

Importing Default

- We can have only one default export per module. 
- A default export can be exported with any name. 

mobile.js 

class Nokia {
    Properties 
    Methods 
}
export default Nokia;

app.js

import Nokia from './mobile.js'

Importing Named 

- We can multiple named export per module. 
- Named exports are useful to export several value. 
- During import, it is mandatory to use same name. 

mobile.js 

export class Nokia {
    Properties
    Methods 
}
function show(){

}
export {show};

app.js 

// import {Nokia} from './mobile.js'
import {Nokia, show} from './mobile.js'

Importing All

mobile.js 

class Nokia{
    Properties 
    Methods 
}
export function show(){

}
export const a = 10;
export {Nokia};

app.js  

import * as device from './mobile.js'

var n = new device.Nokia() 
device.show()
device.a 

Importing Default and Named 

mobile.js 

class Nokia {
    Properties 
    Methods 
}
export function show(){

}
export default Nokia;

app.js 

import Nokia, {show} from './mobile.js'

Note :- write type= module to work with modules it is mandatory 
script type="module" src="" 


Spread operator

- Spread syntax allows an iterable such as array expression or string to be expanded in places where zero 
or more elements (for any literals) are expected, or an object expression to be expanded in places 
where zero or more key-value pairs (for object literals) are expected. 

Ex :- 1
var a = [10, 20, 30];
var b = [5, ...a, 50, 60]; // ... is spread operator, it will take all elements inside of array a
a[0] = 50;
console.log(a[0]);
console.log(b[0]);

Ex :- 2
var a = [10, 20, 30];
var a = [40, 50, 60];
var c = [...a, ...b];
console.log(a); 
console.log(b);
console.log(c);

Ex :-3
var a = {course:'java', tutor:'sarita'};
var b = {...a, duration:'six'};
a.course = 'php';
console.log(a);
console.log(b);

Ex :-4
var a = {course:'java', tutor:'sarita'};
var b = {duration:'six'};
var c = {...a, ...b};

Note :- In array and object are refence type so if you assign it to other variable and then make change in 
one variable then it will affect another variable also so we use spread operator, which can assign value 
of array or object without changing value of first array or object

Promise in javascript

- A promise is an object representing the eventual completion or failure of an Asynchronous operation. 
- A javascript promise object contains both the producing code and calls to the consuming code. It can be 
used to deal with Asynchronous operation in javascript. 

Promise state:- 
Pending - Initial State, Not yet fulfilled or rejected 
Fulfilled/Resolved - Promise completed
rejected - Promise Failed

How promise works

- A pending promise can either be resolved with a value or rejected with a reason(error). 
- when either of these options happens, the associated handlers queued up by a promise's then method are 
called. 
- Promise is said to be settled if it is either resolved or rejected, but not pending. 

Creating a Promise object

Promise() :- 
- A promise object is created using the new keyword and its constructor. 
- This constructor takes a function called 'executor function' as its parameter. 
- This function should take two function as parameters.
- The first of these function (resolve) is called when Asynchronous task complete successfully and returns
a value. 
- The second (reject) is called when the task fails, and returns the result of failure, which is typically
an error. 

Syntax:- Prmoise(executor)
syntax :- 
    
const promiseObj = new Promise( (resolve, reject)=>{
    Do asynchronous operation
    resolve(value)
    reject(Error)
})

- the javascript object contains both the producing code and calls to the consuming code. 

function returning a promise :- 

function myFunction(){
    return new Promise((resolve, reject)=> {
        
    })
}

then() Method

- The then() method returns a Promise.
- It takes up to two arguments : callback function for the success and failure cases of the promise. 
- As then() method returns a promise so we can do chaining. 

Syntax :- then(onResolved, onRejected);

onResolved :- A function called, if the promise is fulfilled, this function has one argument the 
fulfillment value. 

onRejected :- A function called, if the promise is rejected, this function has one argument the rejection 
reason. 

// consuming code
promiseObj.then(value=>{
    console.log(value);
},
error=>{
    console.log(error);
});

EX :- 

const promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>
{
    let req = true;
    if (req == true){
        resolve('Request Success');
    }else{
        reject('Request rejected');
    }
});

promiseObj.then(
    (value)=>{console.log(value);},
    (error)=>{console.log(error);},
);

or 

const promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>
{
    let req = true;
    if (req == true){
        resolve('Request Success');
    }else{
        reject('Request rejected');
    }
}).then(
    (value)=>{console.log(value)},
    (error)=>{console.log(error)},
);

Chaining

- then() method returns a Promise which allows for method chaining. 
- If a function passed as a handler to then, returns a Promise, an equivalent then will be exposed to the 
subsequent then in the method chain.    

const promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
    let num = 10;
    resolve(num);
}).then(
    (value)=>{console.log(value);
    return value+10;
}).then(
    (value)=>{console.log(value);
    });

catch() Method

- The catch() method returns a Promise and deals with rejected cases only. 
- It behaves the same as calling then(undefined, onRejected). 
- In fact, calling catch(onRejected) internally calls then(undefined, onRejected). 
- The catch method is used for error handling in Promise composition. 
- Since it returns a Promise, it can be chained in the same way as its sister method, then()

Syntax :-
where the callback is a function called when the Promise is rejected. this function has one argument
error - The rejection error. 

Ex :- 
const promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
    let req = true 
    if(req==true){
        resolve('request success');
    }else{
        reject('request rejected');
    }
}).then(
    (value)=>{console.log(value);
}).catch(
    (error)=>{console.log(error);
});

finally() Method

- The finally() method returns a Promise. 
- When the Promise is settled i.e either fulfilled or rejected, the specified callback function is executed. 
- whether Promise is fulfilled successfully or rejected once the Promise has been dealt with. 
- this helps to avoid duplicating code in both the promise's then() and catch() handlers. 
Syntax:- 
finally(callback)

Ex :- 1

const promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
    let req = true; 
    if(req==true){
        resolve('Request success');
    }else{
        reject('Request Rejected');
    }
}).then(
    (value)=>{console.log(value);
}).catch(
    (error)=>{console.log(error);
}).finally(
    ()=>{console.log('cleaned');
});

Ex :- 2 

const promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
    let num = 10;
    resolve(num);
}).then(
    (value)=>{console.log(value);
    return value+10
}).then(
    (value)=>{console.log(value);
}).then(
    ()=>{throw new Error('Error Found')};
).catch(
    (error)=>{console.log(error);
});

Ex :- 1 

// Promise - then 
const promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
    let req = true;
    if (req==true){
        resolve('Request success');
    }else{
        reject('Request Rejected');
    }
});

promiseObj.then(
    (value)=>{
        console.log(value);
    },
    (error)=>{
        console.log(error);
    }

// Promise - catch 
var promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
    let req = false;
    if(req==true){
        resolve('reuest success');
    }else{
        reject('Request Rejected');
    }
});

promiseObj.then(
    (value)=>{
        console.log(value);
    },
).catch(
    (error)=>{
        console.log(error);
});

const promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
    let num = 10;
    resolve(num);
}).then(
    (value)=>{
        console.log(value);
        return value+10;
}).then(
    (value)=>{
        console.log(value);
});

Ex :- 4 

// Promise - catch - finally 
var promiseObj = new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
    let req = true;
    if(req == true){
        resolve('Request success');
    }else{
        reject('request rejected');
    }
}).then(
    (value)=>{
        console.log(value);
    }
).catch(
    (error)=>{
        console.log(error);
    }
).finally(()=>{
    console.log('Finally executed');
})

Ex :- 5


console.log('start');

function getName(name){
    return new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
        setTimeout(() => {
            console.log('Inside set time out');
            resolve(name);
        }, 2000);
    })
}

function getHobbies(name){
    return new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
        setTimeout(() => {
            console.log('Inside hobby function');
            resolve(['cricket','dancing']);
        }, 3000);
    })
}

getName('sarita').then(
    (name)=>{
        getHobbies(name);
}).then(
    (hobby)=>{
        console.log(hobby);
    }
)


Async and Await

- This keyword is used to turn a function declaration to async function. 
async function - An async function is a function declared with the async keyword. 
- An async function is a function that knows how to expect the possibility of the await keyword being used 
to invoke asynchronous code. It returns a promise.
- The await operator is used to wait for promise. It can only be used inside an async function within 
regular javascript code. 
- await can be put infront of any async promise-based function to pause your code on that line until the 
promise fulfills, then return the resulting value. 

Async function - 
async function function_name(){.....}

Async function expression - 
let function_name = async function(){.....}

Async Arrow Function - 
let function_name =async() => {....}

Ex:- 

function getName(name){
    return new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
        setTimeout(() => {
            console.log('Inside set time out');
            resolve(name);
        }, 2000);
    })
}

function getHobbies(name){
    return new Promise((resolve, reject)=>{
        setTimeout(() => {
            console.log('Inside hobby function');
            resolve(['cricket','dancing']);
        }, 3000);
    })
}

async function showHobby(){
    const nm = await getName('sonam')
    const hobby = await getHobbies(nm);
    console.log(hobby)
}

console.log('end');

Introduction to Javascript

It is programming language use to create functionality in web page. functionality :- reading input, performing process and providing output. Ex:- displaying menu when the user click on menu.
  • As it is programming language, it provides all concepts like datatype, functions, objects, variables and more
  • It is a case sensitive language. upper case and lower case are different here
  • It is object oriented programming language
  • It is developed by netscape corporation
    • syntax of javascript
  • Internal javascript :- will be written in same html file.
    • placing script in head tag
    • placing script in body tag
  • External javascript :- will be written in seperate javascript file with extention .js

Output statment in javascript

  • output statment is use to use show some output to user
  • console.log is output statement in js
  • we have to open browser console to see output. to open browser console press F12

variables

variable is named memory location in RAM to store particular value.
  • var is a keyword use to declare variable.
  • In javascript variable's datatype can be changed that means we can assign any type of value

Operators in javascript

  • to perform some operation like ... 10 + 2
      • Type of operator
    • Arithmetic operator.... +, *, -, %, /
    • Increment and decrement operators .... ++, --
    • Assignment operator.... used to assign value to var... =, *=, +=, -=, %=
    • Relational operator... ==, !=, <, >, <=, >=
    • Logical operator...
      • && -- and (both condition must be true)
      • || -- or (at least one condition must be true)
      • ! -- not (given condition will be reversed)
    • concatination operator...use to add two string

Control statement

  • by default, statements executes in sequencial order(top-bottom)
  • Types of control statement
  • conditional control statement
    • if
      • if
      • if-else
      • else-if
      • nested if
    • switch - case
    • when we have one variable with many possibility
  • Looping control statement
    • while
    • do - while
    • for

Function

function is a collection of statements, to perform some specific operation.

Arguments - predefined variable

it is used to represent all the argument value that are received by the current function. it is a pre-defined variable that can be used only in the function.
  • arguments : returns collection of all argument value
  • arguments[index]: returns the single arguments based on given index.
  • arguments.length : count of argument volue received
Recursion :- the function calls itself

syntax :-
function functionName(){
    if (condition)
    {
        functionName();
    }
}

EXAMPLE :- factorial of n numbers
function factorial(n){
    if (n==1){
        return 1;
    }
    else 
        return n * factorial(n - 1);
        }

factorial(5)

switch case statment

let weekday = 2;
switch(weekday){
    case 1:
        document.write("monday");
        break;
    case 2:
        document.write("tuesday");
        break;
    case 3:
        document.write("wednesday");
        break;
    case 4:
        document.write("thursday");
        break;
    case 5:
        document.write("friday");
        break;
    case 6:
        document.write("saturday");
        break;
    case 7:
        document.write("sunday");
        break;
    default:
        document.write(` Invalid day `);
}

- it checks whether the expression is null or undefined 
- if it null or undefined  it will return default value -- here unknown
- if not null or undefined - it return value of variable

function to print in reverse order

function reverse(array){
    document.write("function to print in reverse order");
    for(var i=array.length-1;i>=0; i--){
        document.write(array[i]);
    }
}
reverse([10,20,30,40,50]);


function to check identical element

function identical(array){
    document.write("function to check identical element");
    let first = array[0];
    for(var i=1; i< array.length; i++){
        if (array[i] != first)
        {
            return false;
        }
         }
            return true;
        }

iden = identical([10,10,10,10,10]);
console.log(iden);


function to check max number

function maximum(array){
    document.write("function to check max number");
    let max = array[0];
    for (i=1;i< array.length;i++){
        if (array[i]>max){
            max = array[i];
        };
       
    };
    return max;
};

maxi = maximum([10,40,50,80,90]);
document.write(maxi);


function to sum all number

function sum(array){
    document.write("function to sum all number");
    let sum = 0;
    for (num of array){
        sum = sum + num;
    }
    return sum;
}

sum1 = sum([10,20,30,40]);
document.write(sum1);


book management system using javascript

var books = [];
var input = prompt('which operation you want to perform ? [add | list | delete | exit');
while (input != 'exit'){
    if (input == 'add')
    {
        addbook();
    }
    else if(input == 'list')
    {
        listbook();
    }
    else if(input == 'delete')
    {
        deletebook();
    }
    else{
        console.log('please choose valid option');
    }
    input = prompt('which operation you want to perform ? [add | list | delete | exit');
}
console.log('thanks for using our application');

function addbook()
{
var newbook = prompt('enter book name to add');
books.push(newbook);
}

function listbook(){
    console.log('list of available book:-');
    for (book of books){
        console.log(book);
    }
}

function deletebook(){
    var name = prompt('enter name of book to delete');
    index = books.indexOf(name);
    if(index == -1){
        console.log('specified book not avasilable');
    }
    else{
        books.splice(index, 1);
        console.log('specified book deleted');
    }
    
}

Object Oriented Programming In Javascript


object in javascript

- an object is collection of properties.
- It has key and value.
- value can be a function (it is called method)

Example of object:-
let fees = {
    sarita : 100, // property 
    smruti : 200, // property
    total : function (){return (100 + 200);} //method
}

User-defined Objects :- this are custom objects made by user.

Native Objects :- Provided by javascript like string, boolen, function, date etc..

Host Objects :- supported by most host environments like window, navigator..

Document Objects :- this are part of documentobject model (DOM). access to document object is provided 
by browser via document property of the window(window.document)


Declaration and initialization of object

Using Object Literal

var fees = {};
fees['sarita'] = 100;
fees.smruti = 200;
fees["super man"] = 300; // multiword requires quotation
fees['total'] = function (){return (100 + 200 + 300);};

document.write(fees.total()); // to access total method of object
document.write(fees['total']()); // to access total method of object

Using Object Literal

var object_name = new Object();
var fees = new Object(); // var fees = {}
fees['sarita'] = 100;
fees.smruti = 200;
fees['total'] = function (){return (100 + 200 + 300);};

fees.total = sum; // second way to assign function

function sum(){
    return (100 + 200);
}


Accessing Properties of Object

- A property of an object contains named data.
- this can be accessed with dot operator or array [] operator.
- objects functions are called methods.
- this can be accessed with dot operator or array [] operator.

syntax:-object_name.property_name 

Ex:- 
var fees = {Rahul:100, sarita:200};
document.write(fees.Rahul + " " + fees.sarita);

Adding property in Javascript object

fees.sonam = 500;
fees.show = function(){};

document.write(fees.Rahul + " " + fees.sarita + " " + fees.sonam);

Deleting property from javascript objects

Delete operator is used to delete instance property
syntax :- delete object_name.property_name

Ex :- delete fees.Rahul;

after removal with delete property has undefined value.note

Factory Function

when a function returns an object, we call it factory function.
it can produce object without new keyword or classes.

Ex :- 
function mobile(){
    return {
        model : Galaxy,
        price : function(){return ("price: Rs. 3000");}
    }
}

var samsang = mobile();
document.write(samsang.model + " " + samsang.price());

function mobile(model_no){
    return {
        model : model_no,
        price : function(){
            return "Price is Rs. 3000";
        }
    };
}

var samsang = mobile("Galaxy");
var nokia = mobile('3310');
document.write(samsang.model + " " + samsang.price() + "
");
document.write(nokia.model + " " + nokia.price() + "
");

Constructor in javascript

- object instance are created  with constructor.
- constructor are basically special function that prepare new instance of an object for use. 

// Defining constructor is like class in python 
    --here self is replaced with this
    -- first letter of constructor name should be capital 

Ex :- constructor without parameter 

function Mobile(){
    this.model = '3310';
    this.price = function(){document.write(this.model + " Price Rs. 3000")
    }
};

var samsang = new Mobile(); //creating object using constructor
samsang.price(); // accessing method of object 


 Ex :- constructor with parameter 

function Mobile(model_no){
    this.model = model_no;
    this.price = function(){
        document.write(this.model + " Price Rs. 3000 ");
    };
}

var samsang = new Mobile("samsang");
var nokia = new Mobile("nokia");
samsang.price();
nokia.price();


Check properties exists in Javascript


Using typeof operator :-
syntax:- if(typeof object_name.key !== 'undefined')

Ex :-

function Mobie(){
    this.model = '3310';
    this.price = function(){document.write(this.model + " Price Rs. 3000");
    };
};

var nokia = new Mobile();

// check for memory property exists in nokia object or not
if(typeof nokia.memory !== "undefined"){
    document.write("available");
}else{
    document.write("Not available");
}

Using in operator :-

syntax :- if('key' in object_name)

Ex :- 

if('memory' in nokia){
    document.write("available");
}else{
    document.write("not available");
}

Using hasOwnProperty() :-

syntax :- if(object_name.hasOwnProperty("key"))

Ex:- 

if(nokia.hasOwnProperty("memory")){
    document.write("available");
}else{
    document.write("doesn't exit");
}

Class in Javascript

A specific category can be defined as class.

Defining a Class in Javascript

we define class in javascript using custom constructor.

Ex :- 

var Mobile = function(model_no, sprice){
    this.model = model_no;
    this.color = 'white';
    this.price = 3000;
    this.sp = sprice;
    this.sellingprice = function(){
        return (this.price + this.sp);
    };
};

var samsang = new Mobile('Galaxy',2000);
var nokia = new Mobile('3310',1000);
samsang.sellingprice();

Private Properties And Methods

Using var or let or const you can create private properties and methods.

Ex :- 

var Mobile = function(model_no, sprice){
    var model = model_no;
    var color = 'white';
    var price = 3000;
    var sp = sprice;
    var sellingprice = function(){
        return (price + sp);
    };
};

var samsang = new Mobile('Galaxy',2000);
var nokia = new Mobile('3310',1000);
samsang.sellingprice();

Access Private Property outside the function

Private properties declared using var or let or const inside class can be accessed by Defining
public method inside class

Ex :- 

var Mobile = function(model_no, sprice){
    var model = model_no;
    var color = 'white';
    var price = 3000; // by defining public method(sellingprice) we can now access private property price.
    var sp = sprice;
    this.sellingprice = function(){
        return (price); //returns private property's value( price value )
    };
};

var samsang = new Mobile('Galaxy',2000);
var nokia = new Mobile('3310',1000);
samsang.sellingprice();

    };
};

    document.write(key);
