--> createElement(element_name)
--> createTextNode(string)
--> createComment(string)
--> createDocumentFragment()

 create Element Node

- createElement(element_name) method is used to create the HTML element specified by TagName,
or an HTMLUnknownElement if tagName isn't recognized. It returns new element. 

Syntax :- 
createElement(element_name)

var newElem = document.createElement("h2");
console.log(newElem);
Output :- < h2> < /h2>

 create Text Node - createTextNode(string)

- it is used to create Text Node with the specified string. 

Syntax :- 
createTextNode(string)

var newTxtNode = document.createTextNode("text node created by javascript");
console.log(newTxtNode);
Output :- "text node created by javascript"

 create Comment Node - createComment(string)

- it is used to create the comment node with specified string and returns it. 

syntax :- 
createComment(string)

var newComment = document.createComment("we created a comment");
console.log(newComment);
Output :- 

What is Document Fragment in Javascript

 - the DocumentFragment interface represents a minimal document object that has no parent. 
 - a common use of DocumentFragment is to create one, assemble a DOM subtree within it, then append 
 or insert the fragment into the DOM using Node interface methods such as appendchild() or insertBefore. 
 - DocumentFragment isn't part of the active document tree structure, changes made to the fragment 
 don't affect the document. 
 - Doing this, moves the fragment's node into the DOM, leaving behind an empty document Fragment. 
 - An empty document fragment can be created using the document.createDocumentFragment() Method. 

 Create Document Fragment

 - the createDocumentFragment() method creates an imaginary Node object, with all the properties and 
 method of the Node object. 

 var df = document.createDocumentFragment(); // creates empty DocumentFragment
 console.log(df);
 Output :- #document-fragment 

 How to Append Element Node in javascript

 - The appendChild(Child_Node) method is used to add a node to the end of the list of children of 
 specified parent node. 
 - If the given child is a referance to an existing node in the document, appendChild() moves it from 
 its current position to the new position. this method returns the new child node. 

 syntax :- appendChild(Child_Node)
 Parent_Node.appendChild(Child_Node);
  
 mysec.appendChild(child);
 It will append child to mysec. child will be last child of mysec. 

Ex :- 

var parent = document.getElementById("myid");
var child = document.getElementById("add");
console.log(parent);
console.log(child);
parent.appendChild(child);
console.log(parent);

// creating a new element node and appending node. 

var nenode = document.createElement("h3");
var parent = document.getElementById("add");
parent.appendChild(nenode);
console.log(parent)

or

var parent = document.getElementById("add");
parent.appendChild(document.createElement("h3"));
console.log(parent)

Append Text Node in javascript

var parent = document.getElementById("add");
// creating new text node 
var txtNode = document.createTextNode(" / add your future activity to list");
parent.appendChild(txtNode);
console.log(parent);

Append Comment Node in Javascript

var parent = document.getElementById("add");
// creating a comment node 
var commentNode = document.createComment(" adding to do iteams in list");
parent.appendChild(commentNode);
console.log(parent);

Append Element node, Comment node and text node together

// creating new element h2 
var nENode = document.createElement("h2");

//creating text node 
var txtNode = document.createTextNode("here is text node created");

//creating comment node 
var cmtNode = document.createComment("the coment text for element");

// Append text node to element node 
nENode.appendChild(txtNode);
console.log(nENode);

// Append element to an existing element
var parent = document.getElementById("add");
parent.appendChild(nENode);
parent.appendChild(cmtNode);
console.log(parent);

Example of DocumentFragment in javascript

// create empty DocumentFragment and create any two element then add text to those element then append 
those element to DocumentFragment and append DocumentFragment to any element of document 

var df = document.createDocumentFragment(); // create empty DocumentFragment

var elem1 = document.createElement("h3");  // creating h3 element
var elem2 = document.createElement("p");   // creating p element

elem1.textContent = "here is h3 element";  // adding text content to element 
elem2.textContent = "here is p element";   // adding text content to element 

df.appendChild(elem1);  // adding elements to DocumentFragment
df.appendChild(elem2);  // adding elements to DocumentFragment

var parent = document.getElementById("add");

parent.appendChild(df);  // moving DocumentFragment elements to element of document
console.log(parent); // elemnts will be added from document fragment to parent element 

console.log(df);
Output :- #document-fragment //empty document fragment


normalize() method in javascript

this method removes empty text nodes, and joins adjcent text nodes so there will be no adjcent text nodes.

Syntax :- normalize()

var elem = document.getElementById("add");
elem.normalize()

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById("add"); // accessing element

elem.appendChild(document.createTextNode(" hello "));  // adding text node to parent elem
elem.appendChild(document.createTextNode(" I want to"));   //adding text node to parent elem
elem.appendChild(document.createTextNode(" learn JAVASCRIPT "));  //adding text node to parent elem

console.log(elem.childNodes);

elem.normalize(); // it merges all adjcent text nodes, removes empty text nodes
console.log(elem.childNodes);  //it returns all child nodes including whitespace, text & comment nodes 


insertBefore() Method in javascript

- The insertBefore() method is used to insert a node before the reference node as a child of a specified 
parent node. 
- If the given child is reference to an exising node in the document, insertBefore() moves it from 
its current position to the new position. 
- If referenceNode is null, the newNode is inserted at the end of the list of child nodes. 

syntax :- 

var insertedNode = parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, referenceNode);

insertedNode = the node being inserted, that is new node. 
parentNode = the parent of the newly inserted node. 
newNode = the node to be inserted. 
referenceNode = the node before which new node is inserted.

Ex:- 

 inserting new created element before referance eleme

parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");   // accessing element  
refNode = document.getElementById("myli"); // accessing element 

newNode = document.createElement("li"); // creating an element
newNode.textContent = "for loop"; 

parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, refNode); // inserting new element(newNode) before referance element(refNode)
console.log(parentNode);

 inserting existing element before referance element

parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");   // accessing element  
refNode = document.getElementById("myli"); // accessing element 

newNode = document.getElementById("el"); // Existing element

parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, refNode); // inserting Existing element(newNode) before referance element(refNode)
console.log(parentNode);

 inserting element without referance element(null), it will insert element at last position

parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");   // accessing element  

newNode = document.getElementById("el"); // Existing element

parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, null); // inserting Existing element(newNode) at last 
console.log(parentNode);

 inserting text node before referance element

parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");   // accessing element  
refNode = document.getElementById("myli"); // accessing element 

newNode = document.createTextNode("For loop"); // new text nodeValue

parentNode.insertBefore(newNode, refNode); // inserting new text node before reference node  
console.log(parentNode);

insertAdjacentElement() Method

- The insertAdjacentElement() method inserts the specified element into a given specified position. 
- It returns the element that wes inserted or null if insertion failed. 

Syntax :- 

targetElement.insertAdjacentElement("position", element); 
where positions are :- 
    beforebegin :- before the element itself. 
    afterbegin :- just inside the element, before its first child 
    beforeend :- just inside the element, after its last child 
    afterend :- after the element itself. 
element :- the element to be inserted into tree. 
the beforebegin and afterend position work only if the node is in a tree and has an element parent. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");   
var newElem = document.createElement("span");
newElem.textContent = "this is text";
var tarElem = document.getElementById("myli");

tarElem.insertAdjacentElement("beforebegin", newElem); // beforebegin----> < h1> < br> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentElement("afterbegin", newElem);  // < h1> <---- afterbegin < br>< /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentElement("afterbegin", newElem); // < h1> < br> beforeend----> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

// tarElem.insertAdjacentElement("afterend", newElem); // < h1> < br>< /h1> <--- afterend
console.log(elem); 

insertAdjacentHTML() Method 

- this method is used to insert text as HTML (parse the specified text as HTML or XML)

Syntax :- 
element.insertAdjacentHTML("position", text);
where positions are :- 
    beforebegin :- before the element itself. 
    afterbegin :- just inside the element, before its first child 
    beforeend :- just inside the element, after its last child 
    afterend :- after the element itself.

text :- The string to be parsed as HTML or XML and inserted into tree. 

- It is recommended you not use insertAdjacentHTML when inserting plain text instead, 
use the node.textContent property. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");   
var newElem = "< span>Hello < /span>""

var tarElem = document.getElementById("myli");

tarElem.insertAdjacentHTML("beforebegin", newElem); // beforebegin----> < h1> < br> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentHTML("afterbegin", newElem);  // < h1> <---- afterbegin < br>< /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentHTML("afterbegin", newElem); // < h1> < br> beforeend----> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

// tarElem.insertAdjacentHTML("afterend", newElem); // < h1> < br>< /h1> <--- afterend
console.log(elem); 

insertAdjacentText Method in javascript

The insertAdjacentText() method inserts the specified element into a specified position. 

Syntax :- 
targetElement.insertAdjacentText("position", text);
where positions are :- 
    beforebegin :- before the element itself. 
    afterbegin :- just inside the element, before its first child 
    beforeend :- just inside the element, after its last child 
    afterend :- after the element itself.

text - the text which is about to insert. 
The beforebegin and afterend positions work only if the node is in tree and has an element parent. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");   

var tarElem = document.getElementById("myli");
var txt = " Hello ";

tarElem.insertAdjacentText("beforebegin",txt); // beforebegin----> < h1> < br> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentText("afterbegin",txt);  // < h1> <---- afterbegin < br>< /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentText("beforeend",txt); // < h1> < br> beforeend----> < /h1>
console.log(elem);

tarElem.insertAdjacentText("afterend",txt ); // < h1> < br>< /h1> <--- afterend
console.log(elem); 

innerHTML in javascript

- The Element property innerHTML gets or sets the HTML or XML markup contained within the element. 

Syntax :- 
var content = element.innerHTML;
element.innerHTML = htmlstring;

document.getElementById("add").innerHTML = htmlString;

outerHTML in javascript

- The outerHTML is the HTML of an element including the element itself.
- Use the outerHTML to completely replace an element and its content. 
- Use innerHTML to replace the content of an element. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");
var elem1 = element.outerHTML;
elem.outerHTML = " ";

innerText in javascript

- It works same as innerHTML property, except it focus on textual content within an element. 
- it sets and returns the text content of specified node. 
- If we set innerText property, any child nodes are removed and replaced by single text node. 

outerText :- outerText property works same as outerHTML property, modifies the element itself, and replace 
it with a single text node. 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");
var elem1 = element.innerText;
elem.innerText = " ";

write and writeln in javascript

document.write() :- this is used to write arbitary HTML and content into page. 
- If we use this function after HTML document is fully loaded, will delete all existing HTML. 
- It is used for testing purpose. 

Ex :- 
document.write("hello world"); 

document.writeln() :- this is same as document.write() method writing a newline character 
after each statment. 

Ex :- 
document.writeln("hello world");

copy Node in javascript

- The cloneNode(deep) method is used to copy the node. 
- It creates copy of node including their all attribute, values and return the clone. 
- It takes a single boolean argument, indicates wheather copy should include all children or just element. 
- The duplicate node returned by cloneNode is not part of document untill it is added to node 
    which is part of document. 

Syntax :- 

cloneNode(false) -- will copy only element, attribute and their value
cloneNode(true) -- will copy entire element with child as well. 

var duplicateNode = targetNode.cloneNode(false);

Ex :- 

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");

var duplicateNode = elem.cloneNode(true);
console.log(duplicateNode);
Output :- it returns all element including child

var duplicateNode = elem.cloneNode(false);
console.log(duplicateNode); 
Output :- it only returns element

Remove Node in javascript

- removeChild(child_name) Method is used to delete node from tree. 
- the removed child node still exist in memory but no longer part of the DOM. 
- It returns node object that was removed on success and null on failure. 

Syntax :- parentNode.removeChild(target_node);
var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(target_node)

Ex:- 

var parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");
var targetNode = document.getElementById("myli");

var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(targetNode);
console.log(delNode);
console.log(parentNode);

// removing element of which we have not id 

var parentNode = document.getElementById("rad");
var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(parentNode.firstElementChild);
var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(parentNode.firstElementChild.nextElementSibling);
var delNode = parentNode.removeChild(parentNode.childNodes[1]);

// removing element without parent element 

var childElemNode = document.getElementById("myli");
var delNode = childElemNode.parentNode.removeChild(childElemNode);

console.log(parentNode);

How to Replace Node in JAVASCRIPT

- the replaceChild(newChild, oldChild) method is used to replace a node with new node or existing node. 
- It will destroy the content of nodes that are replced. 
- It returns the replaced node (oldChild). 

syntax :- 

var replacedNode = parentNode.replaceChild(newChild, oldChild); 

- newChild is the new node to replace oldChild. If it already exists in the DOM, it is first removed. 
- oldChild existing child to be replaced. 

replacing element with new element

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");
var newChild = document.createElement("li");
newChild.textContent = "while loop is infinite when true";
oldChild = document.getElementById("myli");

var replacedNode = elem.replaceChild(newChild, oldChild);
console.log(replacedNode);

replacing element with existing element

var elem = document.getElementById("rad");
oldChild = document.getElementById("myli");
var existChild = oldChild.firstElementChild;

var replacedNode = elem.replaceChild(existChild, oldChild);
console.log(replacedNode);

delete data in text node in javascript

deleteData(start, length)

- This method is used to delete text content from text node and comment node. 
- It deletes specified length of characters starting from index defined in start. 

Syntax :- 
TextNode.deleteData(start, length);

Ex :-
TextNode.deleteData(0, 5); // it will start from 0 index and delete upto 5th index but not including 5th 

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById("add");
txtNode = elem.firstChild;
txtNode.deleteData(0,6); // it will delete from 0 index to 5th index

var elem = document.getElementById("add");

txtNode.insertData(0, "daily to do activity ");
                        or   
elem.firstChild.insertData(0, "daily to do activity ");

Replace data in text node in javascript

replaceData(start, length, string)

- This method is used to replace text content of text node and comment node. 
- It inserts the value in string, starting at character index specified in start.

Syntax :- 
TextNode.replaceData(start, length, string); 
TextNode.replaceData(0, 4, "bye" ); // start at 0 replace 0 to 3 character with "bye"

Split Text in javascript

- The splitText(start) method breaks the text node into two nodes at the specified start index, keeping 
both nodes in the tree as sibling. 
- It returns right side of the split in new text node and leaves left side in the original node. 

var rightSide = TextNode.splitText(start);

var rightSide = TextNode.splitText(3) // 3 is index where text will be split.

Ex:- 

var elem = document.getElementById("add");
var rightSide = elem.firstChild.splitText(3); // spilt text will be in right side node
console.log(rightSide);  
Output :- to list 

substringData Method in javascript

substringData(start, length);

- It returns part of current element's (text or comment node's) content from specifide index with 
specified length. 

Syntax :- 
TextNode.substringData(start, length);
 
TextNode.substringData(2, 5);

Ex :- 

var elem = document.getElementById("add");
var sub = elem.firstChild.substring(0,3);
console.log(sub);
Output :- Add

- It returns a live collection of all attribute of specified element. It is read-only property. 

Syntax  :- 

Element.attributes[index/key]

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById("add");

console.log(elem.attributes[0]); // it returns attribute at 0 index 
console.log(elem.attributes['type']); // it returns value of type key 

setAttribute and getAttribute  Method in javascript

setAttribute() :- 
- It is used to set the value of an attribute on specified element.
- If the attribute already exists, value is updated, otherwise a new attribute is added with name & value.

Syntax :- 

Element.setAttrribute(name,value);
Element.setAttrribute("style","css properties:value");

Ex :- 
p.setAttribute("id", "mydiv");
p.setAttribute("style","font-size:80px");

getAttribute() :- 
- The getAttribute() returns the value of a specified attribute on the element. If the given attibutes 
does not exist, the value returned will either be null or " ". 

Syntax :- 
var attribute = element.getAttribute(attributeName);

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById("add");
elem.setAttribute('class','myclass');
console.log(elem.getAttribute(class));
elem.setAttribute('style', 'font-style: italic');

removeAttribute() and hasAttribute Method  

removeAttribute() :- 
- This method is used to remove an attribute from the specified element. 

Syntax :- 
element.removeAttribute(attrName);

hasAttribute();
- The hasAttribute() method returns a  boolean value indicating whether the specified element has 
the specified attribute or not. 

Syntax :- 
var result = element.hasAttribute(attr_name);

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById("add");
elem.removeAttribute('class');
console.log(elem.attributes);

var attr = elem.hasAttribute('class');
console.log(attr);


HTML DOM mapping in javascript

- Many object properties are simply direct mapping to the attribute of the HTML element.
- There is a mapping directly between HTML and DOM.

Ex :- 
< p id="myid" title="hello"Paragraph>< /p>

Above title can be accessed in DOM by 
document.getElementById("myid").title;

p tag's title attribute is mapped to DOM property title in the above example that is the reason we can 
access title in DOM that way. 

HTML - DOM mapping

The mapping is direct between HTML Attribute and DOM properties with the following considerations. 

- The mapping is direct if the attribute is single non - reserved word. that's why we can access 
title attribute of element via DOM object's property. 
- the mapping will change case if the attribute has two word. 
    - tabindex attribute will be represented as tabIndex in the DOM. 
- If the HTML attribute is reserved under javascript, the value will be modified to work. 
    - Ex :- class attribute will be represented as className in DOM
            for attribute will be represented as htmlFor in DOM 
- There are also some exception
    - char attribute will be represented as ch in DOM
- For others and custom attribute we have to use setAttribute and getAttribute method because they may 
not have direct mapping. 

CSS DOM mapping in javascript

- We can modify the CSS property by applying  a mapping between the CSS property and the DOM object. 
The mapping is direct between CSS property and the DOM properties with following consideration. 

- If CSS property is  of single word their mapping is direct. 
    Ex :- color in CSS will be represented as color in DOM too. 
- Hyphenated CSS properties are represented as a single word with camelCase in the DOM. 
    - Ex:- background-color in CSS is backgroundColor in DOM
- CSS properties value with vendor prefix. 
    - -webkit-box-shadow in CSS is webkitBoxShadow in DOM.  
- There are some reserved words which can be exception in the above cases. 
 - Ex :- float in CSS will be represented  as cssFloat in DOM. 

CSS Style Declaration object style property in javascript

CSS Style Declaration object Inline style manipulation property in javascript

- It(CSSStyleDeclaration) represents a collection of CSS property value pair. 
    - It is used in API :- 
        - HTMLElement.style 
        - window.getComputedStyle()
    
- when we write any element.style(p.style) it returns CSSStyle Declaration object. 

 properties              Methods
 - cssText               - getPropertyValue(property)
 - length                - getPropertyPriority(property)
 - parentRule            - removeProperty(property)
                         - setProperty(property, value, priority)
                         - item(index)

Inline style Manipultion

- to modify CSS value within javascript through style property, we have to access style object of elemenet.

style property 

- the style property is used to get or set the inline style of an element, while getting, it returns a 
CSSStyleDeclaration object that contains a list of all style properties with value assigned for the 
attribute defined in element's inline style attribute. 
- style attribute represents only CSS declaration in the element's inline style element. 
set :-- 
element.style.property = "value";

- Style declaration is reset by setting it to null or an empty string. 
Ex :- element.style.property = null;

var elem = document.getElementById('add');
elem.style.fontSize = "90px";
elem.style.backgroundColor = "yellow"; 

Dynamic style Manipulation className

- we might manipulate style rules using CSS class selector. 
- The element's class atrribute is represented as className property in DOM. 

Properties              Methods 
- length                - item()
- value                 - add()
                        - remove()
                        - replace()
                        - contains()
                        - toggle()
                        - value()
                    
classList Property

The Element.classList is a read-only property which returns a live DOMTokenList collection of the class 
attributes of the element. 

Syntax :-
var elementClasses = elementNodeReference.classList;

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById('add');
var elementClass = elem.classList;
console.log(elementClass); // it returns DOMTokenList which has element's class collection 
Output :- DOMTokenList ["mycl1", value: "mycl1"]

console.log(elementClass[0]);
Output :- mycl1

console.log(elementClass.length);
Output :- 1

console.log(elementClass.value);
Output :- mycl1

console.log(elementClass.item(0));
Output :- mycl1

elementClass.add("myclass");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList(2) ["mycl1", "myclass", value: "mycl1 myclass"]

elementClass.add("myclass2","myclass1");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList(3) ["mycl1", "myclass2", "myclass1", value: "mycl1 myclass2 myclass1"]

elementClass.remove("myclass1");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList(3) ["mycl1", "myclass2", value: "mycl1 myclass2"]

elementClass.remove("myclass2","myclass1");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList ["mycl1", value: "mycl1"]

elementClass.replace("myclass2","myclass1");
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- DOMTokenList(2) ["mycl1", "myclass1", value: "mycl1 myclass1"]

console.log(elementClass.contains("myclass2"));
console.log(elementClass);
Output :- false

elementClass.toggle("myclass2");
console.log(elementClass); // adding myclass2
Output :- DOMTokenList(3) ["mycl1", "myclass1", "myclass2", value: "mycl1 myclass1 myclass2"]

// toggle adds and removes class from element 

elementClass.toggle("myclass2");
console.log(elementClass); // removing myclass2
Output :- DOMTokenList(2) ["mycl1", "myclass1", value: "mycl1 myclass1"]


CSSStyle Declaration object Properties and methods in javascript

CSSStyle Declaration object represents a collection of CSS property-value pairs. 

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById('add');
var cs = elem.style;
console.log(cs.cssText); 
Output :- 

cs.cssText = "font-size: 70px;"; // setting CSS property of element, it will override all old property 

console.log(cs.length);
console.log(cs.item(0));
console.log(cs[0]);
console.log(cs.getPropertyValue('color'));

cs.removeProperty('color');
console.log(elem);

cs.setProperty('font-size', '90px', 'important');
console.log(elem)

var priority = cs.getPropertyPriority('font-size');
console.log(priority)


Computed Style and getComputedStyle method in javascript

- computed style used to display the element after styling from multiple sources have been applied. 
- style sources can be internal style sheets, External stylesheet inherited styles and browser default. 
- To get the values of all CSS properties for an element you should use window.getComputedStyle(). 
- It returns CSSStyleDeclaration object (collection of CSS property-value pair) which updates 
automatically  when element's style is changed. 

Syntax :- 
window.getComputedStyle(element, pseudoElement)
where 
    element = element for which to get the computed style. 
    pseudoElement = a string specifying pseudo element to match. must be ommited or null for regular 
    elements. 

Ex :- 
var elem = document.getElementById('add');
var allCSSProp = window.getComputedStyle(elem);
console.log(allCSSProp);
console.log(allCSSProp.fontStyle);
console.log(allCSSProp.fontSize);
console.log(allCSSProp[0]);


HTMLTableElement

- It provides special properties for manipulatiing the layout and presentation of tables in an HTML 
element. 

Properties          Methods 
- caption           - createCaption()
- tHead             - deleteCaption()
- tFoot             - createTHead()
- rows              - deleteTHead()
- tBodies           - createTFoot()
                    - deleteTFoot()
                    - insertRow()
                    - deleteRow()

Properties :- 

caption :- this property represents the table caption. If no caption in table, it will return null. 

tHead - this property represent table's < thead> element. It's value is null if there is no such element. 

tFoot - this property represents the table's < tFoot> element. If not present it will return null. 

rows :- this property returns live HTML collection of all rows in table.
        though the property is read-only, returned object allows modification of content. 

tBodies :- this property returns HTMLCollection of table bodies. 
            though the property is read-only, returned object allows modification of content. 

< table id="mytab" border="1">
    < caption>My table Caption < /caption>
    < thead>
            < tr>
                < th>Id< /th>
                < th>Name < /th>
                < th>Courses< /th>
            < /tr>
    < /thead>
    < tbody>
            < tr id="mybody">
                < td>11< /td>
                < td>Rahul < /td>
                < td>Javascript < /td>
            < /tr>
            < tr>
                < td>12< /td>
                < td>Rajul < /td>
                < td>PHP < /td>
            < /tr>
    < /tbody>
    < tfoot>
            < tr>
                < td>55< /td>
                < td>Rahan < /td>
                < td>JSP < /td>
            < /tr>
    < /tfoot>

< /table> 

var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");

// caption property 
var tcap = table.caption;
tcap.innerHTML = Student Data;
console.log(tcap.innerHTML);

// thead property 
var thed = table1.tHead;
console.log(thed);
console.log(thed.innerHTML);
thed.innerHTML = "< tr> 
                    < th> NO < /th>  
                    < th> Student < /th>  
                    < th> course < /th> 
                < /tr> "

// tFoot property 
var tfut = table1.tFoot;
console.log(tfut);
console.log(tfut.innerHTML);
tfut.innerHTML =  "< tfoot>
                    < tr>
                        < td>55< /td>
                        < td>Rahan < /td>
                        < td>JSP < /td>
                    < /tr>
                  < /tfoot> " ;

//tBodies Property
var tbody = table1.tBodies;
console.log(tbody);
console.log(tbody[0]);
console.log(tbody.innerHTML);

HTML table element Methods :-  

createCaption() :-

- this method returns the caption for the table. If no caption element exists on table, this method  
creates it, then returns it. 

deleteCaption() :-

- this method removes the caption from the table. If there is no caption, this method does nothing 

Ex :- 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");

var tcap = table1.createCaption();
tcap.innerHTML = "new caption";
console.log(tcap); 
console.log(tcap.innerHTML);

table1.deleteCaption();

createTHead() :-  

- this method returns the < thead> element of table. If there is no such element in table, this method
 creates it then returns it. 

deleteTHead() :-  

- this method removes < thead> from table. 

Ex :- 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
var thed = table1.createTHead();
console.log(thed);  // it returns < thead> of table 

// if < thead> is not present it creates empty < thead>, we can assign it value

thed.innerHTML = "< thead>
                    < tr>
                        < th>Id< /th>
                        < th>Name < /th>
                        < th>Courses< /th>
                    < /tr>
                  < /thead>"
console.log(thed); 

// to delete < thead> from table. 

var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
table1.deleteTHead();

createTFoot() :- 

- this method returns the < tFoot> element of table, If there is no footer for table, this creates it, 
then returns it. 

deleteTFoot() :- 

- this method removes < tFoot> element from the table. 

var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
var tfut = table1.createTFoot();
console.log(tfut); 

tfut.innerHTML = "< tfoot>
                    < tr>
                        < td>55< /td>
                        < td>Rahan < /td>
                        < td>JSP < /td>
                    < /tr>
                  < /tfoot> "; 

// to delete < tfoot> from table. 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
table1.deleteTFoot();

insertRow() :-  

- this method inserts a new row in the table and returns a reference to the new row. 

Syntax :- 
var row = HTMLTableElement.insertRow(index = -1)

    - index is the row index of new row. 
    - If index is -1 or equal to the number of rows, the row is appended as the last row. 
    - If index is greater than number of rows, an IndexSizeError exception will result. 
    - If index is ommited it defaults to -1. 
    - If a table has multiple tbody elements, by default, the new row is inserted into the last tbody. 

deleteRow() :- 

- this method removes a row from the table. 
- If number row to delete is greater or equal to the number of row available row, or if it is negative
    and not equal to special index -1(last row of table), the exception INDEX_SIZE_ERR is thrown. 

Ex :- 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
var row = table1.insertRow(-1); // it inserts row at last position
var row = table1.insertRow(1); // it inserts row at first position
row.insertCell(0).textContent = "New Data";
console.log(row);

// To delete row 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
table1.deleteRow(0);
console.log(table1);

HTML Table Section Element in javascript

var tbody = document.getElementById("mybody");
var ro = tbody.rows;
console.log(ro);
console.log(ro[0].innerHTML);
ro[1].innerHTML = " < td>55< /td> < td>Rahan < /td> < td>JSP < /td>"

var row = tbody.insertRow(-1);
row.insertCell().textContent = "New";

tbody.deleteRow(1);

 HTML Table Row Element in javascript

- It provides special properties and methods for manipulating the layout of rows in HTML Table. 

Properties :- 
- cells
- rowIndex
- sectionRowIndex

Methods :- 
- insertCell()
- deleteCell()

cells :- 

- It returns HTMLCollection containing the cells in the row. 
- HTMLCollection is automatically updated when cells are added or removed. 

rowIndex :- 

- It returns a long value whichgives the logical position of the row within entire table. 
- If the row is not part of table, returns -1. 

sectionRowIndex :- 

- It returns the long value which gives the logical position of the row within table section it belongs to.
- If the row is not part of section, returns -1. 

Methods :- 

insertCell() :-  

- this method inserts a new cell into a table row and returns a reference to the cell. 

Syntax :- 
var cell = HTMLTableRowElement.insertCell(index = -);

- index is the cell index of new cell. 
- If index is -1 equal to number of cells, the cell is appended as the last cell in row. 
- If index is greater than number of cells, an IndexSizeError exception will result. 

deleteCell() :- 

- It removes the cell at the given position in the row. 
- If given position is greater than amount of cells in row, or smaller than 0, it raises DOMException 
with IndexSizeError.

Ex :- 
var table1 = document.getElementById("mytab");
var myrow = table1.rows;
console.log(myrow[0].cells.length); // returns number of cells present in 0th row
console.log(myrow[0].cells[0]);
console.log(myrow[2].cells[0]);
console.log(myrow[2].cells.item(0));
console.log(myrow[1].cells.namedItem("mycell")); // It returns cell of 1st row given Id="mycell"
console.log(myrow[2].cells[1].innerHTML);
myrow[2].cells[1].innerHTML = "Rehan";

var mycell = myrow[2].insertCell(2); // it will insert an empty cell in 2nd row at 2nd position
mycell.innerHTML = "new cell";

// to delete cell from row 
myrow[1].deleteCell(2); // it will delete 2nd cell of first row

textContent :- 
- This property sets or returns the text content of specified node. 
- setting this property on node removes all children and replaces them with single text node with the 
given value. 
- to grab all text we can use document.element.textContent. 
- textContent returns null if the node is document, DOCTYPE or notation. 

Syntax :- 
node.textContent
node.textContent = text 

var p = document.getElementById("h11");
console.log(p.textContent);
p.textContent = "Hello world";

Difference between textContent and innerHTML

when we want to use only text, we can use textContent but when we want to use HTML also at that time 
we should use innerHTML.

Ex :- 

var p = document.getElementById("h11");
p.textContent = "< em>here we are< /em>"; // em will be same and not applied to text 
p.innerHTML = "< em>here we are< /em>"; // the content will be changed to em

// CSS Selector DOM

// Element Selector 
var list = document.querySelectorAll("p");
console.log(list);

// Group selector 
var list = document.querySelectorAll('div, p');
console.log(list);

//Universal Selector 
var listbook= document.querySelectorAll('*');
console.log(list); 

// Class Selector 
    // Universal style class
    var list = document.querySelectorAll('.game'); // element which has class name 'game' is returned 
    console.log(list); 

    // Element specific style class 
    var list = document.querySelectorAll('p.red');
    console.log(list);
    Output :- it will return collection of all p element which has class = 'red'  

    var list = document.querySelectorAll('p.red.black');
    console.log(list);
    Output :- it will return collection of all p element which has both class = 'red black' 

// ID Selector 
var list = document.querySelectorAll('#book');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return collection of element which has id='book'

var list = document.querySelectorAll('p#book');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return p element which has id='book'

// Attribute Selector 
var list = document.querySelectorAll('p[title]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return all p element which has title attribute 

var list = document.querySelectorAll('p[title = "mypara1"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return all p element which has title = "mypara1" 

var list = document.querySelectorAll('img[width = "30%"][height = "20%"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return img element which has width = 30% and height = 20%

var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class ~= "game"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and value of class attribute is "game"

var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class |= "game"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and it's value should start with word "game"
         the word should either "game" or seperated by hyphen "game-super" but not like "gamesuper" or
         "game super"

var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class ^= "game"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and it's value start with "game"
            it will return any element start with game .... "gamesuper", "game super", "game-super" etc..
         
var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class $= "game"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and it's value ends with "game"
            ex. "game","supergame","super-game" etc. 

var list = document.querySelectorAll('[class *= "ga"]');
console.log(list);
Output :- it will return element which has class attribute and it's value has "ga" word anywhere 

// pseudo Class
    //first-child
    var list = document.querySelectorAll('li:first-child');
    console.log(list);
    Output :- it will return first child of li element 
                         
// In this case second function (disp2) will be executed, it will override disp1 
// when two events are called on same element the newest will override the oldest one. 


addEventListener in javascript

- This method is used to engage an event handler in a page. 

Syntax :-  
Object.addEventListener(event, handler, capturePhase); 
 
where, 
- object is the node to which the listener is to bound. 
- Event is a string indicating the type of event. 
- Handler is the function that should be called when the event occurs. 
- capturePhase is a boolean indicating wheather to use bubbling(false) or capture(true). this is optional.
If you omit there is false bydefault. 

Ex :- 
btn.addEventListener("click", show, false);

Why should we use addEventListener ?
- It allows you to bind multiple handler to an object for same event. 
- It enables you finer-grained control of the phase when the listener is activated( Capture or Bubbling) 
- It works on any DOM element, not just HTML. 

Ex :- 

function show(){
    alert('Button clicked');
}
var btn = document.getElementById('add');
btn.addEventListener('click', show);
btn.addEventListener('mouseover', show);

// It allows you to bind multiple handler to an object for same event. 

function disp1(){
    alert('Button clicked 1');
}
function disp2(){
    alert('Button clicked 2');
}

var btn = document.getElementById('add');
btn.addEventListener('click', disp1);
btn.addEventListener('click', disp2);


removeEventListener()


- This method is used to remove handlers, with the same arguments give when event was added. 
Ex :- 

function show(){
    alert('Button clicked');
}
var btn = document.getElementById('add');
btn.addEventListener('click', show, false);
btn.addEventListener('click', show, true);

btn.removeEventListener('click', show, true);


DOM event flow or event propagation in javascript

- The DOM 2 Event Model specification describes a standard way to create, capture, handle and cancel event 
in a tree like structure such as an XHTML document's object hierarchy. 

Phases :- 
- Capture phase 
- Target phase 
- Bubbling Phase 

Ex :- 
< div id="one">1
    < div id="two">2
        < div id="three">3
            < div id="four">4
        
    


// parent of 4 is 3, parent of 3 is 2, parent of 2 is 1, parent of 1 can be anything like body, etc... 

- Bubbling Phase :- It propagtes from bottom to top. for example, if click event is given to all above 
< div> element and we click 4 then it will triger from 4 then if its parent has click event then it triger 
its parent 3, same way it will triger its parent 2 and then 1 and so on.. 

- Capture Phase :- It is opposite to bubbling phase, it propagates from top to bottom. 
- If we click on 4 then it will move to the top parent element which has click event, here 1 is parent 
with click event so it will triger 1 then it's child which has click event(here 2) then child of 2 is 3, then
child of 3 is 4.

- Target Phase :- 
- It will triger the targetted element not parent and not child. not from top to bottom And not from bottom
to top. 
If we click element 4 then it will triger element 4. 

Ex :- 

//Bubbling Phase 
document.getElementById('one').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('1');},false);
document.getElementById('two').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('2');},false);
document.getElementById('three').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('3');},false);
document.getElementById('four').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('4');},false);

// Capture Phase 
document.getElementById('one').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('1');},true);
document.getElementById('two').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('2');},true);
document.getElementById('three').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('3');},true);
document.getElementById('four').addEventListener('click', function(){console.log('4');},true);


Event Object in javascript

- DOM events pass an event object as an argument to the event handlers. 
- This object contains extra information about the event that occured. 

Ex :- addEventListener('click', function(e){console.log(e)});

where, e is object passed by DOM events as argument which has information about the event that occured. 

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log(e);
    console.log(e.clientX); 
    console.log(e.clientY);
    console.log(e.type);
    console.log(e.target);
    console.log(e.currentTarget);
}); 

we can access many properties through e. 


What is difference between target and currentTarget ?

- Target is pn which we click while current target is according to propagation execution. 

Ex :- 
< div id="one" data-name="1">1
    < div id="two" data-name="2">2
        < div id="three" data-name="3">3
            < div id="four" data-name="4">4
        
    


// Bubbling Phase 
- when we click on 4 the target will remain same 4 but current target will propagate from bottom to top. 

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log('1'); // 1
    console.log('Target = ' + e.target.dataset.name); // Target :- 4
    console.log('current Target = ' + e.currentTarget.dataset.name); // current Target :- 1
}, false);

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log('2'); // 2
    console.log('Target = ' + e.target.dataset.name); // Target :- 4
    console.log('current Target = ' + e.currentTarget.dataset.name); // current Target :- 2
}, false);

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log('3'); // 3 
    console.log('Target = ' + e.target.dataset.name); // Target :- 4
    console.log('current Target = ' + e.currentTarget.dataset.name);  // current Target :- 3
}, false);

document.getElementById('add').addEventListener('click', function(e){
    console.log('4'); // 4
    console.log('Target = ' + e.target.dataset.name); // Target :- 4
    console.log('current Target = ' + e.currentTarget.dataset.name); // current Target :- 4
}, false);

Output :- when we click 4

4
target :- 4
current Target :- 4
3
target :- 4
current Target :- 3
2
target :- 4
current Target :- 2
1
target :- 4
current Target :- 1


Event Methods stopPropagation and stopImmediatePropagation in javascript

stopPropagation() :- Prevents further propagation of the current event in the capturing and bubbling phases. 
Syntax :- e.stopPropagation();

stopImmediatePropagation() :- Prevents other listener of the same event from being called.
Syntax :- e.stopImmediatePropagation();


1
    
2
        
3
        

    




Ex :- 
< div id="one" >1
    < div id="two" >2
        < div id="three" >3
        
    


function div1(e){
    this.style.backgroundColor = 'red';
};

function div2(e){
    this.style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
    e.stopPropagation(); // It will stop propagation and stop div1 from triggering
    e.stopImmediatePropagation(); // this method will stop all event handler even of same event
};

function div2_2(e){
    this.style.width = '250px'; // it should be stopped, but it is trigged because it is stopPropagation()
    // when stopImmediatePropagation() method is called this event will also be stopped. 
};

function div3(e){
    this.style.backgroundColor = 'green';
};

var div_1 = document.getElementById('one');
var div_2 = document.getElementById('two');
var div_3 = document.getElementById('three');

div_1.addEventListener('click', div1, false);
div_2.addEventListener('click', div2, false);
div_2.addEventListener('click', div2_2, false);
div_3.addEventListener('click', div3, false);

// div2 has two event listener 
// bubble up phase will triger event from bottom to top 

- when I click on 3rd element (div), firstly 3 then 2 and then 1 will change its color as per bubble phase. 
- but if we don't want to triger all element, instead only clicked element should be trigered. 
in such case we can add stopPropagation in 3rd element, it will stop propagate so only 3 element will be 
trigered. 
- Now we want 3rd and 2nd element to triger but the 2nd element has two event handlers but we want only One
to be trigged. now if we add stopPropagation() in 2nd element's one handler, even then it will triger both
handlers will not stop another handler because all listener of same event will be triggered and 
stopPropagation() method will not stop it.

- For stoping any event handler of same event we will use stopImmediatePropagation() method it will stop 
all other handlers of same event.  


How to prevent Element default behavior in javascript

preventDefault() :- The event interface's preventDefault() method tells user agent that if the event is not
explicitly handled, its default action should not be taken as it normally would be. 

Syntax :- e.preventDefault();

Ex :- 
< a href="http://www.google.com" id="mylink">Google site< /a>

// default behavior of anchor tag is, when we click link inside it, we will be redirected to that link. 
but if we want something else, we have to first stop default behavior using preventDefault

Ex :- 
< a href="http://www.google.com" id="mylink">Google site< /a>

function stopLink(e) {
    e.preventDefault();
}
var ln = document.getElementById('mylink');
ln.addEventListener('click', stopLink, false);

// It will stop default behavior of link, when we will click on link it will not be redirected and no 
action will be taken. 


Mouse Event in javascript

mousedown :- It fires when mouse button is pressed down. 

mouseup :- It fires when the mouse button is released.

click :- It fires when something is clicked.mousedown, mouseup and click events fires in sequence. 

dblclick :- It fires when something is clicked twice in repid succession. mousedown, mouseup, click, 
mousedown, mouseup, click, and dblclick events fires in sequence. 

mouseenter :- It fires when mouse starts to hover over some element. No bubble. 

mouseleave :- It fires when a mouse exits while while hovering over some element. No bubble. 

mouseover :- It fires when mouse is hovering over some element. 

mouseout :- It fires when mouse leaves from hovering over some element. 

mousemove :- It fires when the mouse moves. 

contextmenu :- It fires when mouse right button is clicked.     

Ex :- 

function div1(e){
    console.log(e.type);
}
function div2(e){
    console.log(e.type);
}
var div_1 = document.getElementById('one');
var div_2 = document.getElementById('two');

div_1.addEventListener('mousedown', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mouseup', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('click', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('dblclick', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mouseenter', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mouseleave', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mousemove', div1, false);
div_1.addEventListener('contextmenu', div1, false);

// bubble up // when we will click on one element there will be 2 click, mousedown and mouseup event 
beccause of bubble phase propagation 

div_2.addEventListener('click', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('click', div1, false);

div_2.addEventListener('mousedown', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mousedown', div1, false);

div_2.addEventListener('mouseup', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mouseup', div1, false);

div_2.addEventListener('contextmenu', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('contextmenu', div1, false);

div_2.addEventListener('mousemove', div2, false);
div_1.addEventListener('mousemove', div1, false);

Ex :- 

Name 

var txt = document.getElementById('mytext');

function changeColorOrange(){
    txt.style.backgroundColor = 'orange';
}
function changeColorWhite(){
    txt.style.backgroundColor = 'white';
}

txt.addEventListener('mouseover', changeColorOrange, false);
txt.addEventListener('mouseout', changeColorWhite, false);


Focus Event in javascript

focus :- It fires when an element gains focus such as selecting form field. No bubble. 

blur :- It fires when an element loses focus, such as moving away from a form field. No bubble. 

focusin :- It fires just as an element is about to gain focus.

focusout :- It fires just as an element loses focus and just before the blur event. 

Name 

var txt = document.getElementById('mytxt1'); 

function focusEvent(e){
    txt.style.backgroundColor = 'orange';
}

function blurEvent(e){
    txt.style.backgroundColor = 'white';
}
txt.addEventListener('focus', focusEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('blur', blurEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('focusin', focusEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('focusout', blurEvent, false);


Key Events in javascript

keydown :- It fires as a key is pressed down. 

keypress :- It fires after a key is pressed down (after keydown). It only works with printable characters. 

keyup :- It fires as the key is released.

Name 

var txt = document.getElementById('mytxt2'); 

function keyEvent(e){
    console.log(e.type + ' ' + e.keyCode + ' ' + String.fromCharCode(e.keyCode));
}

txt.addEventListener('keydown', keyEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('keypress', keyEvent, false);
txt.addEventListener('keyup', keyEvent, false);


Text Events in javascript

- It will whatever character is pressed. 

Name 

var txt = document.getElementById('mytxt'); 

function show(e){
    console.log(e.type + ' ' + e.data);
}

txt.addEventListener('textInput', show, false);


window object in javascript

- window object represents the browser's window or potentially frame, that a document is displayed in. 
- As long as a browser window is open, even if no document is loaded in window, the window object is 
defined in the current model in memory. 
- All global javascript variables, functions and objects automatically becomes member of the window object. 

console.dir(window);

var oh = window.outerHeight;
console.log(oh);

var ow = window.outerWidth;
console.log(ow);

var ih = window.innerHeight;
console.log(ih);

var iw = window.innerWidth;
console.log(iw);


Dialog boxes

- It is used to provide some information to user.
- Types of dialog boxes :- 
    - alert 
    - Confirm 
    - Prompt 

alert() Method

- This window object's method is used to display data in alert dialog box. 
- alert should be used only when you truly want to stop everything and let the user know something. 

syntax :- window.alert() or alert()
          
Ex :- window.alert('hello world');
      window.alert(variable);
      window.alert(4+2);
      window.alert('hello world'+ variable);

confirm() Method

- This method of window object is used to display a message for a user to respond by pressing ok button to
agree with the message or cancel button to disagree with the message. 
- It returns True on Ok and false on Cancel. 

Syntax :-  window.confirm() or confirm()

Ex :- window.confirm('are you sure ?');

if(confirm('Do you want to delete ?')){
    document.write('Data deleted');
}else {
    document.write('Action canceled');
}

var crm = confirm('are you sure?');
if (crm){
    console.log('data deleted');
}else{
    console.log('Action canceled');
}

prompt() Method

- window object's prompt() method can be used to get input from user. 
- It displays a dialog box that prompts the visitor for input.  
- Once the prompt function obtains input from user, it returns that input. 
- If the user press the cancel button or close the dialog, null will be returned. 

Syntax :- prompt(text, defaultText)
Ex :- prompt('Enter your name :- ', 'name');

var name = prompt('enter your name:- ')


open() and close() method in javascript

- The open() method creates a new secondary browser window. 
- It returns a window object representing newly created window.
- If the window couldn't be opened, it returns null. 

Syntax :- window.open(URL, name, features, replace)
URL :- URL indicates the document to load into the window. If no URL is specified, a new window with 
        about:blank is opened. 

Name :- specifies the target atrribute or the name of window. The following values are supported: 
_blank - URL is loaded into a new window. This is default. 
_parent - URL is loaded into the parent frame. 
_self - URL replaces the current page. 
_top - URL replaces any frameset that may be loaded.    

Features :- It is comma separated string that lists the features of the window. 

Replace - It indicates wheather or not the URL specified should replace the window's contents. 
this would apply to the window that was already created. Value can be true / false. 

Ex :- 
var newWindow = window.open('www.goole.com','_self','height=100, width=100')

var new = window.open();
console.log(new);



function createWindow(){
    window.open();
    window.open('https://www.google.com');
    window.open('https://www.google.com','_self');
    window.open('https://www.google.com','_blank');
    window.open('https://www.google.com','_blank','height=400,width=800');
    window.open('https://www.google.com','_blank','height=400,width=800,scrollbars=no');
    var newW = window.open('','_blank','height=400,width=800');
    newW.document.Write('Our new window');
}

b1 = document.getElementById('btn');
b1.addEventListener('click',createWindow, false);


close() Method

- Once the window is open, the close() method is used to close it.
- It closes the current window or the window on which it is called.
- This method is only allowed to called for windows opened by script using window.open() method. 
- It is often used together with open() method.

Syntax :- window.close()

Ex :- 


var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('https;//www.google.com','','height=400,width=600');
}
function clWindow(){
    newWindow.close();
}

bn1 = document.getElementById('mybn1');
bn2 = document.getElementById('mybn2');

bn1.addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
bn2.addEventListener('click', clWindow, false);


print() Method in javascript



function printDoc(){
    window.print();
}

var bn3 = document.getElementById('mybn3');
bn3.addEventListener('click', printDoc, false);


focus() and blur() Method

focus() :- when we work in current window, we are focusing on it.
blur() :- when we leave current window, it is blur. 





var newWindow;
function openWin(){
    newWindow = window.open('','_blank','width=600,height=400');
}
function focusWin(){
    newWindow.focus();
}
function blurWin(){
    newWindow.blur();
}
document.getElementById('openbtn').addEventListener('click', openWin, false);
document.getElementById('focusbtn').addEventListener('click', focusWin, false);
document.getElementById('blurbtn').addEventListener('click', blurWin, false);


Moving Window in javascript

moveBy() 

moveBy() - This method moves the current window by specified amount of pixels. 
Syntax :- window.moveBy(horizontalPixels, verticalPixels);
where, 
window :- It is name of the window to move or it is just window if it is main window. 
horizontalPixels :- It is the number of horizontalPixels to move the window where positive number move the 
window to right and negative number move the window to left. 
verticalPixels :- It is the number pixel to move the window where positive number move the window to bottom 
and negative number move the window to up. 

Ex :- newWindow.moveBy(200,200);





var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('','newWindow','height=3 00,width=400');
}

function mvWin(){
    newWindow.moveBy(200,200);
    newWindow.focus();
}

function mvlWin(){
    newWindow.moveBy(-200,-200);
    newWindow.focus();
}
document.getElementById('opn').addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
document.getElementById('mwr').addEventListener('click', mvWin, false);
document.getElementById('mwl').addEventListener('click', mvlWin, false);

moveTo() Method

moveTo() :- This method moves the window to specified coordinates. 
Syntax :- window.moveTo(x, y);
where,
window - It is the name of window to move or it is called just window. 
x - It is the screen co-ordinate on x - axis to move the window to. 
y - It is the screen co-ordinate on y - axis to move the window to. 
Ex :- newWindow.moveTo(200,200); 




var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('','newWindow','height=300,width=400');
}

function mvWin(){
    newWindow.moveBy(200,200);
    newWindow.focus();
}

document.getElementById('opbtn').addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
document.getElementById('mw').addEventListener('click', mvWin, false);


Resizing Window in javascript

resizeBy()
resizeBy() :- This method is used to resize the current window by a certain amount, relative to its 
current size. 

Syntax :- window.resizeBy(width, height);
where, 
window :- It is the name of window to move or is called window if it is main window.
width :- It is the number of width pixel, where positive number increase the windth and negative number 
decrease the width. 
height :- It is the number of height pixel, where positive number increase the windth and negative number 
decrease the width. 

Ex :- window.resizeBy(200, 200); 




var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('','_blank','height=300,width=400');
}

function rsizeWin(){
    newWindow.resizeBy(200,200);
    newWindow.focus();
}

document.getElementById('obtn').addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
document.getElementById('rsize').addEventListener('click', rsizeWin, false);

resizeTo()

resizeTo() :- this method is used to resize the window to specified width and height. 
syntax:- window.resizeTo(width, height);
window :- It is the name of window to move or is called window if it is main window.
width :- It is an integer representing the new outerWidth in pixels(including scroll bars, title bars). 
height :- It is an integer value representing the new outerHeight in pixel(including scroll bars, etc.) 

Ex :- newWindow.resizeTo(200, 200); 




var newWindow;
function opnWindow(){
    newWindow = window.open('','_blank','height=300,width=400');
}

function rsizeWin(){
    newWindow.resizeTo(200,200);
    newWindow.focus();
}

document.getElementById('opwbtn').addEventListener('click', opnWindow, false);
document.getElementById('r1size').addEventListener('click', rsizeWin, false);


Scrolling window in javascript

scrollBy() Method
scrollBy() - This method scrolls the document in the window by the given amount. 
Syntax :- window.scrollBy(x, y); or window.scrollBy(options);
where,
window :- It is the name of the window to scroll or is called just window if it is main window.
x - How many pixels to scroll by, along the x-axis(horizontal), positive values will scroll to the right,
while negative values will be scroll to the left.
y - How many pixels to scroll by, along the y-axis (vertical). Positive values will be scroll down, while 
negative value will be scroll up. 
options :- It is an object with three properties:
            top, which is the same as the y-coord 
            left, which is the same as the x-coord 
            behavior, which is a string containing one of smooth, instant, or auto; default is auto. 
Ex :- window.scrollBy(0, -20);
      window.scrollBy({top:-20, behavior:'smooth'});
      Note :- for this method to work, the visible property of window's scroll bar must be set true. 






function scrollTWin(){
    // window.scrollBy(0, -20);
    // window.scrollBy({top: -20, behavior: 'smooth'});
    window.scrollBy({top: -20, behavior: 'instant'});
}

function scrollDWin(){
    window.scrollBy(0, 20);
}

function scrollLWin(){
    window.scrollBy(-20, 0);
}

function scrollRWin(){
    window.scrollBy(20, 0);
}

document.getElementById('myb1').addEventListener('click', scrollTWin);
document.getElementById('myb2').addEventListener('click', scrollDWin);
document.getElementById('myb3').addEventListener('click', scrollLWin);
document.getElementById('myb4').addEventListener('click', scrollRWin);

scrollTo() Method
scrollTo() :- This method scrolls to a paricular set of coordinates in the document. 
syntax :- window.scrollTo(x, y); or window.scrollTo(options);
where,
window - It is the name of window to scroll or is called just window if it is main window. 
x - It is the pixel along the horizontal axis of the document.
y - It is the pixel along the vertical axis of the document.

options :- It is an object with three properties:
            top, which is the same as the y-coord 
            left, which is the same as the x-coord 
            behavior, which is a string containing one of smooth, instant, or auto; default is auto. 

Ex :- window.scrollTo(0, 400);
window.scrollTo({top:400, behavior:'smooth'});






function scrollTWin(){
    window.scrollTo(0, 0);
    // window.scrollBy({top: 0, behavior: 'smooth'});
    // window.scrollBy({top: 0, behavior: 'instant'});
}

function scrollDWin(){
    window.scrollTo(0, 20);
}

function scrollLWin(){
    window.scrollTo(-20, 0);
}

function scrollRWin(){
    window.scrollTo(20, 0);
}

document.getElementById('mybtn1').addEventListener('click', scrollTWin);
document.getElementById('mybtn2').addEventListener('click', scrollDWin);
document.getElementById('mybtn3').addEventListener('click', scrollLWin);
document.getElementById('mybtn4').addEventListener('click', scrollRWin);


Location object in javascript

- This is used to access the location(URL) of window.
- The location object can be both read and replaced, so it is possible to update the location of a page
through scripting. 
- Location object is property of window. 
syntax :- 
window.location.property 
window.location.method

Properties

hash - The part of the URL including and following the # symbol.
host - The hostname and port number.
hostname - hostname 
href - entire URL 
pathname - Path relative to the host. 
port - Port number 
protocol - protocol of URL. 
search - The part of URL including and after the ?

console.dir(location);
console.log(window.location.hash);
console.log(window.location.hash);
console.log(window.location.port);
console.log(window.location.href);
console.log(window.location.search);
console.log(window.location.protocol);
console.log(window.location.pathname);
console.log(window.location.hostname);

window.location.hash = '#team';
window.location.href = 'www.google.com';

Methods 

- assign(URL) - It changes the location of current page with passed URL. 
- reload() - Reload the current page. 
- replace(URL) - Replace the current page with the given URL in history. 
  as it is replaced in history it won't be possible to access the current page with back/forward.   

  reload method :- 
  Ex :- 
window.location.reload() 

assign method 
Ex :- 
window.location.assign('https://www.google.com');

replace method 
Ex:- 
window.location.replace('https://www.google.com');


History object in javascript

- The history object is read-only property of URL string that show where the user has been recently. 
Syntax :- 
window.history.property
window.history.method

properties:- 
length - It returns the number of URLs in the history list. 

Methods :- 
back() - It loads the previous URL in the history list. 

forward() :- It loads the next URL in history list. 

go() :- It access a particular item in history list relative to current position.
Using a negative value moves to history item previous to the current location, while a positive number 
moves forward in the history list. 

console.log(window.history.length);

console.log(window.history.back());
console.log(window.history.forward());

console.log(window.history.go(-1)); // it will go 1 site back 
console.log(window.history.go(1)); // It will go 1 site forward 
console.log(window.history.go(2)); // it will go 2 site forward


setTimeout() and clearTimeout() method in javascript

- The setTimeout() sets the timer which executes function or piece of code once after the timer expires. 
- The function is only executed once. 
- It returns a positive integer value, this value can be passed to clearTimeout() to cancel timeout.

syntax:- setTimeout(function, millisecond, para1, para2);
Ex :- 
var timeoutId = setTimeout(show, 2000);


color will be changed after completion of set time duration


function changeColor(){
    document.getElementById('setT').style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
}

setTimeout(changeColor, 5000);

or 

setTimeout(() => {
    document.getElementById('setT').style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
    }, 5000);

or


setTimeout(function() {
    document.getElementById('setT').style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
    }, 5000);

clearTimeout() Method

- The clearTimeout() method cancels a timeout previously established by calling setTimeout() method. 
- The ID returned by setTimeout() method is used to pass as parameter for the clearTimeout() method. 
syntax :- 
clearTimeout(timeoutId);


Ex :- 

var timeoutID = setTimeout(() => {
    document.getElementById('setT').style.backgroundColor = 'blue';
    }, 5000);

function clrTime(){
    clearTimeout(timeoutID);
}

document.getElementById('bt1').addEventListener('click', clrTime);


setInterval() and clearInterval() Method

setInterval() :- 
- It repetedly calls a function or execute a code with a fixed time delay between each call. 
- It returns an intervalId which uniquely identifies interval so we can remove it by calling clearInterval(). 

Syntax :- setInterval(function, millisecond, para1, para2);

clearInterval() :- 
- This method cancels a timed, repeating action which was set by setInterval()
Syntax :- clearInterval(intervalID);


use of setInterval :- 



Ex :- 

intervalID = setInterval(function(){
    document.getElementById('setI').textContent += ' hello';
 }, 2000);

 function clrInt(){
     clearInterval(intervalID);
 }

document.getElementById('clI').addEventListener('click', clrInt);

Form handling in javascript

- javascript provide access to forms within an HTML document through the form object known as 
HTMLFormElement in the DOM. which is a child of the document object. 

Accessing Forms :- 
- javascript provides various way of accessing form:-
    - document.forms[index_number] -  It returns collection of form in the document. 
    - document.forms["name_attribute_value"] - we can use name attribute of the form.
    - document.name_attribute_value - we can use name attribute of form with dot as well. 
    - getElementById('ID') - If form has an unique id we can use it. 



    User Name: 
    Password : 
    






    User Name: 
    Password : 
    



Ex :- 
Accessing Form :- 
// with Index number

var form1 = document.forms[0];
var form2 = document.form[1];
console.log(form1); // It will returns form1
console.log(form2); // It will returns form2

// with name attribute using square bracket

var form1 = document.forms['form1'];
var form2 = document.forms['form2'];
console.log(form1); // It will returns form1
console.log(form2); // It will returns form2

// with name attribute using dot 

var form1 = document.form1;
var form2 = document.form2;
console.log(form1); // It will returns form1
console.log(form2); // It will returns form2

// getElementById method

var form1  = document.getElementById('fm1');
var form2  = document.getElementById('fm2');
console.log(form1);
console.log(form2);

- If form field has unique Id then we can access it using getElementById method. 
- elements[] - It contains collection of elements. 

Syntax :- document.form_name.elements[index_number];
document.form_name.elements['name_attribute_value'];
document.form_name.name_attribute_value;
document.form_name.ID_attribute_value;

- getElementsByName('field_name') - this method is also used to access form field.

var username = document.form1.elements['username1'];

// with id attribute
